1. Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Edition

James Larminie & John Lowry · Wiley · 500 Q&As

Basic w-hist-001
What is an electric vehicle?
An electric vehicle is a vehicle powered fully or partly by electricity instead of burning fuel. It uses an electric motor driven from a battery or supply line. EVs help reduce noise, local pollution, and dependence of transport on oil.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1. Introduction (chapter intro) · Page: 22
"Electric vehicles are becoming increasingly important as not only do they reduce noise and pollution, but also they can be used to reduce the dependence of transport on oil"
Basic w-hist-002
Why are electric vehicles considered important today?
Electric vehicles matter because they reduce noise and local pollution, cut transport's dependence on oil, and can lower overall carbon-dioxide emissions when their electricity comes from non-fossil sources such as nuclear, wind or hydro power, helping the world fight climate change.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1. Introduction (chapter intro) · Page: 22
"Production of zero release of carbon dioxide requires that the energy for electric vehicles is produced from non-fossil-fuel sources such as nuclear and alternative energy."
Basic w-hist-003
Roughly how many years of oil supply are left at current usage rates?
The textbook gives a worst-case estimate of only about 40 years of oil supply at current usage rates. In practice, scarcity will raise prices, slowly cutting demand. Coal can also be turned into oil, with over 100 years of coal still available.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1. Introduction (chapter intro) · Page: 22
"The worst scenario is that we have only 40 years supply of oil left at current usage rates."
Basic w-hist-004
Why is global warming linked to fossil-fuel vehicles?
Burning fossil fuels in vehicles releases carbon dioxide into the atmosphere. This carbon dioxide is widely blamed for global warming, which can cause climate change and rising sea levels that could damage or destroy many of the world's coastal cities.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1. Introduction (chapter intro) · Page: 22
"Global warming is blamed on the release of carbon dioxide when fossil fuels are burnt and it is believed to give rise to a myriad of problems including climate change and rising sea levels"
Basic w-hist-005
Who invented the first practical DC electric motor?
The British scientist William Sturgeon invented the first commutator-type direct-current electric motor capable of turning machinery, in 1832. His work built on Michael Faraday's earlier discoveries in 1821, which laid the foundation for modern electric motors and generators.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 23
"The first commutator-type direct current electric motor capable of turning machinery was invented by the British scientist William Sturgeon in 1832."
Basic w-hist-006
Who built the first known electric locomotive, and when?
The first known electric locomotive was built in 1837 by the Scottish chemist Robert Davidson. It was powered by non-rechargeable batteries. He later built a larger locomotive that was shown at the Royal Scottish Society of Arts Exhibition in 1841.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 23
"The first known electric locomotive was built in 1837 by the chemist Robert Davidson, and was by powered by non-rechargeable batteries."
Basic w-hist-007
When and where did the first regular electric tram service begin?
The first regular electric tram service was the Gross-Lichterfelde Tramway, which began running in May 1881 in Lichterfelde, a suburb of Berlin, Germany. The tramway was produced by the German engineering company Siemens & Halske AG, an early pioneer in electric transport.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 23
"The first regular electric tram service, the Gross-Lichterfelde Tramway, went into service in Lichterfelde, a suburb of Berlin, Germany, and was produced by Siemens & Halske AG, in May 1881."
Basic w-hist-008
When did the first electric street tramway open in Britain?
The first electric street tramway in Britain was the Blackpool Tramway, which opened on 29 September 1885. By the outbreak of the First World War, electric trams had become a common form of city transport in many countries around the world.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 23
"The first electric street tramway in Britain, the Blackpool Tramway, was opened on 29 September 1885."
Basic w-hist-009
When did trolleybuses first appear?
The trolleybus dates back to 29 April 1882, when Dr Ernst Werner ran his bus in a Berlin suburb. The world's first passenger-carrying trolleybus then started service in 1901 at Bielathal, near Dresden, Germany. Britain got trolleybuses in 1911.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 23
"The trolleybus dates back to 29 April 1882, when Dr Ernst Werner ran his bus in a Berlin suburb."
Basic w-hist-010
Who was Camille Jenatzy and what record did he set?
Camille Jenatzy was a Belgian racing driver. Driving an electric car called 'La Jamais Contente', he set a new land-speed record of 106 kph (about 65.9 mph). This made it the first car ever to exceed 100 kph.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 23
"the Belgian racing diver Camille Jenatzy, driving the electric vehicle known as 'La Jamais Contente', 1 set a new land speed record of 106 kph (65.9 mph) making this the first car to exceed 100 kph."
Basic w-hist-011
Why were early electric cars preferred to petrol cars around 1900?
Around 1900, electric cars were reliable and started instantly. Internal combustion (IC) cars were unreliable, smelly and had to be hand-cranked to start. Steam-engine cars also needed time to light their burners and had relatively low thermal efficiency, making EVs the better choice.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"The electric vehicle was relatively reliable and started instantly, whereas IC engine vehicles were at the time unreliable, smelly and needed to be manually cranked to start."
Basic w-hist-012
How many electric vehicles were produced by the 1920s?
By the 1920s, several hundred thousand electric vehicles had already been built. They served as cars, vans, taxis, delivery vehicles and buses. After cheap oil and the IC self-starter (invented in 1911) arrived, however, petrol cars rapidly overtook them.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"By the 1920s several hundred thousand electric vehicles had been produced for use as cars, vans, taxis, delivery vehicles and buses."
Basic w-hist-013
What is regenerative braking?
Regenerative braking is a system where the electric motor acts as a generator while the car is slowing down. It converts the vehicle's kinetic energy back into electricity, which is returned to the battery for reuse instead of being lost as heat.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"regenerative braking, a system where the motor acts as a generator, braking the vehicle and converting the kinetic energy of the vehicle to electrical energy, which is returned to battery storage"
Basic w-hist-014
How much energy per kilogram does petrol store compared with lead-acid battery?
Petrol stores roughly 9000 Wh per kilogram of fuel, while a lead-acid battery stores only about 30 Wh per kilogram. That is around 300 times less energy per kilogram, which is a major reason combustion engines historically beat batteries on range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"The specific energy of fuels for IC engines varies, but is around 9000 Wh kg-1 whereas the specific energy of a lead acid battery is around 30 Wh kg-1."
Basic w-hist-015
What is the typical efficiency of a petrol engine and gearbox?
A typical petrol engine plus gearbox and transmission has an overall efficiency of about 20%. That means only one-fifth of the fuel's chemical energy becomes useful motion at the shaft, while most of the rest is lost as heat through exhaust and cooling.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"Once the efficiency of the IC engine, gearbox and transmission (typically around 20%) for a petrol engine is accounted for"
Basic w-hist-016
How efficient is an electric motor in turning battery energy into motion?
An electric motor is highly efficient, typically converting about 90% of the electrical energy from the battery into useful motion at the motor shaft. That is much higher than a petrol engine's roughly 20%, which is one of the biggest advantages of EVs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"With an electric motor efficiency of 90% only 27 Wh kg-1 of useful energy (at the motor shaft) can be obtained from a lead acid battery."
Basic w-hist-017
Why is recharging time a big issue for battery vehicles?
Filling a petrol tank takes about a minute, but recharging a lead-acid battery normally takes several hours, even with sufficient power supply. Newer batteries have cut this to under an hour, but it is still much slower than refuelling a petrol car.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 26
"there is a minimum time, normally several hours, required to recharge a lead acid battery – whereas 45 l of petrol can be put into a vehicle in approximately minute."
Basic w-hist-018
Who built the first hybrid vehicle?
Ferdinand Porsche developed an early hybrid vehicle in 1900. His design could run on electricity from a battery or use a 2.5-horsepower Daimler petrol engine to drive a generator. This combined the strengths of both power sources in a single car.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 27
"In 1900, Ferdinand Porsche developed a hybrid vehicle... This vehicle could run with electricity either from the battery or from the 2.5 hp Daimler engine."
Basic w-hist-019
Why do railway companies prefer electric trains?
Electric trains require less maintenance, both of the locomotive itself and of the track. They are also clean at the point of use and have developed steadily through the twentieth century using both DC and AC systems, making them the preferred option for rail operators.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.2 The Middle of the Twentieth Century · Page: 28
"Electric trains are the preferred option of railway companies as they require less maintenance, both of the locomotive and the track."
Basic w-hist-020
Where are electric vehicles ideal because of their quiet, clean operation?
Electric vehicles produce no exhaust emissions where they are driven and are inherently quiet. That makes them ideal for warehouses, inside buildings, and on golf courses, where pollution from exhaust gases and engine noise would not be tolerated by people working nearby.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.2 The Middle of the Twentieth Century · Page: 28
"they produce no exhaust emissions in their immediate environment, and, secondly, that they are inherently quiet. This makes the electric vehicle ideal for environments such as warehouses, inside buildings and on golf courses"
Basic w-hist-021
What is one of the most common everyday uses of electric vehicles in Europe and the USA?
A very common use of battery electric vehicles in Europe and the USA is mobility devices for elderly and physically handicapped users. They can be driven on pavements, into shops and inside buildings, with a typical range of about 4 miles being enough.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.2 The Middle of the Twentieth Century · Page: 28
"One popular application of battery/electric drives is for mobility devices for the elderly and physically handicapped"
Basic w-hist-022
Why are EVs efficient in start-stop driving?
Electric vehicles keep their efficiency in start-stop driving, unlike IC engines which become very inefficient and polluting in stop-and-go conditions. This made EVs attractive for delivery work — the British 'milk float' is a famous historical example of this practical strength.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.2 The Middle of the Twentieth Century · Page: 29
"Electric vehicles also retain their efficiencies in start–stop driving, when an IC engine becomes very inefficient and polluting."
Basic w-hist-023
What is the Shinkansen, and when did it start running?
The Shinkansen is Japan's bullet train, a high-speed electric train. The first Tokaido Shinkansen line began service in 1964 between Tokyo and Osaka, covering about 515 km in around four hours. Modern Shinkansen trains reach speeds of around 300 kph.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 29
"The Tokaido Shinkansen began service in 1964 travelling from Tokyo to Osaka, a distance of 515.4 km, in 4 hours."
Basic w-hist-024
What is a maglev train?
A maglev (magnetic levitation) train does not use wheels. It is magnetically levitated above a special track and pushed forward by linear electric motors. The experimental Japanese JR-Maglev reached 581 kph (361 mph), the current world record for a crewed train.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 29
"Maglev trains do not use wheels but run on this special track. The train is magnetically levitated and moved forward by linear electric motors."
Basic w-hist-025
What recent advance enabled the modern wave of electric cars?
The biggest recent advance has been the lithium battery. It offers a reasonable specific energy and a much shorter charging time than older batteries. This made vehicles like the Tesla sports car, Nissan Leaf and Mitsubishi MiEV commercially practical.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 30
"the biggest change in electric vehicles in the last few years has been the development of the lithium battery, which has a reasonable specific energy and a more reasonable charge time than previous batteries."
Basic w-hist-026
What kind of hybrid is the Toyota Prius?
The Toyota Prius is a hybrid vehicle that cannot be recharged from the mains. It is efficient, but it still relies entirely on oil because it cannot draw electricity from the grid, which may be generated from a wide range of cleaner sources.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 32
"Non rechargeable hybrids, while efficient, still rely entirely on oil. As a result they cannot make use of mains electricity"
Basic w-hist-027
What kind of vehicle is the Chevrolet Volt?
The Chevrolet Volt is a rechargeable (plug-in) hybrid released by General Motors. It can complete many journeys using only electricity, and uses its internal combustion engine as a 'range extender' to keep going when the battery runs low on longer trips.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 32
"General Motors has released the Volt, a rechargeable hybrid... This can complete many of its journeys using electricity, relying on the IC engine as a range extender for longer journeys."
Basic w-hist-028
Why might a fuel-cell vehicle have an advantage over a battery EV?
A fuel-cell vehicle can give a much longer range than a battery EV. It normally runs on hydrogen, which is stored on board the vehicle. Honda's FCX Clarity is an example of a hydrogen fuel-cell car leased to customers in the USA.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 33
"Fuel cell vehicles have an advantage over batteries in that they can give much longer ranges."
Basic w-hist-029
How fast did electric two-wheeler sales grow in China?
Annual sales of electric bicycles and scooters in China grew from about 56,000 in 1998 to over 21 million in 2008. For comparison, China sold around 9.4 million automobiles in the same year, showing the huge popularity of two-wheeled EVs there.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 33
"annual sales of bicycles and scooters grew from 56 000 in 1998 to over 21 million in 2008, compared with 9.4 million automobiles in 2008."
Basic w-hist-030
What are the three main environmental benefits of electric vehicles?
Electric vehicles offer three main environmental benefits: reducing local pollution from the vehicles themselves, reducing dependence on oil and other fossil fuels, and reducing overall carbon-dioxide emissions, especially when the electricity used comes from cleaner sources such as nuclear or renewables.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2 Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Page: 34
"These benefits include reducing local pollution from the vehicles themselves, reducing dependence on oil and other fossil fuels and reduction of carbon emissions."
Basic w-hist-031
How does shifting from planes to electric trains save energy?
Electric trains use only a fraction of the energy per passenger-mile compared with aircraft. So encouraging people to take high-speed electric trains instead of flying for shorter trips can lead to large energy savings and reductions in carbon emissions overall.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2.1 Energy Saving and Overall Reduction of Carbon Emissions · Page: 35
"A good example is replacing air travel with transport by electric train, which uses a fraction of the energy per passenger mile."
Basic w-hist-032
What share of Britain's electricity came from low-carbon sources at the time of writing?
At the time of writing, around 20% of Britain's electricity was generated by nuclear power, with about another 10% coming from alternative sources such as wind and hydro. So roughly 30% of UK electricity came from low-carbon sources.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2.1 Energy Saving and Overall Reduction of Carbon Emissions · Page: 35
"In Britain nuclear energy provides around 20% of the electricity and a further 10% is generated by alternative energy such as wind and hydro."
Basic w-hist-033
What share of France's electricity in 2003 was carbon-free?
In 2003, around 90% of France's electricity generation released no carbon. About 75% was generated by nuclear power and a further 15% by hydro, while only about 10% came from fossil-fuel power stations — making French EVs unusually clean.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2.1 Energy Saving and Overall Reduction of Carbon Emissions · Page: 35
"In 2003, for example, approximately 75% of France's electricity was generated by nuclear power and a further 15% by hydro."
Basic w-hist-034
What is California's Low Emission Vehicle Program?
California's Low Emission Vehicle Program is a set of regulations that encouraged motor manufacturers to produce electric vehicles and pushed for the introduction of zero-emission cars. The complex rules led to important developments in fuel-cell, battery and hybrid electric vehicle technology.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2.2 Reducing Local Pollution · Page: 36
"The state of California has encouraged motor vehicle manufacturers to produce electric vehicles with its Low Emission Vehicle Program."
Basic w-hist-035
What does 'tail-pipe emissions' mean?
Tail-pipe emissions are the exhaust gases that come out of a vehicle's exhaust pipe — the gases produced by burning fuel in the engine. Electric vehicles have no tail-pipe emissions; any emissions are produced at the power station, which can control them better.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2.2 Reducing Local Pollution · Page: 36
"they do away with tail pipe emissions from IC vehicles. Much of the emission problem is transferred to the power stations, where it can be handled responsibly."
Indirect w-hist-036
Why did petrol cars overtake electric cars in the early 20th century?
Around 1900 electric cars were more reliable than petrol cars, but the 1911 invention of the IC self-starter and the arrival of cheap oil tipped the balance. Heavy, expensive batteries with slow recharging and short range made EVs less practical for most drivers.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"once cheap oil was widely available and the self-starter for the IC engine (invented in 1911) had arrived, the IC engine proved a more attractive option for powering vehicles."
Indirect w-hist-037
How much battery mass would be needed to match 45 litres of petrol?
To match the useful energy from 45 litres (10 gallons) of petrol, the textbook says you would need a staggering 2.7 tonnes of lead-acid batteries. That huge mass is exactly why early battery EVs could not compete on long-distance range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"For lead acid batteries to have the effective energy capacity of 45 l (10 gal) of petrol, a staggering 2.7 tonnes of batteries would be needed!"
Indirect w-hist-038
Why does owning a battery EV stay expensive over time?
Batteries are expensive when new, so an EV usually costs more than a similar petrol car. Batteries also have a limited life, typically about five years. Owners therefore must make further large investments to replace the battery pack periodically.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 27
"The batteries also have a limited life, typically 5 years, which means that a further large investment is needed periodically to renew the batteries."
Indirect w-hist-039
Why are high-speed electric trains becoming a real alternative to flying?
High-speed electric trains travel city centre to city centre, load faster than aircraft, and use only a fraction of the energy per passenger. In countries with low-carbon grids like France, they also avoid fossil fuels altogether, producing no CO2 emissions in use.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 30
"Most importantly, high speed trains use a fraction of the energy of aircraft. In countries such as France where electricity is largely generated by nuclear power electric trains do not rely on fossil fuels and produce no carbon emissions."
Indirect w-hist-040
How do typical US driving distances make a 100-mile-range EV practical?
In the USA, about 50% of journeys are under 25 miles, 75% under 40 miles, and 94% under 100 miles. So a modern EV like the Nissan Leaf with about 100 miles of range can comfortably cover the vast majority of typical daily trips.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.3 Usage Patterns for Electric Road Vehicles · Page: 36
"50% of all journeys are less than 25 miles (40 km), 75% are around 40 miles (64 km) and around 94% of journeys are less than 100 miles (161 km)."
Indirect w-hist-041
Why is regenerative braking valued for reasons beyond saving energy?
After all the losses through the motor, controller and battery, less than a third of the braking kinetic energy is recovered. So regenerative braking is valued as much as a convenient way of slowing down heavy electric cars as for the modest energy savings.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"regenerative breaking tends to be used as much as a convenient way of braking heavy vehicles, which electric cars normally are, as for energy efficiency."
Indirect w-hist-042
Why doesn't a plug-in hybrid need recharging on every trip?
A plug-in hybrid like the Chevrolet Volt has an electric-only range of about 40 miles, which already covers roughly 75% of typical journeys. For longer drives, its onboard petrol engine acts as a range extender, so the car never needs to stop to charge.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.3 Usage Patterns for Electric Road Vehicles · Page: 36
"The refuelable hybrid, the Chevrolet Volt, has a range of around 40 miles before it needs to resort to the IC engine, and therefore would be able to complete 75% of journeys on a single charge alone."
Indirect w-hist-043
How do EVs help city air quality even with a coal-heavy grid?
Even when grid electricity comes from fossil fuels, EVs remove tail-pipe pollution from busy city streets and shift those emissions to power stations, where they can be controlled. So cities still see cleaner air and quieter roads, even before the grid gets greener.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2.2 Reducing Local Pollution · Page: 36
"Much of the emission problem is transferred to the power stations, where it can be handled responsibly."
Indirect w-hist-044
Why is a Toyota Prius less environmentally clean than a plug-in hybrid?
The Toyota Prius is a non-rechargeable hybrid, so ultimately all its energy comes from petrol. A plug-in hybrid like the Chevrolet Volt can also draw electricity from the mains, and that electricity may come from cleaner sources such as nuclear or wind.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 32
"Non rechargeable hybrids, while efficient, still rely entirely on oil. As a result they cannot make use of mains electricity, which can be generated from a wide range of sources."
Indirect w-hist-045
Why don't trams and trolleybuses suffer from range anxiety?
Trams, trolleybuses and electric trains take their power directly from overhead lines or supply rails along their route, rather than from on-board batteries. So they never run out of stored energy and never need to be recharged or refuelled in service.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.3 Usage Patterns for Electric Road Vehicles · Page: 36
"Trains, trolleybuses and trams do not have limitations on range problem in the sense that they can travel wherever there are supply lines."
Medium w-hist-046
Using textbook numbers, how does shaft energy from 4 kg of petrol compare with 270 kg of lead-acid battery?
A 4 kg petrol tank (4.5 L) holds about 36,000 Wh of energy; at 20% engine plus gearbox efficiency, that gives about 7,200 Wh of useful shaft energy. A 270 kg lead-acid pack stores about 8,100 Wh; at 90% motor efficiency, also about 7,200 Wh.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 27
"Tank containing 4 kg (4.5 litres) of fuel with a calorific value of 36,000 Wh ... Lead acid battery with a mass of 270 kg ... energy 8100 Wh"
Medium w-hist-047
Why is doubling EV range much harder than doubling petrol-car range?
Doubling a petrol car's range needs only about 4 extra kilograms of fuel, but doubling a lead-acid EV's range needs another 270 kg of batteries. The extra mass itself uses energy to accelerate, decelerate and climb hills, eating into the range gained.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"To double the energy storage and hence the range of the petrol engine vehicle requires storage for a further 4.5 l of fuel with a mass of around 4 kg only, whereas to do the same with a lead acid battery vehicle requires an additional battery mass of about 270 kg."
Medium w-hist-048
Why is the recovery rate from regenerative braking actually quite low?
Each stage of regenerative braking loses some energy: the motor acting as generator, the controller, the battery storing the energy, then the controller and motor again on reuse. After all these losses, in practice less than a third of the kinetic energy is recovered.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.1 Early Days · Page: 25
"when the efficiency of generation, control, battery storage and passing the electricity back through the motor and controller is accounted for, less than a third of the energy is likely to be recovered."
Medium w-hist-049
Why does an EV's environmental benefit depend so much on the local grid mix?
Most EV emissions are shifted from the road to the power station. In France, where about 90% of electricity is low-carbon, EV charging is very clean. In a coal-heavy grid, well-to-wheel CO2 is much higher, so the same EV is greener in one country than another.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.2.1 Energy Saving and Overall Reduction of Carbon Emissions · Page: 35
"Replacing IC vehicles with electric vehicles saves energy, provided that the electricity is produced by an efficient grid system using modern power stations."
Medium w-hist-050
Why did the arrival of lithium batteries trigger the modern EV revival?
Lithium batteries store much more energy per kilogram than lead-acid and can be recharged in a shorter time. That combination made longer driving range and shorter charging stops practical, enabling commercial cars such as the Tesla sports car, Nissan Leaf and Mitsubishi MiEV.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 1. Introduction · Section: 1.1.3 Developments towards the End of the Twentieth Century and the Early Twenty-First Century · Page: 30
"the lithium battery, which has a reasonable specific energy and a more reasonable charge time than previous batteries. This has ultimately led to a series of commercial vehicles such as the Tesla sports car"
Basic w-type-001
What are the three main parts of a battery electric vehicle?
A battery electric vehicle consists of three core parts: an electric battery for energy storage, an electric motor to drive the wheels, and a controller that manages the power going from the battery to the motor, deciding how fast and in which direction the vehicle moves.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.1 Battery Electric Vehicles · Page: 38
"The vehicle consists of an electric battery for energy storage, an electric motor and a controller."
Basic w-type-002
How is a battery EV's battery recharged?
A battery EV's battery is normally recharged from mains electricity. The car is connected via a plug to a battery charging unit, which can either be carried on board the vehicle itself or fitted permanently at the charging point or station.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.1 Battery Electric Vehicles · Page: 38
"The battery is normally recharged from mains electricity via a plug and a battery charging unit that can be either carried on board or fitted at the charging point."
Basic w-type-003
What is a two-quadrant controller in an EV?
A two-quadrant controller lets an electric vehicle move forwards and backwards. It manages the power supplied to the motor, controlling vehicle speed in both directions. It is called 'two-quadrant' because it handles only the two driving directions, without controlled regenerative braking.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.1 Battery Electric Vehicles · Page: 38
"This is normally known as a 'two-quadrant controller' – forwards and backwards."
Basic w-type-004
What is a four-quadrant controller?
A four-quadrant controller adds regenerative braking in both directions to a two-quadrant design. It can drive the vehicle forwards and backwards and also brake regeneratively in either direction, recovering some kinetic energy back into the battery instead of wasting it as heat.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.1 Battery Electric Vehicles · Page: 38
"When in addition the controller allows regenerative braking in forward and reverse directions it is known as a 'four-quadrant controller'."
Basic w-type-005
What is a hybrid vehicle?
A hybrid vehicle is one that has two or more sources of power. The most common type combines an internal combustion engine with a battery and an electric motor (which can also act as a generator). This gives the car flexibility in how power is delivered.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 38
"A hybrid vehicle has two or more power sources... The most common types of hybrid vehicles combine an IC engine with a battery and an electric motor and generator."
Basic w-type-006
What are the two basic arrangements for hybrid vehicles?
There are two basic arrangements for hybrid vehicles: the series hybrid and the parallel hybrid. They differ in how the IC engine and the electric motor are linked to the wheels. Each has its own advantages depending on how the vehicle is used.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 38
"There are two basic arrangements for hybrid vehicles: the series hybrid and the parallel hybrid"
Basic w-type-007
How does a series hybrid drive the wheels?
In a series hybrid, only the electric motor drives the wheels. The IC engine never directly powers the wheels; instead it spins a generator that produces electricity. This electricity then either goes to the battery or directly powers the drive motor that turns the wheels.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 38
"In the series hybrid design the vehicle is driven by one or more electric motors supplied directly either from the battery or from the IC-engine-driven generator unit"
Basic w-type-008
How does a parallel hybrid drive the wheels?
In a parallel hybrid, both the IC engine and the electric motor can drive the wheels. The engine can drive directly through a transmission, the electric motor can drive through the transmission or directly, or the two can drive the wheels together at the same time.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 38
"In the parallel hybrid the vehicle can be driven either by the engine working directly through a transmission system, or by one or more electric motors"
Basic w-type-009
What is a non-rechargeable hybrid?
A non-rechargeable hybrid cannot be plugged in to recharge from the mains. All its energy ultimately comes from the petrol it carries; the battery is only ever charged from the IC engine while driving. So it always runs entirely from fossil fuel.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 39
"Figures 2.2–2.4 show the hybrids as non-rechargeable hybrids, in which case the hybrid EV will need to run entirely from fossil fuel."
Basic w-type-010
What is a rechargeable (plug-in) hybrid?
A rechargeable hybrid has a much larger battery than a non-rechargeable hybrid, large enough to give the vehicle a useful electric-only range. The battery can be recharged from the mains when the car is parked, in addition to being charged by the IC engine while driving.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 39
"An alternative is to use rechargeable hybrids which normally have much larger batteries to give the vehicle an effective range when working from the battery alone."
Basic w-type-011
Can hybrid vehicles use regenerative braking?
Yes. Both series and parallel hybrid designs allow regenerative braking. The drive motor temporarily works as a generator, which simultaneously slows the vehicle and converts some of its kinetic energy back into electricity to recharge the battery, instead of losing it as heat.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 39
"Both series and parallel hybrid designs allow for regenerative braking – for the drive motor to work as a generator and simultaneously slow down the vehicle and charge the battery."
Basic w-type-012
Where is the series hybrid traditionally used?
The series hybrid is traditionally used in specialist applications. The diesel-powered railway engine is nearly always a series hybrid, as are some ships. Some special all-terrain vehicles use a series hybrid layout with a separately controlled electric motor in each wheel.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"The series hybrid traditionally is used only in specialist applications. For example, the diesel-powered railway engine is nearly always a series hybrid"
Basic w-type-013
What is the main disadvantage of a series hybrid?
The main disadvantage of the series hybrid is that power from the engine cannot be transmitted mechanically to the wheels. Instead, every bit of engine power must pass through both the generator and the electric motor, with losses at each stage of conversion.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"The main disadvantage of the series hybrid is that power from the engine cannot be transmitted mechanically to the wheels but must pass through both the generator and the motors."
Basic w-type-014
Why are electric machines smaller in a parallel hybrid?
In a parallel hybrid the electric machines do not have to convert all of the vehicle's energy, because the engine can still power the wheels directly. So the motor and generator can be much smaller and cheaper than they would need to be in a series hybrid.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"The electric machines can be much smaller and cheaper, because they do not have to convert all the energy."
Basic w-type-015
What is the 'degree of hybridisation'?
The degree of hybridisation is a variable used to describe how much of a parallel hybrid's power comes from its electric system versus its IC engine. A greater degree of hybridisation lets the car use a smaller IC engine running near its optimum efficiency more often.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"The greater the degree of hybridisation, the greater the scope for using a smaller IC engine, and having it operate at near its optimum efficiency for a greater proportion of the time."
Basic w-type-016
What kind of battery does the Toyota Prius use?
The Toyota Prius uses a nickel-metal hydride (NiMH) battery. It is a non-rechargeable hybrid; the battery is only charged from the engine while driving. The car cannot be plugged in, so it is refuelled with petrol only, the conventional way.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"The Toyota Prius... is a non-rechargeable hybrid. A nickel metal hydride battery is used."
Basic w-type-017
What is the Toyota Prius's fuel economy?
The Toyota Prius has a high overall fuel economy of about 56.5 mpg (US gallons) or 68 mpg (UK gallons). Its top speed is 160 kph (100 mph), and it can accelerate from 0 to 100 kph in about 13.4 seconds.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"This car uses regenerative braking and has a high overall fuel economy of about 56.5 mpg (US) or 68 mpg (UK)."
Basic w-type-018
Why does the Prius use the electric motor at start-up and low speeds?
At start-up and low speeds, the Toyota Prius runs solely on its electric motor. This avoids using the IC engine when it is least efficient and most polluting, which improves fuel economy and reduces emissions during the kinds of stop-and-go driving common in towns.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"At startup or at low speeds the Prius is powered solely by the electric motor, avoiding the use of the IC engine when it is at its most polluting and least efficient."
Basic w-type-019
Why is the Honda Insight cited as a good example of a parallel hybrid?
The Honda Insight is given as a good example of a true parallel hybrid vehicle. Like other parallel hybrids, it allows both the IC engine and the electric motor to drive the wheels, either separately or together, sharing the work between the two power sources.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 42
"Many companies are now bringing out vehicles that are true parallel hybrids. The Honda Insight is a good example."
Basic w-type-020
How far can the Chevrolet Volt drive on battery alone?
The Chevrolet Volt can run for up to about 40 miles (64 km) on its battery alone before the IC engine needs to start. It carries a larger battery than non-rechargeable hybrids and can be recharged from the mains while not in use.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 42
"It carries a larger battery than non-rechargeable hybrids and can run for up to 40 miles (64 km) using the battery alone."
Basic w-type-021
What is a fuelled EV?
A fuelled EV works on the same basic principle as a battery EV, but the rechargeable electric battery is replaced by a fuel cell or by a metal-air battery that runs on a chemical fuel. The fuel is consumed during operation and refilled, like petrol.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"The basic principle of EVs using fuel is much the same as with the battery EV, but with a fuel cell or metal air battery replacing the rechargeable electric battery."
Basic w-type-022
When were fuel cells invented?
Fuel cells were invented in about 1840, so the basic technology has existed for nearly two centuries. Even so, they are still an unfamiliar technology for most people today, and full details of their operation are discussed in Chapter 5 of the textbook.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"Although invented in about 1840, fuel cells are an unfamiliar technology for most people"
Basic w-type-023
What is the main fuel for fuel cells in EVs?
The main fuel for fuel cells used in EVs is hydrogen. The hydrogen can be stored directly on board the vehicle, though this is not easy. An alternative is to make hydrogen on board from a liquid fuel such as methanol using an onboard reformer.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"a major issue with fuel cells is that, generally, they require hydrogen fuel."
Basic w-type-024
Where does the Necar 5 fit among the types of EVs?
The Necar 5 is a fuel-cell vehicle that carries an onboard methanol reformer. It can be refuelled with methanol the same way a normal car is filled with petrol. The Necar 5 has a top speed of 150 kph and uses about 5 litres of methanol per 100 km.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"This is the approach taken with the Necar 5, which has an onboard reformer. The car can simply be refuelled with methanol in the same way as a normal vehicle is filled up with petrol. The car has a top speed of 150 kph and an overall fuel consumption of 5 l/100 km of methanol."
Basic w-type-025
Why are buses a promising early use of fuel cells?
Buses are a very promising early application of fuel cells because they only refuel at one place, usually their depot. This makes the special infrastructure needed for novel fuels like hydrogen much easier to provide, since you don't need a station on every street.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"Public service vehicles such as buses can more conveniently use novel fuels such as hydrogen, because they only fill up at one place. Buses are a very promising early application of fuel cells"
Basic w-type-026
How does a zinc-air battery fit into the EV power-source landscape?
A zinc-air battery is a kind of metal-air battery in which zinc electrodes react with oxygen from air to produce electricity. It is a variation on a fuel cell, and the zinc electrodes are recycled after being consumed, with the EFTC trialling them in zero-emission buses.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"Zinc–air batteries produced by the Electric Fuel Transportation Company (EFTC) have been tested in vehicles both in the USA and in Europe."
Basic w-type-027
Where do metal-air batteries fit among the types of EV power sources?
Metal-air batteries are a variation on the fuel cell. They are refuelled by physically replacing the metal electrodes, which can then be recycled. Zinc-air batteries are a particularly promising battery in this class and have been tested in buses in the USA and Europe.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"Metal–air batteries (described in Chapter 3) are a variation on fuel cells. They are refuelled by replacing the metal electrodes, which can be recycled."
Basic w-type-028
How are trolleybuses and trams powered?
Trolleybuses and trams take their power from overhead electric supply lines along their route. The trolleybus usually also has a small battery so it can travel a short distance off-wire. Both were once widely used as zero-emission city transport in many cities.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.4 EVs using Supply Lines · Page: 43
"Normally electricity is supplied by overhead lines and a small battery is used on the trolleybus to give it a limited range without using the supply lines."
Basic w-type-029
Why were many trams and trolleybuses withdrawn from service?
When trams and trolleybuses were withdrawn, cost mattered more than environmental concerns. Fossil fuel was cheap, overhead wires were thought unsightly, inflexible, expensive and a maintenance burden, and trams were seen as impeding private cars in busy streets, so cities ripped them out.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.4 EVs using Supply Lines · Page: 43
"Fossil fuel was cheap and overhead wires were considered unsightly, inflexible, expensive and a maintenance burden. Trams in particular were considered to impede the progress of the all-important private motor car."
Basic w-type-030
What are flywheels and supercapacitors best at?
Flywheels and supercapacitors both have a high specific power. That means they can take in and release energy very quickly. The amount of energy they store is still rather small, so they have good power density but poor energy density compared with batteries.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.5 EVs which use Flywheels or Supercapacitors · Page: 43
"both of these devices have high specific powers, which means that they can take in and give out energy very quickly. Although they can do this, the amount of energy they can store is currently rather small."
Basic w-type-031
How does the Parry flywheel tram work?
The Parry tram stores energy in a flywheel. While the tram stops at a station, an electric motor spins the flywheel up to speed. The tram is then driven from the flywheel through a variable cone-and-ball gearbox; braking transfers kinetic energy back into the flywheel.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.5 EVs which use Flywheels or Supercapacitors · Page: 43
"The vehicle is essentially a tram in which the flywheel is speeded up by an electric motor. Power to achieve this is supplied when the tram rests while picking up passengers at one of its frequent stations."
Basic w-type-032
How are ultracapacitors used in the MAN hybrid bus?
In the MAN bus, the main power comes from a diesel engine. An ultracapacitor sits alongside it to recover kinetic energy when the bus slows down and to provide extra peak power when accelerating. This lets the bus use a smaller engine or fuel cell.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.5 EVs which use Flywheels or Supercapacitors · Page: 43
"The MAN bus, for example, uses a diesel engine; the purpose of the capacitor is to allow the recovery of kinetic energy when the vehicle slows down, and to increase the available peak power during times of rapid acceleration"
Basic w-type-033
What is a solar-powered vehicle?
A solar-powered vehicle uses photovoltaic cells on its body to convert sunlight directly into electricity for the motor. The Honda Dream, which won the 1996 World Solar Challenge, crossed Australia averaging about 85 kph. Such cars are expensive and only work in very sunny conditions.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.6 Solar-Powered Vehicles · Page: 44
"Solar-powered vehicles such as the Honda Dream, which won the 1996 World Solar Challenge, are expensive and only work effectively in areas of high sunshine."
Basic w-type-034
What is a linear motor?
A linear motor is essentially an electric motor that has been 'unrolled'. Instead of producing rotary motion as a torque, its unrolled stator and rotor produce a straight-line force along their length, making it useful for systems like maglev trains which travel along a track.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.7 Vehicles using Linear Motors · Page: 45
"A linear motor is an electric motor that has had its stator and rotor 'unrolled' so that instead of producing rotary motion due to torque it produces linear motion due to the force along its length."
Basic w-type-035
Where are linear motors most important in transport today?
Linear motors are most important today in maglev trains. Combined with magnetic levitation, they propel a train forward along a special track without wheels. Japan's experimental JR-Maglev train uses linear motors and has reached speeds of about 581 kph.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.7 Vehicles using Linear Motors · Page: 45
"Linear motors combined with magnetic levitation are becoming increasingly important due to their use in Maglev trains."
Indirect w-type-036
Why might a parallel hybrid let you use a smaller IC engine?
In a parallel hybrid, the electric motor and battery can supply peak demand bursts during acceleration. So the IC engine only needs to supply the base load, typically around 50% of peak. That lets the engine be smaller and run closer to its most efficient operating point.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"A popular arrangement is to obtain the basic power to run the vehicle, normally around 50% of peak power requirements, from the IC engine, and to take additional power from the electric motor and battery"
Indirect w-type-037
Why does a diesel locomotive use a series hybrid layout?
A diesel locomotive uses a series hybrid because a mechanical drive between a powerful diesel and the wheels would be very heavy and inefficient. Instead, the diesel spins a generator and electric motors at each axle, giving smooth, controllable torque without complicated transmissions or gearboxes.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"the diesel-powered railway engine is nearly always a series hybrid"
Indirect w-type-038
Why is the Toyota Prius not a 'pure' parallel hybrid?
The Prius mostly behaves as a parallel hybrid because its IC engine can drive the wheels directly. But it also has a separate motor and generator and a complex epicyclic 'power-splitter' gearbox, so it can also operate in series mode at times — making it a mixed design.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 42
"However, it does have a separate motor and generator, can operate in series mode and is not a 'pure parallel hybrid. It has a fairly complex 'power splitter' gearbox, based on epicyclic gears"
Indirect w-type-039
Why is the Honda FCX Clarity sometimes called a fuel-cell battery hybrid?
The Honda FCX Clarity uses a hydrogen fuel cell together with a lithium-ion battery in the same vehicle. Because energy comes from two different electric sources — the fuel cell and the battery, working in combination — the car can also be described as a fuel-cell battery hybrid.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.3 Fuelled EVs · Page: 42
"As the vehicle uses a lithium ion battery working in conjunction with the fuel cell it may also be described as a fuel cell electric battery hybrid!"
Indirect w-type-040
Why might trams and trolleybuses make sense again today?
Today IC cars clog streets and pollute the air, so the priorities have changed. The textbook argues that EVs powered by overhead supply lines, like trams and trolleybuses, could once again make a useful contribution to clean urban transport, and shouldn't be overlooked by designers.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.4 EVs using Supply Lines · Page: 43
"Today, when IC engine vehicles are clogging up and polluting towns and cities, the criteria have changed again. EVs powered by supply lines could make a useful impact on modern transport"
Indirect w-type-041
Why is a flywheel-only car not practical for long journeys?
A flywheel has high specific power — it can absorb and deliver energy quickly — but its energy density is poor. So it cannot store enough energy for a long journey. That is why flywheels are mostly used to assist hybrids rather than as the only source.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.5 EVs which use Flywheels or Supercapacitors · Page: 43
"they have a good power density, they have a poor energy density."
Indirect w-type-042
Why isn't the Honda Dream solar car practical for everyday use?
Solar cars like the Honda Dream are expensive and only work effectively in regions with intense sunshine. Their PV cells cannot capture enough energy in cloudy or short-day conditions for normal commuting. More realistically, solar cells can be used to top up a battery EV's charge.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.6 Solar-Powered Vehicles · Page: 44
"it is unlikely that a car of this nature would be a practical proposition as a vehicle for everyday use"
Indirect w-type-043
Why are there so many possible hybrid combinations?
Possible hybrid energy sources include rechargeable batteries, fuel cells, solar cells, IC engines, supply lines, flywheels and capacitors. Any two of these can be paired to make a hybrid, giving over 21 two-source combinations alone, with even more options when three or more are combined.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.5 EVs which use Flywheels or Supercapacitors · Page: 43
"Any two or more of these can be used together to form a hybrid EV, giving over 21 combinations of hybrids with two energy sources."
Indirect w-type-044
Why does the Volt's IC engine sometimes engage at 30–70 mph?
At 30–70 mph, when the Volt's battery is below its charge threshold, the control system sometimes clutches the IC engine into the drive through an output-split planetary gearset. This lets the engine help the traction motor directly, improving high-speed performance and efficiency.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 42
"At certain loads and speeds, namely 30–70 mph (48–112 kph), the IC engine may at times be engaged mechanically via a clutch to an output split planetary gearset and assist the traction motor to propel the Volt."
Indirect w-type-045
Why is the Volt sometimes described as three vehicles in one?
Depending on its battery state of charge and operating conditions, the Volt can run as a pure electric vehicle, a series hybrid, or a parallel hybrid. The control system picks whichever drive mode is most efficient at the time, so the car effectively switches identities.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 42
"the Volt can operate as a pure EV, a series hybrid or a parallel hybrid depending on the battery's state of charge (SOC) and operating conditions."
Medium w-type-046
Compare series and parallel hybrids on efficiency.
A series hybrid sends all engine power through a generator and then through electric motors, with losses at each step. A parallel hybrid lets the engine power the wheels mechanically when convenient, with the electric motor only supplementing it, so total energy losses can be lower.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"The main disadvantage of the series hybrid is that power from the engine cannot be transmitted mechanically to the wheels but must pass through both the generator and the motors."
Medium w-type-047
What mechanical components do hybrids let you save?
In the series arrangement, hybrids let you remove the gearbox; the transmission can be simplified and the differential can be eliminated by using a pair of motors on opposite wheels. In both series and parallel layouts, the conventional battery-starter arrangement can also be eliminated.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 40
"In the series arrangement there is no need for a gearbox, transmission can be simplified and the differential can be eliminated by using a pair of motors fitted on opposite wheels. In both series and parallel arrangements the conventional battery starter arrangement can be eliminated."
Medium w-type-048
Why is the Prius's epicyclic 'power-splitter' gearbox important?
The Prius's power-splitter epicyclic gearbox lets power from the electric motor and the IC engine be sent to the wheels in almost any proportion. It also routes power from the wheels to the generator during regenerative braking, giving the system great flexibility in choosing the best mix.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.2 The IC Engine/Electric Hybrid Vehicle · Page: 42
"a fairly complex 'power splitter' gearbox, based on epicyclic gears, that allows power from both the electric motor and the IC engine, in almost any proportion, to be sent to the wheels or gearbox."
Medium w-type-049
Why do flywheels and supercapacitors suit hybrids but not stand-alone EVs?
Flywheels and supercapacitors can absorb and release energy quickly, perfect for handling braking energy and acceleration bursts in a hybrid. But their energy density is poor, so they cannot store enough energy for a long journey on their own, ruling out a stand-alone EV.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.5 EVs which use Flywheels or Supercapacitors · Page: 43
"Energy stores such as capacitors and flywheels can be used in a wide range of hybrids."
Medium w-type-050
Could solar cells be useful on an ordinary EV even though solar cars aren't practical?
Yes. Although a pure solar car like the Honda Dream is impractical for daily use, the textbook says it is perfectly feasible to wrap PV cells on a commuter EV's surface to keep the battery topped up. Falling solar costs may make this practical in future.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 2. Types of Electric Vehicles – EV Architecture · Section: 2.6 Solar-Powered Vehicles · Page: 44
"The concept of using solar cells, which can be wrapped to the surface of the car, to keep the batteries of a commuter vehicle topped up is a perfectly feasible idea"
Basic w-batt-001
What is a battery in an EV?
A battery is a set of two or more electric cells connected together. The cells convert chemical energy directly into electrical energy. In a classical EV the battery is the only energy store and is the part with the highest cost, weight and volume on the whole vehicle.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.1 Introduction · Page: 45
"A battery consists of two or more electric cells connected together. The cells convert chemical energy to electrical energy."
Basic w-batt-002
What makes a battery cell produce electricity?
A cell has positive and negative electrodes sitting in a liquid called the electrolyte. A chemical reaction between the electrodes and the electrolyte releases electrons, which produces direct-current (DC) electricity when the cell is connected into a circuit.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.1 Introduction · Page: 45
"The cells consist of positive and negative electrodes in an electrolyte. It is the chemical reaction between the electrodes and the electrolyte which generates DC electricity."
Basic w-batt-003
What is a rechargeable (secondary) battery?
A secondary or rechargeable battery is one whose chemical reaction can be reversed. By forcing current through it in the opposite direction during charging, the battery is returned to its charged state, ready to deliver electricity again. Lead-acid is the classic example.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.1 Introduction · Page: 45
"In the case of secondary or rechargeable batteries the chemical reaction can be reversed by reversing the current and the battery returned to a charged state."
Basic w-batt-004
What is internal resistance in a battery?
Internal resistance is the small built-in resistance every battery has. When current flows out, part of the battery's voltage drops across this resistance, so the terminal voltage you measure is lower than the open-circuit voltage. The lower the internal resistance, the better for EVs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.1 Cell and Battery Voltages · Page: 48
"the voltage at the terminals is a different voltage V, because of the voltage across the internal resistance R."
Basic w-batt-005
What is open-circuit voltage?
Open-circuit voltage is the voltage across a battery's terminals when no current is flowing. It is the battery's 'fixed' internal voltage with no load connected. As soon as current flows, the terminal voltage drops below this value because of the internal resistance.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.1 Cell and Battery Voltages · Page: 48
"if the current I is zero, the terminal voltage is equal to E, and so E is often referred to as the open-circuit voltage."
Basic w-batt-006
What is the unit used to express battery capacity?
Battery capacity is given in amp-hours (Ah). One amp-hour is the charge a battery delivers when one amp flows for one hour. A 10 Ah battery, for example, could in principle supply one amp for ten hours, or two amps for five hours.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.2 Charge (or Amphour) Capacity · Page: 48
"Instead the amphour is used – 1 A flowing for 1 hour. The capacity of a battery might be, say, '10 Ah'."
Basic w-batt-007
Why does battery capacity drop if you draw current quickly?
When current is drawn quickly, unwanted side reactions inside the cell take place faster. So less of the stored charge becomes useful electricity. For example, a nominally 100 Ah battery may give only about 70 Ah if discharged in one hour, but 110 Ah if discharged over 20 hours.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.2 Charge (or Amphour) Capacity · Page: 48
"if the charge is removed in 1 hour, the capacity falls very considerably to about 70 Ah. On the other hand, if the current is drawn off more slowly, in say 20 hours, the capacity rises to about 110 Ah."
Basic w-batt-008
What does '2C' or '0.4C' mean in battery talk?
C stands for the battery's capacity in amphours. Saying '2C' means a current equal to twice the amphour value, and '0.4C' means 0.4 times it. For a 42 Ah battery, 2C is 84 A and 0.4C is 16.8 A. It scales current to battery size.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.2 Charge (or Amphour) Capacity · Page: 48
"Battery users talk about 'a discharge current of 2C', or 'charging the battery at 0.4C'. In these cases this would mean a 'discharge current of 84 A', or a 'charging current of 16.8 A'."
Basic w-batt-009
What is specific energy in a battery?
Specific energy is the amount of electrical energy a battery stores per kilogram of its mass, measured in watt-hours per kilogram (Wh/kg). A higher specific energy means more energy for the same weight — directly meaning a longer driving range for the EV.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.4 Specific Energy · Page: 50
"Specific energy is the amount of electrical energy stored for every kilogram of battery mass. It has units of Wh kg−1"
Basic w-batt-010
What is energy density in a battery?
Energy density is the amount of electrical energy a battery stores per cubic metre (or per litre) of its volume, measured in Wh/m³ or Wh/L. A higher energy density means the battery takes up less space inside the car for the same stored energy.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.5 Energy Density · Page: 50
"Energy density is the amount of electrical energy stored per cubic metre of battery volume. It normally has units of Wh m−3."
Basic w-batt-011
What is specific power?
Specific power is the amount of power a battery can deliver per kilogram of its mass, in watts per kilogram (W/kg). It tells you how fast the battery can release its energy — useful for hard acceleration. Batteries with high specific power often have lower specific energy.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.6 Specific Power · Page: 51
"Specific power is the amount of power obtained per kilogram of battery."
Basic w-batt-012
What is a Ragone plot?
A Ragone plot is a graph of specific power against specific energy on logarithmic axes. It shows how a battery's specific energy drops as specific power rises. It is used to compare different battery types and other energy sources fairly across many operating points.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.6 Specific Power · Page: 51
"This is often done using a graph of specific power against specific energy, which is known as a 'Ragone plot'."
Basic w-batt-013
What is amphour (charge) efficiency?
Amphour efficiency is the ratio of the charge a battery gives back to the charge put into it during charging. Real batteries are always below 100% efficient; the efficiency depends on battery type, temperature, charging rate and the battery's state of charge.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.7 Amphour (or Charge) Efficiency · Page: 51
"In an ideal world a battery would return the entire charge put into it, in which case the amphour efficiency is 100%. However, none do!"
Basic w-batt-014
What is energy efficiency of a battery?
Energy efficiency is the ratio of the electrical energy a battery delivers when discharging to the energy needed to recharge it to the same state. Faster charging and discharging both cut this efficiency. High energy efficiency is one of the key reasons electric vehicles save energy overall.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.8 Energy Efficiency · Page: 51
"it is defined as the ratio of electrical energy supplied by a battery to the amount of electrical energy required to return it to the state before discharge."
Basic w-batt-015
What is self-discharge in a battery?
Self-discharge is when a battery slowly loses its charge by itself, even when left unused. The rate depends on the battery type and on temperature — higher temperatures greatly speed up self-discharge. Some batteries cannot be left for long periods without recharging.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.9 Self-discharge Rates · Page: 51
"Most batteries discharge when left unused, and this is known as self-discharge."
Basic w-batt-016
What are deep cycles in a battery?
A deep cycle is a discharge that takes a battery down to a low state of charge, such as 20%, then back up to full again. Most rechargeable batteries will only survive a few hundred deep cycles. This number reflects battery lifetime and EV running costs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.2.12 Battery Life and Number of Deep Cycles · Page: 51
"Most rechargeable batteries will only undergo a few hundred deep cycles to 20% of the battery charge."
Basic w-batt-017
What is a lead-acid battery made from?
In a lead-acid cell, the negative plate is spongy lead, the positive plate is lead dioxide, and the electrolyte is dilute sulfuric acid. During discharge, both plates form lead sulfate and the electrolyte becomes more dilute. Charging reverses the reactions and restores the acid.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.3.1 Lead Acid Battery Basics · Page: 55
"the negative plates have a spongy lead as their active material, while the positive plates have an active material of lead dioxide. The plates are immersed in an electrolyte of dilute sulfuric acid."
Basic w-batt-018
What is a VRLA battery?
VRLA stands for valve-regulated sealed lead-acid. The battery is sealed and uses a gel electrolyte, so there is no need to top up with water. A small valve releases gas only if pressure builds up, making it essentially maintenance-free under normal use.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.3.3 Battery Life and Maintenance · Page: 57
"This feature is a safety requirement and leads to the name 'valve-regulated sealed lead acid' (VRLA) for this modern type of battery."
Basic w-batt-019
What is sulfation in a lead-acid battery?
Sulfation happens when a lead-acid battery is left in a discharged state for two weeks or more. The lead sulfate on the plates forms into large crystals that are hard to convert back into lead or lead dioxide, and they coat the plates with an insulating layer.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 3. Batteries, Flywheels and Supercapacitors · Section: 3.3.3 Battery Life and Maintenance · Page: 57
"the process called 'sulfation'. This occurs if the battery is left for a long period (i.e. 2 weeks or more) in a discharged state."
Basic w-batt-020
How many cycles does a typical lead-acid EV battery last?
