The ideal aerodynamic shape is a teardrop, like a free-falling water droplet. Its drag coefficient can be as low as 0.04 when its length-to-diameter ratio is 2.4. Real cars never get this low, but aerodynamicists treat the teardrop as the 'aiming point' for body design.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 233
"The ideal aerodynamic shape is a teardrop... having the lowest value of Cd = 0.04 when the ratio of the length to diameter is 2.4."
Basic w-des-002
What is a typical drag coefficient for a normal hatchback?
A typical saloon or hatchback car has a drag coefficient (Cd) between about 0.3 and 0.5. A reasonably aerodynamic van is around 0.5. The Honda Civic hatchback, for example, has Cd ≈ 0.36 with a frontal area of about 1.9 m².
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 233
"The aerodynamic drag coefficient for a saloon or hatchback car normally varies from 0.3 to 0.5"
Basic w-des-003
What's the drag coefficient of the GM EV1 electric car?
The GM EV1 has an extraordinarily low drag coefficient of 0.19. The Honda Insight hybrid is also very low at 0.25, while the Bluebird record-breaking electric car achieved Cd ≈ 0.16 — all illustrating how aerodynamics matter even more for EVs than for petrol cars.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 233
"Good examples are the Honda Insight hybrid electric car, with a Cd of 0.25, and the General Motors EV1 electric vehicle with an even lower Cd of 0.19. The Bluebird record-breaking electric car had a Cd of 0.16."
Basic w-des-004
How does lowering Cd from 0.30 to 0.19 affect range?
Drag — and the power used to overcome it — is directly proportional to Cd. Lowering Cd from 0.30 to 0.19 cuts drag to about 63% of the original. So battery capacity needed to overcome air drag drops by about 37%, or the vehicle range goes up significantly.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 233
"a reduction of Cd from 0.3 to 0.19 will result in a reduction in drag of 0.19/0.3, that is 63.3%."
Basic w-des-005
What is the Kamm-back design?
The Kamm back is an aerodynamic trick used on cars like the Honda Insight. Beyond a certain point, tapering the rear of the body produces little extra benefit, so the body is simply cut off vertically. This avoids long, useless tail sections while keeping drag low.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.2 Body/Chassis Aerodynamic Shape · Page: 236
"the teardrop shape is abruptly cut off in what is called the Kamm effect. The Kamm back takes advantage of the fact that beyond a certain point there is little aerodynamic advantage of rounding off or tapering"
Basic w-des-006
Why does the Honda Insight have narrower rear wheels?
On the Honda Insight, the rear track is 110 mm narrower than the front. This lets the body taper towards the back, approaching a teardrop shape. Narrower rear wheels plus a sloping floor and rear hatch together let the car neck in smoothly, reducing aerodynamic drag.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.2 Body/Chassis Aerodynamic Shape · Page: 236
"The rear wheels are placed 110 mm closer together than the front wheels, allowing the body to narrow."
Basic w-des-007
Why are under-body covers used on EVs?
The under-body is a major source of turbulence. EVs and hybrids like the Honda Insight use flat under-body covers to smooth airflow beneath the vehicle, reduce drag and improve range. Separate fairings protect exhaust pipes and fuel tanks so air still flows smoothly around them.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.2 Body/Chassis Aerodynamic Shape · Page: 236
"The Insight body features a flat under-body design that smoothes air flow under the car including three under-body covers."
Basic w-des-008
Does rolling resistance depend on vehicle speed?
No. Rolling resistance is independent of speed. It is set by the coefficient of rolling resistance and the vehicle's weight. Higher tyre pressure or better-designed EV tyres can lower the coefficient, but the force stays roughly the same at 20 kph or at 100 kph.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.3 Consideration of Rolling Resistance · Page: 238
"The rolling drag is independent of speed."
Basic w-des-009
Why is aerodynamic drag unimportant at low speeds?
Aerodynamic drag rises with the square of speed, so it is tiny at low speeds. Below about 50 kph, rolling resistance dominates and aerodynamics barely matter. Above 50 kph, aerodynamic drag rises quickly and becomes the major influence on the power needed to keep moving.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.3 Consideration of Rolling Resistance · Page: 238
"at low speeds, for example under 50 kph, aerodynamics have very little influence, whereas at high speeds they are the major influence on power requirements."
Basic w-des-010
Why don't EVs need a clutch or multi-gear gearbox?
An electric motor produces torque from zero speed upwards, so no clutch is needed to disengage it. A single fixed gear ratio is normally enough, because the motor's wide speed range covers everything from idling to top speed. This makes EV transmissions far simpler than IC engine ones.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.4 Transmission Efficiency · Page: 238
"no clutch is needed as the motor can provide torque from zero speed upwards. Similarly, a conventional gearbox is not needed, as a single-ratio gear is normally all that is needed."
Basic w-des-011
What are the three main EV transmission layouts?
Three main layouts exist: (a) one motor driving a pair of wheels through a differential, (b) one motor per wheel via a small gearbox (no differential needed), and (c) the motor mounted directly inside the wheel hub. Each trades cost, weight and complexity differently.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.4 Transmission Efficiency · Page: 238
"The three basic variations of electric vehicle transmission are illustrated in Figure 9.6."
Basic w-des-012
What is an in-wheel motor?
An in-wheel motor is built directly into the hub assembly of a wheel, with no shaft, gearbox or differential between motor and wheel. It can offer 100% mechanical transmission efficiency. Popular in electric scooters and bicycles, it saves space but raises the wheel's mass.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.4 Transmission Efficiency · Page: 239
"to connect the motor directly to the wheels via a shaft, or actually to design the motor as part of the hub assembly. This system has huge potential advantages, including a 100% transmission efficiency."
Basic w-des-013
Why does extra vehicle mass matter so much in an EV?
Heavier vehicles have higher rolling resistance, climb hills less efficiently, and waste more kinetic energy starting and stopping in cities. In an EV, all of these mean bigger and more expensive batteries to keep the same range. So weight directly drives up the vehicle's cost.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.5 Consideration of Vehicle Mass · Page: 242
"The mass of an electric vehicle has a critical effect on the performance, range and cost of an electric vehicle."
Basic w-des-014
Why is hill climbing demanding for an EV?
Climbing a hill needs power proportional to the vehicle's weight and to the sine of the slope angle. A 1500 kg EV at 80 kph on a 10° slope needs about 12× the power used on the flat. That is why motors must be sized for the worst hills.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.5 Consideration of Vehicle Mass · Page: 242
"the 1500 kg car... has to provide approximately 12 times as much power at 10◦ than is needed on the flat."
Basic w-des-015
What is regenerative braking's practical limit?
The maximum practical limit on the recovery of kinetic energy through regenerative braking is about 40%. In light vehicles the losses associated with starting and stopping are smaller anyway, so the benefit of regenerative braking is also smaller than in heavy cars on hilly or stop-start routes.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.5 Consideration of Vehicle Mass · Page: 243
"The maximum practical limit on the recovery of kinetic energy is about 40%."
Basic w-des-016
What is a monocoque body?
A monocoque integrates body and chassis into a single shell where every part — including the glazing — contributes to strength and stiffness. This makes the vehicle much lighter than a separate body-on-frame chassis. Most modern cars use monocoque construction, though some EVs still use a separate chassis.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.1 Body/Chassis Requirements · Page: 244
"the body and chassis have been combined as a monocoque so that every part, including the glazing, adds to the strength and stiffness, resulting in a much lighter vehicle."
Basic w-des-017
What should an ideal vehicle chassis or body do?
It should be strong, light, rigid, vibration-free, aerodynamic, impact-resistant and able to crumple evenly in a crash to protect passengers. It must also be cheap, corrosion-proof, aesthetically pleasing, and provide hard points to which other components can be attached securely.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.1 Body/Chassis Requirements · Page: 244
"It should be: strong; light; rigid; vibration-free... resistant to impact; able to crumple evenly in an accident... cheap; aesthetically pleasing; corrosion proof."
Basic w-des-018
How does EV layout differ from IC car layout?
An EV has no engine bonnet, fuel tank or exhaust system. Batteries can be placed anywhere along the bottom of the vehicle (often low, for a low centre of gravity). Motors and gearing can be in the hubs. This gives designers vastly more flexibility in vehicle layout.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.2 Body/Chassis Layout · Page: 246
"there is no need for a bonnet housing and engine. In addition, batteries can be placed virtually anywhere along the bottom (for stability) of the vehicle"
Basic w-des-019
What is the Twike three-wheeler?
The Twike is a popular three-wheel electric commuter vehicle. It has one wheel at the front and two at the rear, with two passengers sitting side by side. The two rear wheels provide stability. Its low-speed urban use makes its 'wrong-way-round' aerodynamic shape acceptable.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.2 Body/Chassis Layout · Page: 246
"one of the most popular three-wheel electric vehicles is the 'Twike'... The two rear wheels with the passengers sitting side by side give stability."
Basic w-des-020
What is the SAE J227a driving schedule?
The SAE J227a is an old (1970s) driving cycle developed specifically for EVs. It has four variants (A–D) with different speeds. Each cycle is short, consisting of acceleration, constant velocity, coast, braking and a stationary phase. SAE J227a-C is most often used for electric scooters and city EVs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.1 Driving Cycles · Page: 217
"A fairly old standard, which was developed specifically for electric vehicles in the 1970s, is the SAE J227a driving schedule. This has four versions, with different speeds."
Basic w-des-021
What is the ECE-47 cycle used for?
The European ECE-47 cycle is used for emission testing of mopeds and motorcycles with engines under 50 cc. It is also widely used to simulate the range of electric scooters. Unlike fixed-speed cycles, ECE-47 runs the vehicle at wide-open throttle for 50 seconds before settling to 20 kph.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.1 Driving Cycles · Page: 217
"the European ECE-47 cycle, which is used for the emission testing of mopeds and motorcycles with engine capacity less than 50 cm3. It is also widely used for the range simulation of electric scooters."
Basic w-des-022
How is EV range determined in a battery simulation?
At each 1-second step, the simulation finds tractive effort needed, computes motor power, applies motor efficiency, adds accessory load, then updates the battery's state of charge using its current and the Peukert correction. The process repeats through driving cycles until the battery hits 80% depth of discharge.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.2.1 Principles of Battery Electric Vehicle Modelling · Page: 219
"the energy required to move the vehicle for each second of the driving cycle is calculated, and the effects of this energy drain are calculated. The process is repeated until the battery is flat."
Basic w-des-023
How does cold weather affect EV range?
Cold weather raises battery internal resistance, increases the Peukert coefficient slightly and lowers cell voltage. In a GM EV1 simulation, switching from clement daytime to cold-and-dark conditions drops range from over 90 miles to about 70 — matching the manufacturer's '50–90 miles, depending on conditions'.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.2.3 Using MATLAB® or Excel to Simulate an Electric Vehicle · Page: 224
"We can also simulate colder weather by increasing the internal resistance by 25% or so, raising the Peukert coefficient and reducing the battery voltage very slightly... the range, usually given when 80% discharge is reached, drops from a little over 90 miles to about 70 miles."
Basic w-des-024
Does regenerative braking help a scooter much?
On a small electric scooter, the textbook simulation shows that adding 50% motor braking only extends range from 48.8 km to about 51 km — barely 4%. So in a light vehicle the benefit of regenerative braking is small, though it is much greater for heavy or aerodynamic cars.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.2.3 Using MATLAB® or Excel to Simulate an Electric Vehicle · Page: 224
"With no regenerative braking at all, the range is 48.82 km. Fifty per cent is probably the highest practical possible motor braking, and this extends the range less than 2 km, or 4%."
Basic w-des-025
Why is a fuel-cell vehicle simpler to simulate than a battery EV?
A fuel-cell vehicle has no regenerative braking to integrate, no Peukert current corrections, and no need to track battery state of charge. Fuel cell efficiency is essentially constant at all powers. So the simulation just tracks hydrogen used per second from the power demand.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.5 Range Modelling of Fuel Cell Vehicles · Page: 229
"this simulation is a great deal easier than with batteries because: there is no regenerative braking to incorporate; there are no currents to calculate; there is no Peukert correction of the current to be done."
Basic w-des-026
What is a hybrid vehicle's controller responsible for?
A hybrid controller monitors all power flows and battery state of charge, deciding moment by moment how much power should come from the engine, battery and electric motor. The controller's logic isn't fully determined by simple equations — it depends on operating conditions, history and need to equalise charge.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.6 Range Modelling of Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 230
"Hybrid electric vehicles involve a controller, which monitors the various power in the system and the state of charge of the battery, and makes decisions about the power to be drawn from the engine, battery, and so on."
Basic w-des-027
What is ADVISOR?
ADVISOR (Wipke et al., 1999) is one of the best-known EV simulation programs. It is MATLAB-based and supports the modelling of hybrid electric vehicles, including their complex controller logic. The textbook recommends using Simulink rather than plain MATLAB for serious hybrid simulation.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.6 Range Modelling of Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 230
"Among the most well known of these is ADVISOR (Wipke et al., 1999), which is MATLAB® based."
Basic w-des-028
Why is the EV1 range better on SFUDS than at constant 120 kph?
Constant 120 kph asks the EV1 to fight maximum aerodynamic drag continuously, giving a range under 80 km. SFUDS spends time stopping and starting at speeds up to 60 kph — much lower drag — and the EV1 simulation shows over 140 km of range in good conditions.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 234
"If the MATLAB file used in Section 8.4 for the range modelling of the GM EV1... are adapted for a constant speed of 120 kph, it will be found that the predicted range is less than 80 km. However, when driving the SFUDS cycle... the range could be over 140 km"
Basic w-des-029
Why are wing mirrors and aerials worth redesigning in an EV?
Wing mirrors and antennas stick out of the body, creating turbulence and drag. Replacing them with electronic video systems and internal antennas — fully enclosed within the body's aerodynamic envelope — reduces drag. The smaller battery this enables can be cheaper than the added cost of cameras and electronics.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 235
"Aerials do not need to be external to the car body and wing mirrors can be replaced by electronic video systems that can be contained within the aerodynamic envelope of the car."
Basic w-des-030
Are differentials a good idea in EVs?
A differential is well-tested, reliable, mass-produced engineering, but it loses power and adds weight. EVs can sometimes eliminate the differential by using one motor per wheel with an electronic controller balancing the torques — at the cost of more complex electronics and (usually) higher per-kW motor cost.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.4 Transmission Efficiency · Page: 239
"The differential can be eliminated by connecting a motor to each wheel via a single ratio gearbox or even a toothed belt drive."
Indirect w-des-031
Why are aerodynamics more critical in EVs than in petrol cars?
In an IC car, slightly more drag just means burning a little more fuel — cheap. In an EV, extra drag means bigger or more batteries, which are heavy and expensive. So every reduction in Cd directly reduces battery cost or extends range, making aerodynamic refinement much more valuable.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.1 Body/Chassis Requirements · Page: 246
"extra weight is not so important with an IC vehicle... The same is true for aerodynamic drag... Savings in weight as well as increases in efficiency contribute directly to the size of the batteries and these are both heavy and expensive."
Indirect w-des-032
Why is in-wheel motoring tricky?
An in-wheel motor must run slowly (wheel speeds are 2–4× lower than typical motor speeds), which means a heavier motor. The added unsprung mass at each wheel also hurts handling. In-wheel motors save space and give 100% transmission efficiency, but cost more per kilowatt than centrally mounted motors.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.4 Transmission Efficiency · Page: 239
"most electric motors typically run at two to four times faster than the vehicle's wheels, and designing a motor to work slowly results in a large heavy motor."
Indirect w-des-033
Why does an EV with the same Cd struggle more at high speed than at low speed?
Aerodynamic drag rises with the square of speed, and the power to overcome it rises with the cube. A 100 km range at 160 kph requires roughly 400 kg of lead-acid battery just to fight drag, even with a Cd of 0.19. So EVs are ill-suited to sustained high-speed driving.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 234
"Even a well designed car, with a Cd of 0.19, still needs about 400 kg of lead acid batteries just to overcome wind resistance to travel for 100 km when going at 160 kph."
Indirect w-des-034
Why do golf buggies not need streamlining?
Golf buggies and similar very low-speed vehicles barely encounter aerodynamic drag — even at 30 kph it's tiny. The buggy's rolling resistance on grass dominates. So designing a teardrop body is wasted effort. On a saloon car driven at motorway speeds, by contrast, drag is huge and streamlining matters enormously.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.2 Body/Chassis Aerodynamic Shape · Page: 236
"On very low-speed vehicles (<30 kph), such as golf buggies, where tranquillity and pure air are more important than rushing around at speed, the aerodynamic shape of the vehicle is almost irrelevant."
Indirect w-des-035
Why must hill climbing be folded into EV range tests?
Power needed to climb a 10° hill is much larger than for flat cruising — for a 1500 kg car, about 12× the flat power. Real journeys include hills, so simulations without them overstate EV range. The textbook suggests adding gradients to driving cycles for any specific route being modelled.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.5 Consideration of Vehicle Mass · Page: 242
"Considerable power is required for hill climbing, and such terrain will restrict the range of electric vehicles relying solely on rechargeable batteries. When designing electric vehicles the effect of hills must be taken into account"
Indirect w-des-036
Why is fuel cell efficiency roughly constant at all powers?
At low currents the fuel cell's voltage (and so efficiency) rises. But at low currents the auxiliary balance-of-plant — pumps, compressors, controllers — also takes a larger share of net output. The two effects roughly cancel, giving a fuel cell system net efficiency that is fairly flat across power levels.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.5 Range Modelling of Fuel Cell Vehicles · Page: 228
"in practice, the efficiency of a fuel cell is, to quite a good approximation, more or less constant at all powers."
Indirect w-des-037
Why does a heavier car gain more from regenerative braking?
Heavier cars store more kinetic energy at any given speed (KE = ½ m v²). So they have more to recover when braking. Light vehicles never have much kinetic energy in the first place, so even recovering 40% of it yields little battery payback compared with the heavier case.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.5 Consideration of Vehicle Mass · Page: 243
"In light vehicles the losses associated with continually creating and then losing kinetic energy are much less, and the benefits of regenerative braking are similarly reduced."
Indirect w-des-038
Why is the GM EV1 motor so large compared to its average power use?
On the SFUDS urban cycle, the EV1 uses only about 12 kW average. But the motor is rated at 100 kW. The extra headroom is needed for hard acceleration and especially for climbing steep hills with a heavy car — peak demands that can be ten times the average usage.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.5 Consideration of Vehicle Mass · Page: 242
"we see why the GM EV1 electric car needs a motor of power about 100 kW. In the SFUDS simulation we noted that the maximum power needed was only 12 kW... Taking heavy vehicles up hills requires high power."
Indirect w-des-039
Why are vans harder to streamline than cars?
Vans need maximum interior volume to carry cargo, which favours boxy shapes. That conflicts with the slim, tapered teardrop shape that minimises drag. Designers use under-body covers, flat wheels and rounded corners to reduce Cd, but vans never reach the low values that purpose-built EV cars can.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.2 Body/Chassis Aerodynamic Shape · Page: 236
"there is a conflict between an aerodynamic shape and low frontal area and the need for maximising interior space, particularly for load carrying."
Indirect w-des-040
Why are low-rolling-resistance tyres especially valuable for low-speed EVs?
On slow vehicles like mobility scooters or golf carts, air drag is tiny and rolling resistance dominates. Cutting μ_rr from 0.015 to 0.005 cuts that loss to one-third. So battery mass can be tripled in range, or cut by two-thirds for the same range — a substantial saving.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.3 Consideration of Rolling Resistance · Page: 238
"A reduction of rolling resistance to one-third is a substantial benefit, particularly for low-speed vehicles such as buggies for the disabled."
Medium w-des-041
How does battery mass for aerodynamic drag scale with speed?
Battery mass to fight aerodynamic drag scales as Cd·A·v² × distance ÷ specific energy ÷ efficiency. So at 160 kph it takes roughly 4× the battery mass it would at 80 kph for the same range. That makes high-speed EVs particularly battery-hungry compared with low-speed city EVs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.1 Aerodynamics and Energy · Page: 234
"The battery mass mb (kg) of a battery with specific energy SE (W h kg−1) required to overcome the aerodynamic drag at a velocity v (m s−1) over a distance d(m)"
Medium w-des-042
How does the EV1 fuel-cell conversion change vehicle mass?
Removing 594 kg of lead-acid batteries and adding 8.5 kg of hydrogen plus 51.5 kg of tank and 250 kg of fuel cell system gives a total vehicle mass of about 1066 kg, down from the original 1350-plus-kg EV1. Lighter total mass means less rolling and acceleration energy.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.5 Range Modelling of Fuel Cell Vehicles · Page: 229
"Total mass of vehicle is now (1350 — 594) + 8.5 + 51.5 + 250 = 1066 kg."
Medium w-des-043
How does the textbook compute the fuel-cell target operating voltage?
If the fuel-cell stack averages 0.65 V per cell but the system has 38% overall efficiency referred to LHV, then the equivalent 'system' voltage is about 0.475 V per cell. The 0.175 V gap represents power consumed by the balance-of-plant — pumps, compressors and controllers.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.5 Range Modelling of Fuel Cell Vehicles · Page: 228
"the fuel cell will probably, in fact, be running at about 0.65 V, but the difference between this and 0.475 represents the energy used by the balance of plant."
Medium w-des-044
What's the loss model used for motor efficiency in range simulation?
The model uses the same four-term loss formula as Chapter 7: copper losses k_c·T², iron losses k_i·ω, windage k_w·ω³, plus constant losses C. Plug torque T and angular speed ω at each second of the cycle into this formula to get current motor efficiency for that second.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.2.2 Modelling Equations · Page: 220
"where kc is the copper losses coefficient, k i is the iron losses coefficient, kw is the windage loss coefficient and C represents the constant losses that apply at any speed."
Medium w-des-045
Why is a low centre of gravity a design goal in EVs?
Distributing heavy battery cells along the bottom of the vehicle lowers its centre of gravity, improving stability and handling. EVs have great flexibility here because batteries can be split and packed wherever convenient. This gives EVs a structural advantage IC cars don't easily match.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.2 Body/Chassis Layout · Page: 246
"Batteries can also be arranged to ensure that the vehicle is perfectly balanced around the centre of gravity, giving good handling characteristics."
Medium w-des-046
How can you simulate constant-velocity range in MATLAB simply?
Use linspace(v, v, N) to create an array of N identical velocity values v. Drop this into the range-simulation in place of a real cycle. It's not elegant, but lets the same code base run constant-velocity tests using the cycle infrastructure already built. Useful for quick what-if checks.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.3 Constant Velocity Range Modelling · Page: 225
"linspace(12.5, 12.5, 100); This creates an array of 100 values, all equal to 12.5, which corresponds to 45 kph."
Medium w-des-047
Why does the textbook prefer cycle-based simulation over constant velocity?
Constant-velocity tests ignore the stops, starts and varying speeds that dominate real driving. Driving cycles reflect actual usage patterns, including the time spent in low-efficiency regions of the motor map. So cycle results are more useful for range claims, even though they take more computation.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.3 Constant Velocity Range Modelling · Page: 225
"Constant velocity simulations are clearly very unrealistic, and so are of limited use."
Medium w-des-048
Why are computational fluid dynamics (CFD) and wind tunnels used for EVs?
Real Cd values depend on every surface curve, gap and protrusion. CFD packages let designers predict drag from a 3D model before any prototype is built. Wind tunnels confirm CFD results on full-size cars, sometimes with rolling roads to mimic moving ground. Both are essential to optimise EV aerodynamics.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.2.2 Body/Chassis Aerodynamic Shape · Page: 238
"Modern computational fluid dynamics (CFD) packages will accurately predict aerodynamic characteristics of vehicles. Most motor manufacturers use wind tunnels"
Medium w-des-049
Why does the EV's motor often spend time near its sweet spot?
Plotting motor operating points (torque vs angular speed) over a typical driving cycle often shows they cluster near 120 rad/s and 10 N·m — exactly the efficiency map's peak. So motor sizing has been well matched to the cycle, which helps explain why simulated range often beats the spec sheet.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.4 Other uses of Simulations · Page: 227
"the motor is frequently operating in the region of about 120 rad s−1 speed, and low ( 10 N m) torque. From Figure 7.7 we can see that this is precisely the area where the motor is most efficient."
Medium w-des-050
Why must hybrid simulation often be written in C, not just MATLAB?
A hybrid's energy-management controller is usually written in C for the real vehicle. Wrapping the simulation in the same language lets the actual controller code be tested directly in simulation. This reduces bugs and ensures the simulator and the production controller behave identically.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 8. Electric Vehicle Modelling · Section: 8.4.6 Range Modelling of Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 230
"The program for the energy controller in a hybrid system, which is a subsystem of vital importance, will often be written in a high-level language such as C. It makes sense to incorporate the simulator in the same language"
Basic w-env-001
What is well-to-wheels analysis?
Well-to-wheels analysis considers pollution and energy use across the whole chain that powers a vehicle — from extraction of the fuel or generation of the electricity at source, through any conversions, all the way to the energy actually delivered at the wheels. It avoids tunnel-vision focus on just the tailpipe.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.1 Introduction · Page: 266
"the so-called 'well-to-wheels' analysis, where the pollution of all parts of the energy cycle in the use of a vehicle is considered, not just the vehicle itself."
Basic w-env-002
Why must 'efficiency' be carefully defined when comparing vehicles?
Efficiency only makes sense when comparing like with like. The same vehicle has different efficiency numbers depending on whether you count road energy versus electricity, road energy versus chemical fuel, or road energy versus energy at the original source — each is valid but tells a different story.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.1 Introduction · Page: 264
"The term efficiency is only useful when it is used for comparing like with like."
Basic w-env-003
What is the typical tank-to-wheels efficiency of an EV?
An EV's efficiency from electricity supplied to the battery through to energy delivered at the wheels is around 80%. By comparison, an IC vehicle from chemical fuel to wheels achieves only about 20%. So an EV uses far less stored energy for the same distance.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.1 Introduction · Page: 264
"the efficiency of the EV (road energy/electrical energy supplied to the vehicle) may well be around 80%. The efficiency of the IC engine vehicle (road energy/petrol energy) may well be 20%."
Basic w-env-004
How efficient is a typical coal power station?
An older coal power station has an efficiency around 25% (electricity generated divided by energy in the coal burnt). The current average is 28%. Modern power stations can reach 45%, and combined-cycle plants can achieve as high as 60%, which makes a big difference to well-to-wheels figures.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.1 Introduction · Page: 264
"The efficiency of older coal power stations is around 25%... modern power stations can achieve efficiencies of 45%. Combined cycle power stations can achieve efficiencies as high as 60%"
Basic w-env-005
How do you multiply efficiencies in a chain?
If a power station is 30% efficient, the lines that carry its power are 90% efficient, and the motor at the end is 80% efficient, the overall well-to-wheels efficiency is 0.30 × 0.90 × 0.80 = 0.216, or 21.6%. Each step multiplies the loss.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.2 Definition of Efficiency · Page: 264
"the overall efficiency of the combined system (shaft energy from the motor/chemical energy in the fuel) will be 0.3 × 0.9 × 0.8 = 0.216 or 21.6%."
Basic w-env-006
How much CO₂ does a 100-mile EV journey cause in the UK?
A Nissan Leaf needs about 26.7 kWh of mains electricity (after 90% charging efficiency) to drive 100 miles. With UK grid CO₂ emissions of roughly 0.44 kg per kWh at the time of the book, that gives around 11.75 kg of CO₂ for the trip.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 264
"the CO2 released in the UK will be 26.7 × 0.44 11.75 kg."
Basic w-env-007
How much CO₂ does the same 100-mile EV journey cause in France?
France's grid is largely nuclear and hydro, with CO₂ emissions around 0.07 kg per kWh — far below the UK's 0.44. The same 100-mile EV journey requiring 26.7 kWh of grid electricity therefore releases only about 1.87 kg of CO₂ in France.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 264
"In France where the CO2 release is currently 0.07 kg kWh−1 the amount of CO2 released would be 1.87 kg."
Basic w-env-008
How much CO₂ does a 100-mile diesel journey produce?
A diesel car with 40 mpg fuel economy uses 11.25 litres of diesel to cover 100 miles. Each litre of diesel releases about 2.672 kg of CO₂ when burnt, so the total CO₂ release for the trip is roughly 30 kg, more than double a UK-charged EV.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 264
"A diesel car with an economy of 40 mpg or 8.9 l per mile travelling 100 miles will use 2.5 gal or 11.25 l of diesel... it will release 11.25 X 2.672 = 30 kg CO2."
Basic w-env-009
How does a fuel-cell car compare to a diesel for CO₂?
A Honda FCX fuel-cell car using hydrogen reformed from natural gas releases about 16.3 kg of CO₂ over 100 miles — roughly 54% of the diesel car's 30 kg. Honda claims around 60%. The fuel cell's advantage depends on how the hydrogen was made.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 264
"The fuel cell car releases 54% of the CO2 compared with the CO2 release from the diesel engined car."
Basic w-env-010
Why does the source of hydrogen matter so much?
Hydrogen reformed from natural gas emits about 16.3 kg of CO₂ per 100 miles of FCX driving. Producing the same hydrogen by electrolysing water with UK grid power emits about 48.1 kg — even worse than diesel. Only renewable or nuclear electricity makes hydrogen truly low-carbon.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 265
"A hydrogen fuel cell car using hydrogen electrolysed from water using mains electricity would release 48.1 kg of CO2 in the UK and 6.2 kg in France."
Basic w-env-011
What are the main pollutants from IC engine vehicles?
The major IC engine pollutants are carbon dioxide, carbon monoxide, nitrous oxides (NOx), volatile organic compounds (VOCs), particulate matter (PM) and sulfur dioxide. All cause documented health problems and contribute to urban air pollution. CO₂ is the main driver of climate change.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"The major IC engine pollutants include carbon dioxide, carbon monoxide, nitrous oxides, volatile organic compounds (VOCs), particulate matter (PM) and sulfur dioxide."
Basic w-env-012
How does carbon monoxide harm health?
Carbon monoxide inhibits the blood's ability to carry oxygen, which is particularly dangerous to smokers and people with heart disease. It can also cause permanent damage to the nervous system. So even sub-lethal exposure on busy streets is a real health concern.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"Carbon monoxide inhibits the ability of the blood to carry oxygen, and in particular is dangerous to smokers and people with heart disease. It can also cause permanent damage to the nervous system."
Basic w-env-013
What harms do nitrous oxides (NOx) cause?
NOx exacerbate asthma, affect the lungs and make children and the elderly more vulnerable to respiratory infection. In sunlight with VOCs, NOx produce ground-level ozone, which irritates eyes and damages lungs. NOx also help form acid rain, which kills plants and fish.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"Nitrous oxides (NOx) exacerbate asthma, affect the lungs and increase the susceptibility of young children and the elderly to respiratory infections."
Basic w-env-014
Why is particulate matter (PM) a serious health risk?
PM causes lung problems, worsens cardiovascular disease, damages lung tissue and can cause cancer. Ultra-fine PM gets past the upper airway, deep into lung tissue and the bloodstream. Above 5 μg/m³ it presents a real cancer risk and harms the reproductive and endocrine systems.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"PM causes lung problems including shortage of breath, worsens cardiovascular disease, damages lung tissue and causes cancer."
Basic w-env-015
What is the greenhouse effect of CO₂?
The sun's short-wave radiation is absorbed by the earth and re-emitted as longer-wavelength heat radiation. CO₂ and other greenhouse gases absorb that heat and re-radiate it back down, warming the earth's surface. Atmospheric CO₂ has risen by about 25% over the past 100 years.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"some of the short-wave radiation from the sun is absorbed by the earth and then re-emitted at a longer wavelength. This is absorbed by carbon dioxide and other gases and then re-emitted, the downward radiation warming the surface of the earth."
Basic w-env-016
What share of UK energy use comes from road transport?
Road transport accounts for about 25% of total UK energy use, and therefore about 25% of the country's greenhouse-gas emissions. Other western countries show similar figures. So making transport more efficient — including the shift to EVs — can make a major dent in national CO₂ output.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.3 Vehicle Pollution in Context · Page: 270
"Road transport represents about 25% of the energy used, and thus about 25% of the greenhouse gas production."
Basic w-env-017
Why do petrol cars get less efficient in city traffic?
IC engines work poorly at low loads. In slow traffic, fuel consumption rises sharply per kilometre. EVs are different — motor efficiency dips a bit at low speeds, but battery efficiency rises, giving an overall fairly steady efficiency across all speeds. So EVs are much better suited to congested cities.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"One significant problem with IC engine vehicles in slow traffic is that fuel consumption rises very dramatically as vehicles crawl along at slow speeds and pollution gets considerably worse"
Basic w-env-018
What's the typical city traffic speed in London or Tokyo?
In cities such as London and Tokyo, the average traffic speed is normally less than 15 kph, and in rush hour it is considerably less. At these speeds, IC engine cars waste enormous amounts of fuel and emit much pollution, while EVs maintain a fairly steady, efficient operation.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"In cities such as London and Tokyo the average speeds are normally less than 15 kph and in the rush hour are considerably less."
Basic w-env-019
What are the simplest ways to clean up city traffic?
The simplest way to remove emissions from town and city streets is to enforce zero-emission vehicles by legislation. Even hybrid vehicles running on electricity in city zones (but petrol elsewhere) would massively cut the noise, particulates and NOx people breathe in dense urban environments.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"The simplest way of eliminating these problems from town and city streets is to enforce zero-emission vehicles into the towns and cities by legislation or other means."
Basic w-env-020
Are IC engines forever doomed to be polluting?
No. IC engines can run on sustainable fuels like Brazil's sugar-cane ethanol, or even on pure hydrogen with essentially zero exhaust pollutants. But it has turned out to be easier and more efficient to use fuel cells, and electricity for batteries can come from renewables — so EVs are winning.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.1 Introduction · Page: 266
"IC engines could also be made to run with virtually zero emissions, burning hydrogen for example, and thus giving an exhaust gas of (almost) just water and air."
Basic w-env-021
What is a heat pump used for in an EV?
A heat pump moves heat from one place to another, providing more heat energy out than electrical energy in. For every 1 kW of electricity, a heat pump typically delivers 3 kW of heat. The GM EV1 used a reversible heat pump for both cabin heating and cooling.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 256
"Heat pumps have a coefficient of performance which is typically three or more; in other words, for every kilowatt of electrical input, 3 kW or more of heat will be pumped into, or taken from, the car."
Basic w-env-022
Why is heating an EV trickier than heating a petrol car?
In an IC car, plenty of waste heat from the engine warms the cabin almost for free. In a pure battery EV, the motor and electronics produce little waste heat, so any cabin warmth must come from the battery — which directly reduces driving range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 256
"With IC engine vehicles, copious waste heat will quickly warm the vehicle... but with battery-powered electric vehicles there is little waste heat, and where heating is required this must be supplied from a suitable source."
Basic w-env-023
Why is electric power steering (EPS) better for an EV?
Hydraulic power steering is driven mechanically by the engine, placing a continuous load on it even when no steering assist is needed. EPS draws electric power only when assisting the driver, improving fuel/energy efficiency. It is also simpler and more reliable than a hydraulic system.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.4 Power Steering · Page: 259
"A typical hydraulic power steering system is continually placing a small load on the engine, even when no steering assist is required. Because the EPS system only needs to draw electric power when steering assist is required, no extra energy is needed when cruising"
Basic w-env-024
Why do EVs sometimes use a stick controller instead of pedals?
A four-quadrant motor controller handles both acceleration and regenerative braking, so it is natural to use a single lever to control both. Pushing the stick forward accelerates the vehicle; pulling it back applies regenerative braking. Mechanical brakes are added only at the extreme of travel for safety.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.3 Design of the Controls · Page: 258
"Because one electronic controller is used for both acceleration and normal braking it is easier to use one lever to accelerate and brake the vehicle."
Basic w-env-025
What can satellite navigation do for an EV beyond directions?
In an EV, satellite navigation can do more than route-find. It can keep journeys minimal, automatically direct drivers to nearby charging points, and enforce speed limits via the electronic motor controller. This improves road safety while maximising vehicle range — features that are easier in EVs than petrol cars.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.3 Design of the Controls · Page: 258
"With electric vehicles, where the aim is always to save energy, onboard computers coupled to satellite navigation systems can be even more advantageous."
Basic w-env-026
Why are low-rolling-resistance tyres popular on EVs?
Low-rolling-resistance tyres like the Michelin Proxima RR used on the GM EV1 reduce drag without compromising handling or safety. They are usually inflated to about 3.5 bar, giving a slightly firmer ride. The Proxima RR also has self-sealing tread, removing the need for a spare wheel.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.5 Choice of Tyres · Page: 260
"Low-rollingresistance tyres such as the Michelin Proxima RR as used on the GM EV1 have a very low rolling resistance and it is worthwhile to use low-energy tyres such as these."
Basic w-env-027
Why are luggage racks and external aerials bad for EV efficiency?
Roof racks, external aerials and wing mirrors all stick out into the airflow, increasing the drag coefficient and cutting EV range. Replacing wing mirrors with cameras, putting aerials inside rear windows and discouraging roof racks are all ways to keep the body's slippery aerodynamic profile intact.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.6 Wing Mirrors, Aerials and Luggage Racks · Page: 260
"It is obviously illogical to spend endless time and effort perfecting the aerodynamics of vehicles and then to stick wing mirrors, aerials and luggage racks out of their sides. This immediately increases the aerodynamic drag coefficient"
Basic w-env-028
What's the role of selective-coated glass in EV thermal design?
Most cars act like greenhouses — sunlight enters through the glass and heats the interior. Glass coated with a selective layer reflects much of the solar radiation, sharply reducing internal heat build-up. That cuts the load on the air-conditioning system and so improves EV range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 257
"This problem can be considerably reduced by using glass covered with a selective coating, which considerably cuts down the amount of solar radiation that enters the vehicle."
Basic w-env-029
Why is pre-heating the cabin while charging a smart idea?
Heating or cooling the cabin half an hour before driving — using a remote control or timer while still plugged in — means the electricity for cabin comfort comes from the grid, not from the battery. The driver finds the cabin pre-conditioned without sacrificing range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 257
"It is also worth cooling or heating the vehicle half an hour or so before it is used – by using either a remote control or a time switch. Where a heat pump system is used the electricity would come from the charge point."
Basic w-env-030
What does an onboard charger do?
An onboard charger is a battery-charging unit carried inside the vehicle. Most EVs have one, so the car can be plugged into a regular wall socket anywhere when fixed external chargers aren't available. Onboard chargers usually charge more slowly than dedicated high-power roadside chargers.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.7 Electric Vehicle Recharging and Refuelling Systems · Page: 260
"The majority of electric vehicles carry an onboard charger, though this will usually recharge the batteries at a rather slower speed than is possible with more sophisticated offboard systems."
Indirect w-env-031
Why does an EV charged from solar power give a misleading 'efficiency' number?
A solar power station is only ~10% efficient end-to-end, so a solar-charged EV has a well-to-wheels efficiency of just 2.5%, ten times worse than a petrol car. But it still emits zero CO₂. The headline efficiency number on its own is misleading without considering carbon and cost.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.1 Introduction · Page: 264
"Typical efficiencies of the solar power station (road energy/solar energy) will be around 10%. This means that the overall efficiency of the EV supplied with solar electricity is 2.5% (road energy/energy at source) compared with the efficiency of the IC vehicle... which will still be 25%."
Indirect w-env-032
Why isn't the fuel-cell vehicle always greener than the EV?
If hydrogen comes from natural gas reforming, an FCX emits about 16 kg CO₂ per 100 miles — similar to a UK-charged battery EV. If hydrogen comes from electrolysis using UK grid power, an FCX emits 48 kg, worse than diesel. Only clean-electricity hydrogen makes fuel cells a real winner.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 266
"the hydrogen fuel cell is not as carbon friendly as the battery EV when using mains electricity to obtain hydrogen from electrolysing water."
Indirect w-env-033
Why does the EV's CO₂ advantage grow as the grid cleans up?
An EV's per-mile CO₂ scales with grid CO₂ per kWh. Today's UK average is about 0.44 kg/kWh; France's is 0.07. As grids add more nuclear and renewables, EV CO₂ falls — while a diesel car's emissions stay fixed. So EVs' lead over diesel widens every year.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 266
"As the amount of CO2 released per kilowatt-hour of electricity decreases when more carbon neutral electricity generation is used, the battery EV will show a marked advantage over the fuel cell vehicle."
Indirect w-env-034
Why might using a small fuel-burning heater in an EV be a bad idea?
Fuel-burning cabin heaters were tried on US Postal Service EVs. They proved hard to control — drivers ended up opening doors to dump excess heat — and the vehicles consumed nearly as much fuel as the diesel vans they replaced. The EVs then no longer counted as zero-emission.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 256
"Such heaters have been used in battery vehicles used by the US postal service. It was said that such heaters could only be controlled by opening the doors and letting the heat out – and the result was that the vehicles ended up using almost as much fuel as the diesel-powered vehicles they replaced!"
Indirect w-env-035
How does heat storage in wax help an EV?
Heated wax stores energy via latent heat of fusion at a higher specific energy than a battery. Charged from the grid when the car is plugged in, it then warms the cabin on a cold morning without draining the battery. The car is warm by the time the driver gets in.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 256
"More modern night storage heaters use the latent heat of fusion of materials such as wax, which gives an even higher specific energy than that obtained by heating water."
Indirect w-env-036
Why can't sustainable IC engines simply replace EVs?
IC engines can run cleanly on hydrogen or sugarcane ethanol, but they still produce tail-pipe emissions (NOx) and noise locally. They are also far less efficient than electric motors. And renewable electricity scales more easily than producing huge volumes of sustainable liquid fuels, so EVs win out long-term.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.1 Introduction · Page: 266
"Perhaps fortunately, it is becoming easier and more efficient to use fuel cells, and electricity for charging batteries can be derived from renewable sources."
Indirect w-env-037
How does carbon fibre help cut EV battery cost?
Carbon fibre has by far the best strength-to-mass and rigidity-to-mass ratio of common chassis materials — nearly six times better than aluminium or steel. A carbon-fibre Formula One chassis can mass just 35 kg. Lighter chassis means smaller, cheaper battery for the same range, which can offset carbon's higher material cost.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.3 Body/Chassis Strength, Rigidity and Crash Resistance · Page: 249
"It can be seen in the table that carbon fibre has the best strength to mass (σ/ρ) as well as the best rigidity to mass (E/ρ), nearly six times the other materials"
Indirect w-env-038
Why are crumple zones still essential in an EV body?
In a crash, a body absorbs energy via plastic deformation. A well-designed crumple zone forces this to happen progressively, spreading deceleration forces over more time and protecting occupants. Both metals and composites absorb impact energy, though metals' crush behaviour is easier to predict with modern finite-element software.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 9. Design Considerations · Section: 9.6.3 Body/Chassis Strength, Rigidity and Crash Resistance · Page: 249
"If the car is designed so that the energy is absorbed in a controlled manner the forces on the driver and passengers can be minimised. It is therefore normal to design cars with energy-absorbing crumple zones."
Indirect w-env-039
Why is glass area both helpful and harmful in EVs?
Large glazed areas give passengers good visibility but also turn the cabin into an effective passive solar heater on hot, sunny days — quickly raising temperatures past safe limits. Selective coatings on glass can reflect much of the solar radiation, cutting cooling demand and improving range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 257
"most cars are highly efficient passive solar heating systems – most would make good greenhouses. There is a large glazed area allowing sunlight into the vehicle where it is absorbed by the interior as heat."
Indirect w-env-040
Why is using the air-conditioner often greener than opening windows?
Opening windows at speed disrupts the body's airflow and substantially increases aerodynamic drag, shortening range. Keeping windows closed and running the air-conditioner can use less battery overall, especially on long high-speed drives. So full air-conditioning is recommended for EVs intended to do long distance.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 257
"this will affect the aerodynamics, considerably increasing the drag and shortening the range. It would make better sense to install air-conditioning in all electric vehicles where long range is required."
Medium w-env-041
Why is 'fossil-fuel-to-wheels' efficiency about the same for petrol and EV (with coal grid)?
A petrol IC car turns ~20% of its fuel's chemical energy into wheel energy. An EV with 80% tank-to-wheels efficiency, charged from a 25% coal grid, lands at 0.25 × 0.8 ≈ 20% from fossil fuel to wheels. Locally cleaner, but globally similar — unless the grid gets cleaner.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.1 Introduction · Page: 264
"Typically the efficiency of converting coal to electricity and transmitting it to end users may be around 25%. Hence the overall efficiency of the EV (road energy/energy in the fossil fuel at the power station) is the same in both cases."
Medium w-env-042
How would you compute a fuel-cell vehicle's well-to-wheels CO₂?
Start with the hydrogen consumed per 100 miles, then divide by reforming efficiency (70%) and compression efficiency (90%) to get natural-gas energy. Multiply by 0.185 kg CO₂ per kWh. For a Honda FCX using 1.67 kg of H₂, this gives 88.2 kWh and about 16.3 kg CO₂.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 264
"the energy in the natural gas from which the hydrogen was reformed will be 55.6/0.9/0.7 = 88.2 kWh. From Table 11.1 this will cause a CO2 release of 0.185 23 kg of CO2 per kilowatt-hour in the natural gas, that is 16.3 kg."
Medium w-env-043
What does a 25% rise in CO₂ over 100 years mean?
Atmospheric CO₂ has climbed about 25% in the last century, mostly from burning fossil fuels. Even small percentage rises trap a lot of extra heat globally. Effects include altered weather patterns in grain belts and melting ice caps that threaten coastal cities like London, New York and Perth.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"The atmospheric concentration of carbon dioxide has increased by about 25% over the past 100 years."
Medium w-env-044
How does an EV compare to a diesel on a full UK 100-mile journey?
Diesel: ~30 kg CO₂. UK-charged EV: ~11.75 kg. So the EV saves over 60% of the diesel's emissions even on the UK's relatively dirty grid. The same EV in France emits about 1.9 kg — a 94% saving against diesel. So grid mix matters enormously.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 265
"A battery car (e.g. the Nissan Leaf) charged in the UK will cause 14.5 kg of CO2 to be released for a journey of 100 miles or 160 km."
Medium w-env-045
How does PM concentration above 5 μg/m³ matter?
Above about 5 μg per cubic metre of air, particulate matter — especially ultra-fine PM — presents a significant cancer risk. It also damages the reproductive and endocrine systems. Many PMs are confirmed mutagens. So city air pollution from diesel engines isn't just unpleasant; it is genuinely toxic.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"At concentrations above 5 μg m −3 PM presents a significant cancer risk."
Medium w-env-046
How does latent heat let water store more energy than batteries?
Storing 1 kg of insulated water heated 70°C above ambient holds 293 kJ (~81 Wh) — better than lead-acid (35 Wh/kg) or NiCad batteries. The ice form, melting from 0°C to 15°C, holds 110 Wh/kg via latent heat of fusion plus warming. Useful for cabin heating or cooling.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 10. Design of Ancillary Systems · Section: 10.2 Heating and Cooling Systems · Page: 256
"1 kg of water housed in a suitable insulated container and raised through 70 ◦C above ambient contains 293 kJ or 81 Wh of heat. At 81 Wh kg−1 this is a considerably better specific energy than both lead acid and NiCAD batteries."
Medium w-env-047
Why is 3-nitrobenzanthrone a concerning find in diesel exhaust?
Researchers (Arlt, 2005) have isolated 3-nitrobenzanthrone in diesel exhaust. It is described as a highly potent mutagen — a compound that can damage DNA and seed cancer. Such findings underscore that diesel exhaust is far worse than just a smelly nuisance; it is genuinely hazardous to long-term human health.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.2 Vehicle Pollution – The Effects · Page: 270
"Researchers have apparently isolated a compound called 3-nitrobenzanthone which is a highly potent mutagen"
Medium w-env-048
Why does the textbook give EV charging an extra 90% efficiency factor?
Charging is never 100% efficient: rectification, conversion and battery acceptance all lose some energy. The book assumes about 90% charging efficiency for the Nissan Leaf calculation, meaning a 24 kWh battery actually needs about 26.7 kWh from the wall to fill it.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 11. Efficiencies and Carbon Release Comparison · Section: 11.3 Carbon Dioxide Emission and Chemical Energy in Fuel · Page: 264
"Allowing an efficiency of 90% for charging efficiency (electrical energy stored/electrical energy supplied). The vehicle will require 26.7 kWh of electricity."
Medium w-env-049
Why might legislation be the key driver of EV adoption?
Cleaner-but-pricier transport happens only when society makes individual people choose it. Laws and regulations can force the change — banning the dirtiest vehicles, taxing fossil fuels, requiring zero-emission zones. The textbook calls this 'collective coercion to be good' and sees it as central to scaling up EVs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.4 The Role of Regulations and Lawmakers · Page: 270
"the power of law and regulation is important in making individual people make choices – in favour of less pollution at a higher price. One of the major roles of society is a 'collective coercion to be good'"
Medium w-env-050
How does electric bicycle availability help the environment beyond replacing cars?
If electric bicycles work well and are widely available, some drivers may abandon private cars altogether. That reduces emissions even more than replacing a petrol car with an EV — because a bicycle, electric or not, uses far less energy per kilometre than any car of any kind.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.1 Introduction · Page: 266
"if electric bicycles worked well, and were widely available, could this persuade some people to abandon their private cars, which can generate considerable pollution whatever their power source?"
Basic w-fut-001
What is CARB?
CARB stands for the California Air Resources Board. It is a Californian government body that sets vehicle emission rules. CARB pushed the use of catalytic converters on petrol-engine exhausts and later forced car makers to develop zero-emission electric vehicles for the California market.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.4 The Effect of Electrified Transport · Page: 271
"the actions of California through its Air Resources Board (CARB). This organisation was a major promoter of the now almost universal catalytic converter on IC engine exhausts."
Basic w-fut-002
What did California's CARB ask car makers to do in 1998?
In the late 1980s CARB ruled that car makers selling vehicles in California had to make 2% of their 1998 sales zero-emission vehicles, rising to 5% by the year 2000. The California car market is huge, so this pushed makers to develop electric vehicles seriously.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.4 The Effect of Electrified Transport · Page: 271
"2% of vehicles sales in 1998, rising to 5% in 2000, would have to be zero-emission vehicles."
Basic w-fut-003
What is a Zero-Emission Vehicle (ZEV)?
A Zero-Emission Vehicle, or ZEV, is one that produces no exhaust emissions when driven, such as a battery electric vehicle. The California Air Resources Board used the ZEV idea to push car makers toward cleaner technology, even though well-to-wheel emissions also matter.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.4 The Effect of Electrified Transport · Page: 271
"would have to be zero-emission vehicles. The California vehicles market is huge, about 1 million per year, so this had massive implications"
Basic w-fut-004
Why did California change its original zero-emission vehicle targets?
The original 1998 and 2000 ZEV sales targets proved too ambitious for car makers to meet. California also realised that hybrids and well-to-wheel analysis could give cleaner overall results than a small share of pure ZEVs, so CARB rolled back deadlines and added flexibility.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.4 The Effect of Electrified Transport · Page: 272
"These revisions came in two forms. The first was a rolling back of the targets in time. The second was to make them much more complex"
Basic w-fut-005
What is the average global efficiency of coal-fired power plants?
The average global efficiency of coal-fired power plants today is about 28%. That means only 28% of the energy in the coal becomes useful electricity. The most modern plants reach roughly 45%, and upgrading old plants is one easy way to cut carbon emissions.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.2 Power Generation using Fossil Fuels · Page: 274
"The average global efficiency of coal-fired plants is currently 28% compared with 45% for the most efficient plants."
Basic w-fut-006
What is the world's most efficient coal-fired power station?
Unit 3 at the Nordjylland Power Station in Denmark is currently the world's most efficient coal-fired power station. It is rated at 400 MWe and has reached 50% efficiency, almost double that of older coal plants, by using more advanced combustion and steam technology.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.2 Power Generation using Fossil Fuels · Page: 274
"The 400 MWe Unit 3 at Nordjylland Power Station, a coal-fired power plant in Denmark, is at present the world's most efficient coal-fired power station and has achieved efficiencies of 50%."
Basic w-fut-007
What is a combined-cycle power station?
A combined-cycle power station uses two or more heat engines in tandem, so heat that would otherwise be wasted by the first engine is captured and used by the second. This lifts overall efficiency above 50%, and the very best designs have reached 60%.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.2 Power Generation using Fossil Fuels · Page: 274
"Combined cycles use two or more heat engines in tandem. Combined cycle power stations have achieved efficiencies of more than 60%"
Basic w-fut-008
What are the two main ways of turning sunlight into electricity?
The two well-established ways are photovoltaic panels, which convert sunlight straight into DC electricity, and solar thermal systems, which use sunlight to heat a fluid that drives a steam turbine. Both can supply electricity to a grid that can later charge electric vehicles.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.1 Solar Energy · Page: 275
"The two well-established ways of turning solar radiation into electricity are by photovoltaic panels, which turn solar radiation into DC electricity, and solar thermal power systems"
Basic w-fut-009
How does the amount of sunshine vary between Alaska and the Sahara?
Average sunshine on a flat surface is about 87 watts per square metre in Alaska but around 273 watts per square metre in the Sahara. So a solar panel placed in the desert collects roughly three times more energy than the same panel placed near the Arctic.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.1 Solar Energy · Page: 275
"The average sunshine radiation on a horizontal surface varies from around 87 W m−2 in Alaska to 273 W m−2 in the Sahara."
Basic w-fut-010
What efficiency do typical mass-produced solar panels reach?
Cheap, mass-produced solar photovoltaic panels turn about 10% of the sunlight that hits them into electricity. More expensive panels can reach about 20%. The cheaper, lower-efficiency type is expected to be the most widely deployed, because of its much lower cost per watt.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.1 Solar Energy · Page: 275
"Cheaper solar photovoltaic panels have an efficiency of about 10% (electrical energy generated/solar energy); expensive ones perform at 20% efficiency."
Basic w-fut-011
How might solar power help charge electric vehicles?
Solar power output peaks during the middle of the day. If EVs are scheduled to charge when solar electricity is most abundant, they soak up clean power that might otherwise be wasted. Linking solar farms in different time zones with HV DC lines can extend this benefit further.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.1 Solar Energy · Page: 276
"EVs could be charged at times of day when solar electricity is abundant. An attractive option is to use a series of solar farms distributed around the globe and connected by high-voltage, high-efficiency electric transmission lines."
Basic w-fut-012
What share of the world's electricity comes from hydroelectric power?
Hydroelectricity supplies about 6% of the world's electricity today. It is the most widely used form of renewable energy and accounts for roughly 21% of all renewable generation. Some countries depend on it heavily — for example, Canada gets about 60% of its electricity from hydro.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.3 Hydroelectricity · Page: 277
"The surprisingly high figure of 6% of world electricity generation is currently obtained from hydro power. In Britain 2% of power is obtained, compared with Canada where the figure is 60%."
Basic w-fut-013
What is the Rance Power Station?
The Rance Power Station, on the Rance estuary in France, is the best-known tidal power scheme. It dams the estuary and channels rising and falling tides through 24 axial-flow turbines. It has an installed capacity of 240 MW and generates about 600 GWh of electricity per year.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.4 Tidal Energy · Page: 278
"Probably the best known tidal scheme is the Rance Power Station in France. In this scheme the tidal energy is captured by damming the estuary and forcing the tidal waters through axial flow turbines."
Basic w-fut-014
What is the proposed Severn Barrage?
The Severn Barrage is a long-proposed tidal scheme in England that would dam the Severn estuary. A barrage at Weston-super-Mare would deliver 2 GW continuously. A larger dam further east could yield 36.5 TWh per year — roughly 15% of Britain's electric-transport requirement.
