Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.4 Tidal Energy · Page: 279
"A barrage at Weston-super-Mare would produce 2 GW continuously and alternatively a dam further east would produce double this amount, that is 36.5 TWh of electricity per annum, 15% of the requirement for electric transport in Britain."
Basic w-fut-015
Where is the Gordon Dam, and how big is it?
The Gordon Dam is in Tasmania, Australia. It is one of many large hydro facilities used to generate electricity. The dam has an installed capacity of 430 MW, making it a meaningful contributor to renewable electricity supply on the island, while leaving local valley water levels regulated.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.3 Hydroelectricity · Page: 278
"The Gordon Dam in Tasmania is one of many large hydro facilities, with an installed capacity of 430 MW."
Basic w-fut-016
What is wave energy?
Wave energy is electricity generated by capturing the up-and-down motion of ocean surface waves. Several pilot devices have been built and tested, but none have yet reached large-scale commercial use. It remains an interesting future option for sustainable electricity supply in coastal countries.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.6 Wave Energy · Page: 280
"Another method of obtaining sustainable energy is by tapping the power in the waves. There are several systems under trial but as yet none have been commercialised."
Basic w-fut-017
What are biofuels?
Biofuels are liquid or solid fuels made from biomass — plant or animal matter. Examples include ethanol from fermented sugar, biodiesel from vegetable oil, and burning wood. Cars, ships, aircraft and trains can all run on biofuels using ordinary combustion engines instead of fossil fuels.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.4.1 Nuclear Fission · Page: 281
"Biofuels consist of a wide range of fuels derived from biomass... Cars, ships, aircraft and trains can all be run successfully on biofuels using conventional combustion engines."
Basic w-fut-018
What is the main problem with using biofuels widely?
Biofuels work technically, but they compete with food crops for land. Supplying just today's aviation industry from biofuels would need an area roughly the size of Texas, Oklahoma, Kansas and Iowa combined. That land cost makes biofuels a poor replacement for fossil fuels at large scale.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.4.1 Nuclear Fission · Page: 281
"The problem with widespread use of biofuels is not whether they can be used successfully, but whether growing crops for biofuels will detract from essential food production."
Basic w-fut-019
What is nuclear fission?
Nuclear fission is the splitting of heavy atoms such as uranium to release large amounts of heat. That heat boils water to drive steam turbines that generate electricity. Fission produces no carbon dioxide, so it can power future electric transport, though radioactive waste must be managed.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.4.2 Nuclear Fusion · Page: 282
"Nuclear fission certainly has the potential to generate enough electricity to power future electric transport."
Basic w-fut-020
What is a pebble-bed nuclear reactor?
A pebble-bed reactor is a nuclear-fission design in which uranium fuel is scattered through tennis-ball-sized graphite pebbles. Helium gas is used as the coolant rather than water, so the coolant cannot itself become radioactive. The design aims to overcome the safety problems of older reactors.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.4.2 Nuclear Fusion · Page: 282
"Pebble bed reactors are considered to overcome many of the safety problems which are associated with nuclear fission reactors... the fuel takes the form of uranium bits scattered among graphite pebbles. Helium is used as the coolant"
Basic w-fut-021
What is nuclear fusion?
Nuclear fusion is the joining of light atoms, like hydrogen, to release energy. It is the process that powers the sun and a hydrogen bomb. Researchers have produced fusion briefly in machines such as JET, but a commercial fusion power station is still many years away.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.4.2 Nuclear Fusion · Page: 282
"An example of nuclear fusion is the process which takes place in a hydrogen bomb and also in the sun. To create useful fusion power we need to be able to control this process in a power station."
Basic w-fut-022
What does the book conclude about future zero-carbon power for transport?
The book concludes that electricity for transport can be produced without burning fossil fuels. The likely mix is nuclear fission plus a range of renewables, with solar energy as the main contributor, supplemented by wind, tidal and undersea-current generation, and possibly nuclear fusion in the long term.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.5 In Conclusion · Page: 283
"such methods will include a mix of nuclear fission power stations and a range of alternative energy sources. Solar energy is likely to be the main alternative energy but a mix of solar, wind, tidal and undersea currents... are likely to feature strongly."
Basic w-fut-023
What is a Low-Speed Vehicle (LSV)?
A Low-Speed Vehicle, or LSV, is a small electric vehicle aimed at short local trips like shopping, commuting and visiting friends. They typically have ranges below 100 km and are sold as eco-friendly transport for retirees and city users who do not need motorway speeds.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.2.3 Low-Speed Vehicles · Page: 287
"LSVs are an 'environmentally friendly' mode of transport for short trips, commuting and shopping... Most have ranges under 100 km"
Basic w-fut-024
How far do most US drivers travel each day?
About 75% of US drivers are believed to make daily round trips of less than 40 km. That is well within the range of small electric Low-Speed Vehicles, which suggests LSVs could realistically replace petrol cars for most everyday driving, especially in rural areas with light traffic.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.2.3 Low-Speed Vehicles · Page: 287
"In the USA, for example, 75% of drivers are believed to drive round trips of less than 40 km per day."
Basic w-fut-025
What kind of electric vehicle was the Peugeot 106 Electric?
The Peugeot 106 Electric and the Peugeot Partner were ordinary petrol Peugeots converted to run on batteries. Their range was good enough for city deliveries but shorter than purpose-built electric cars. They illustrate the cost-versus-range trade-off when converting an existing vehicle to electric drive.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.1 Peugeot 106 and the Partner · Page: 288
"The Peugeot electric vehicles are examples of conventional vehicles converted to electric vehicles. Their range is doubtless adequate for uses such as city deliveries, but is less than might have been obtained with a purpose-built electric vehicle."
Basic w-fut-026
What is the GM EV1?
The GM EV1 is a two-seat rechargeable-battery electric car launched by General Motors in 1997. Unlike the Peugeot, it was designed from scratch as an electric vehicle rather than converted from a petrol car. At launch it was probably the most advanced battery EV in the world.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 288
"The GM EV1 is a rechargeable battery-powered two-seater car, which at the time of its introduction represented probably the most advanced electric vehicle using rechargeable batteries. It was purposely designed through and through as an electric vehicle"
Basic w-fut-027
What battery did the GM EV1 use first?
When the EV1 was first introduced in 1997 it used lead-acid batteries, specifically 26 valve-regulated high-capacity cells of 12 V and 60 Ah each. Later versions switched to nickel-metal-hydride (NiMH) batteries, which gave the car a longer driving range between charges.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 288
"It was introduced in 1997 initially using lead acid batteries, but more recent versions have used NiMH batteries to give an extended range."
Basic w-fut-028
What is the drag coefficient of the GM EV1?
The GM EV1 has a drag coefficient (Cd) of just 0.19, which at the time of its launch was the lowest of any production car. The slippery shape combined with very low rolling-resistance tyres reduces the power needed to push it through the air, extending its range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 289
"It has the lowest drag coefficient of any production car (Cd 0.19) and uses very low rolling resistance tyres."
Basic w-fut-029
What motor powers the GM EV1?
The EV1 is powered by a 102 kW three-phase AC induction motor. Power goes through a single-speed, dual-reduction gearset with a ratio of 10.946 to 1, so there is no clutch or multi-speed gearbox — typical of electric drivetrains where motor torque is available from rest.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 289
"The EV1 is powered by a 102 kW, three-phase AC induction motor and uses a singlespeed, dual-reduction gearset with a ratio of 10.946:1."
Basic w-fut-030
How long does the GM EV1 take to charge?
Using its 220 V inductive charger, the EV1 takes about five and a half to six hours to charge from empty to full. Inductive charging means there are no exposed metal contacts, so the car can be charged safely outdoors in rain or other bad weather.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 289
"The EV1 can be charged safely in all weather conditions with inductive charging. Using a 220 V charger, charging from 0 to 100% takes from 51/2; to 6 hours."
Basic w-fut-031
How is the GM EV1 unlocked and started?
The EV1 does not use a traditional metal key. The driver enters a five-digit personal identification code on a keypad outside the door to unlock the car, then enters the same code on a keypad on the centre console to switch the car on and drive away.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 291
"The EV1 does not require a conventional key to unlock the door. A five-digit personal identification code is entered on the exterior keypad to allow access."
Basic w-fut-032
What is the top speed of the GM EV1?
The GM EV1 has an electronically limited top speed of 80 mph, which is about 128 kph. The car comes with traction control, cruise control, anti-lock brakes and airbags, so although it is a small two-seat electric car, it is equipped much like a regular production car.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 290
"The EV1 has an electronically regulated top speed of 80 mph (128 kph). It comes with traction control, cruise control, anti-lock brakes, airbags"
Basic w-fut-033
What is the Nissan Leaf?
The Nissan Leaf is a five-door hatchback battery electric car launched commercially by Nissan. It uses a lithium-ion battery and a permanent-magnet synchronous motor, giving a range of about 100 miles (160 km) between charges. It was released in Japan in 2010 and later built in Britain.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.4 Hybrid Vehicles · Page: 292
"Nissan has released a commercial five-door hatchback electric car fitted with a lithium ion battery driven by a permanent magnet synchronous motor and with a range of around 100 miles (160 km) between charges."
Basic w-fut-034
How long does the Nissan Leaf take to charge?
From a home charging unit the Leaf takes about eight hours to charge from empty to full. A rapid charger can top it up to 80% of full capacity in just 30 minutes, which is handy for longer trips that need a short pause partway through.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.4 Hybrid Vehicles · Page: 292
"The Leaf can be charged from a home charging unit in 8 hours and can take a rapid charge to 80% of the battery capacity in 30 minutes."
Basic w-fut-035
What is the Honda Insight?
The Honda Insight is a hybrid passenger car that combines a small petrol engine with an electric motor powered by a battery. Both can drive the wheels. The Insight is not plugged in — instead, the engine and regenerative braking keep the battery charged as the car is driven.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.4.1 The Honda Insight · Page: 293
"The Honda Insight is a hybrid vehicle combining a conventional petrol-driven engine with an additional motor driven by a battery. The engine and motor can both be used to propel the vehicle."
Indirect w-fut-036
Why does the GM EV1 have its rear wheels closer together than its front wheels?
Bringing the rear wheels in by about 23 cm gives the body a teardrop shape. A teardrop is one of the most aerodynamic shapes possible, so the trick reduces drag, lets a smaller motor push the car the same distance, and stretches the battery range — important for any EV.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 290
"The rear wheels are 9 in (23 cm) closer together than the front wheels, which allows for a teardrop body shape that lessens drag"
Indirect w-fut-037
Why was the GM EV1 only leased, never sold outright?
GM only leased the EV1 because it was made in limited numbers as a compliance car for California's ZEV rule. Once California rolled back the strict zero-emission mandate, GM pulled the car and recovered every lease, ending the programme rather than supporting long-term retail ownership of the car.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 289
"The vehicle was produced in limited numbers and could only be leased rather than bought. To the dismay of electric vehicle enthusiasts the EV1 was recently taken off the market."
Indirect w-fut-038
Why would rooftop solar alone not be enough to power future electric transport?
Rooftop solar panels only cover a small total area and only generate during daylight. Even if all suitable roofs were used, the output would only be a fraction of what mass EV charging would need. Big solar farms or other renewables would be required to fill the gap.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.1 Solar Energy · Page: 275
"rooftop solar will only produce a fraction of the power which may be needed for future electric transport."
Indirect w-fut-039
Why are biofuels not a real long-term replacement for petrol or diesel?
Biofuels can technically run any vehicle, but growing enough biomass to replace petrol and diesel competes with food production. Even matching just today's aviation fuel use needs roughly the cropland of Texas, Oklahoma, Kansas and Iowa combined, so biofuels cannot scale up without starving people.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.4.1 Nuclear Fission · Page: 281
"To supply the global aviation industry at current levels of consumption would require some 274.8 million acres of cropland... Clearly the use of biofuels would detract from food production and there is little argument for using biofuels as a major replacement for fossil fuels."
Indirect w-fut-040
Why does the Honda Insight count only as a partial zero-emission vehicle?
The Insight has an engine and a battery-driven motor. In heavy slow traffic it runs from the battery and emits nothing locally, behaving like a pure EV. At higher loads the petrol engine fires up, so it still emits exhaust gases — it is therefore only partly emission-free.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.4.1 The Honda Insight · Page: 293
"In heavy traffic the car is driven from the batteries via the motor/generator only. Hence it can be classified as a partial zero-emission vehicle (PZEV)."
Indirect w-fut-041
Why are globally distributed solar farms with HV DC links seen as attractive?
If solar farms are spread across longitudes and joined by high-voltage DC transmission, sunshine somewhere on the network is producing power at any hour of day. That smooths the supply, removing the day-and-night problem of a single site and giving steady electricity for EVs around the clock.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.1 Solar Energy · Page: 276
"An attractive option is to use a series of solar farms distributed around the globe and connected by high-voltage, high-efficiency electric transmission lines. Global distribution would provide solar electricity throughout the day and night."
Indirect w-fut-042
Why is undersea current energy more predictable than wind or solar?
Ocean currents are driven by tides and large-scale circulation, which follow regular astronomical and oceanographic patterns. Their speed and direction can be forecast accurately, while wind and sunshine depend on weather. That predictability makes underwater turbines a steady source of energy for a power grid.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.6 Wave Energy · Page: 280
"Marine currents are more predictable than wind and solar."
Indirect w-fut-043
Why did CARB switch to a credit-based system for zero-emission vehicles?
Strict ZEV-only rules ignored the fact that some hybrids may pollute less than a battery car charged from a coal-fired grid. A credit system lets a car maker earn fractions of a ZEV credit for selling cleaner-than-average vehicles, which better reflects true well-to-wheels emissions.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 12. Electric Vehicles and the Environment · Section: 12.4 The Effect of Electrified Transport · Page: 272
"Vehicles that are not fully 'zero emission' might actually produce fewer emissions in the whole well-to-wheel analysis than a zero-emission vehicle (ZEV)... The regulations now incorporate a system of credits"
Indirect w-fut-044
Why is a purpose-built EV better than converting a petrol car?
A car designed from scratch as an EV, like the GM EV1, can use slippery aerodynamics, low-rolling-resistance tyres and battery placement made specifically for an electric drive. A converted petrol car carries spare weight and shape, so it ends up with less range for the same battery size.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.3.2 The GM EV1 · Page: 291
"The advanced performance clearly illustrates the benefits of designing the vehicle as an electric car rather than simply converting an existing vehicle."
Indirect w-fut-045
Why is the market for Low-Speed Vehicles expected to grow in western countries?
Western countries have ageing populations. Many active retired people still want to visit friends, shop and run errands, but do not need to drive long distances or at motorway speeds. Quiet, simple, short-range electric LSVs match this lifestyle, so demand is likely to rise steadily.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.2.3 Low-Speed Vehicles · Page: 287
"These vehicles are particularly targeted at fairly active retired people who still want to get about... The demographics of most western countries show there is little doubt that the market for this type of vehicle will grow steadily."
Medium w-fut-046
How does the Toyota Prius split power between its engine, motor, generator and wheels?
The Prius uses a planetary gearset called the power splitter and an electronically controlled CVT. The split sends engine power partly to the wheels and partly to a generator that charges the battery and feeds the motor. A dashboard display shows energy flow at every moment in real time.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.4.2 The Toyota Prius · Page: 295
"The transmission incorporates a fairly complex system of planetary gears, called a 'power splitter', which directs power between the IC engine, the electric motor, the generator and the wheels"
Medium w-fut-047
How does the Chevrolet Volt switch from pure-electric to series-hybrid driving?
The Volt runs as a pure EV from its lithium battery for the first 40 to 80 km. Once the battery falls to a preset low level, the petrol engine starts but only drives a generator, which feeds the traction motor — making the Volt operate as a series hybrid.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.4.3 The Chevrolet Volt · Page: 296
"The car runs entirely from the battery for the first 25–50 miles (40–80 km), after which it functions primarily as a series hybrid with the IC engine driving the generator to power the traction electric motor."
Medium w-fut-048
How does the Honda Insight recover energy when the driver brakes?
On a light brake press, the Insight's motor/generator switches into generator mode. It loads the wheels and slows the car, turning kinetic energy back into electricity stored in the battery. Only when the driver presses harder do the conventional friction brakes engage to bring the car to a stop.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 14. Recent Electric Vehicles · Section: 14.4.1 The Honda Insight · Page: 293
"When the brake pedal is pressed lightly, the Insight's electric motor operates in regeneration mode, and the car begins to slow just as it would with normal brakes. Once the brake pedal is pressed further, the normal brakes come into play"
Medium w-fut-049
How much of Britain's electric-transport demand could the Severn Barrage cover?
A Severn Barrage near Weston-super-Mare would generate 2 GW continuously. A larger dam further east would double that and yield about 36.5 TWh per year — roughly 15% of all the electricity Britain would need to electrify its transport, from a single tidal site.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.3.4 Tidal Energy · Page: 279
"a dam further east would produce double this amount, that is 36.5 TWh of electricity per annum, 15% of the requirement for electric transport in Britain."
Medium w-fut-050
What efficiency gap separates old coal stations from modern combined-cycle stations?
Old coal-fired power stations averaged around 28% efficiency — only about a quarter of the fuel's energy reached the grid. Modern combined-cycle stations, which use two heat engines in tandem, regularly exceed 50%, with the best designs reaching 60% — roughly doubling the useful output per unit of fuel.
Source: Electric Vehicle Technology Explained, 2nd Ed. (Larminie & Lowry, Wiley)
Chapter: 13. Power Generation for Transport, Particularly for Zero Emissions · Section: 13.2 Power Generation using Fossil Fuels · Page: 274
"Combined cycle power stations have achieved efficiencies of more than 60% (electrical energy generated/energy in the fuel). In general service combined cycle efficiencies are over 50%"

2. Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)

various contributors · CRC Press / Taylor & Francis · 50 Q&As

Basic c-crc-001
What is a Hybrid Electric Vehicle (HEV)?
A Hybrid Electric Vehicle combines an internal combustion engine and an electric motor within the same drive train. The electric motor usually supports the engine to improve fuel economy or performance, and the vehicle is propelled by either the engine or the electric drive.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Introduction to Electric Vehicles · Section: 1.2 Benefits and Challenges · Page: 7
"A Hybrid Electric Vehicle (HEV) combines an ICE and an electric motor within the drive train."
Basic c-crc-002
What distinguishes a Plug-in Hybrid Electric Vehicle from a regular hybrid?
A Plug-in Hybrid Electric Vehicle carries a larger battery than a normal hybrid and can be recharged from home outlets or charging stations. Many PHEVs can run in fully electric mode if enough energy is stored in the battery, unlike standard hybrids.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Introduction to Electric Vehicles · Section: 1.2 Benefits and Challenges · Page: 7
"a vehicle equipped, in general, with a larger battery compared to HEVs, that allows recharging of the battery via home outlets or at charging stations"
Indirect c-crc-003
Why are Full Electric Vehicles not truly zero-emission?
While Full Electric Vehicles release no pollutants while driving, the electricity used to recharge their batteries usually comes from power plants that do emit pollutants. So overall emissions depend on the cleanliness of the country's power generation, not just the vehicle itself.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Introduction to Electric Vehicles · Section: 1.2 Benefits and Challenges · Page: 7
"the recharging of the batteries will cause emissions depending on the actual emissions of the power generation in the country"
Basic c-crc-004
What is range anxiety in the context of electric vehicles?
Range anxiety refers to driver worry about an EV's limited range plus its unpredictable depletion when heating, air conditioning, or detours are added. Because EV ranges below 300 km in good conditions are common, drivers fear running out of charge before reaching their destination.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Introduction to Electric Vehicles · Section: 1.2 Benefits and Challenges · Page: 11
"The latter two issues are often grouped together as one and discussed under the title of range anxiety"
Indirect c-crc-005
Why has the cost of batteries been such a big obstacle to EV adoption?
Batteries make up a major portion of an EV's total price, keeping vehicles expensive even with government subsidies. Some companies have tried leasing batteries to customers to offset this cost. Forecasts suggest battery costs will fall dramatically in coming years, easing the pressure.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Introduction to Electric Vehicles · Section: 1.2 Benefits and Challenges · Page: 11
"A major factor in the cost of such vehicles is the cost of the battery"
Basic c-crc-006
What is regenerative braking in an electric machine?
Regenerative braking is the braking mode in an electric machine where, instead of wasting kinetic energy as heat, the machine converts the vehicle's mechanical energy from the wheels back into electrical energy. This recovered energy can recharge the battery and help extend driving range.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: — · Page: 16
"The braking mode in electric machines is referred to as regenerative braking."
Indirect c-crc-007
Why does an electric motor typically give a vehicle better acceleration than an internal combustion engine?
Electric motors deliver full torque even at very low speeds, and their instantaneous power can be two or three times their rated power. This means an electric drive gives strong launch and excellent acceleration from a relatively small, nominally rated motor.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: — · Page: 16
"the motor provides full torque at low speeds and the instantaneous power rating can be two or three times the rated power of the motor"
Basic c-crc-008
Why have DC series motors become obsolete in modern EV applications?
Although DC series motors matched road load characteristics well and were easy to control in older prototype EVs, their large physical size and heavy maintenance requirements (mostly due to brushes and commutators) have made them obsolete in the automotive industry and in motor drives generally.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: — · Page: 16
"the size and maintenance requirements of DC motors are making their use obsolete not just in the automotive industry"
Basic c-crc-009
What is a brushless DC motor?
A brushless DC motor is a permanent magnet motor with concentrated three-phase windings whose air-gap flux distribution is trapezoidal. It is driven by a six-switch inverter, much like an induction motor, but its control is simpler because of the trapezoidal back-EMF shape.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: — · Page: 16
"The trapezoidal motors have concentrated three-phase windings and are also known as brushless DC motors."
Medium c-crc-010
How do switched reluctance motors produce torque differently from DC or PM motors?
DC and permanent magnet motors produce torque by mutual interaction between two orthogonal magnetic fields. Switched reluctance motors instead use a varying-reluctance flux path: the rotor is pulled toward whichever position minimises the magnetic circuit's reluctance, giving torque without rotor windings or magnets.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.1 Simple Electric Machines · Page: 16
"by using a varying reluctance flux path where the rotor moves toward attaining the minimum reluctance position"
Indirect c-crc-011
Why are switched reluctance motors attractive for vehicle traction despite their drawbacks?
SR motors have a simple rotor with no windings, magnets, or cage, which gives them excellent fault tolerance, a high torque-to-inertia ratio, and the widest possible constant-power speed range. These traits are ideal for traction, though acoustic noise and torque ripple remain known concerns.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: — · Page: 16
"The constant power speed range is the widest possible in SR motors compared to other technologies, which makes it ideally suitable for traction applications."
Basic c-crc-012
In an electric machine, what is the back-EMF?
The back-EMF, also called motional voltage, is the voltage induced in the armature when its conductors move through the magnetic field. For a DC machine, back-EMF is proportional to rotor speed when the field flux is held constant by design.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.1.2.3 DC Machine Back-EMF and Torque · Page: 22
"Ea is the induced voltage or motional voltage, more commonly known as back-emf of the machine"
Basic c-crc-013
How is a separately excited DC motor defined in the CRC reference?
A separately excited DC motor is one whose armature and field windings are supplied by independently controlled DC sources. This independence allows separate control of armature current and field current, giving the maximum flexibility for tuning torque and speed in the machine.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.2 DC Machines · Page: 24
"When the armature and field windings are supplied from independently controlled DC sources, then it is known as a separately excited DC machine."
Indirect c-crc-014
Why is a DC series motor good for fast starting acceleration?
In a series DC machine the armature and field windings are in series, so the same current passes through both. This produces a very high starting torque, which translates into rapid acceleration. The trade-off is the loss of independent control over flux and armature current.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.2 DC Machines · Page: 24
"The greatest advantage of the series machine is the very high starting torque that helps achieve rapid acceleration."
Basic c-crc-015
What does it mean to minimise losses in a separately excited DC motor?
Losses in a separately excited DC motor are minimised when the armature-circuit losses (mainly resistive copper losses in the armature) equal the field-circuit losses. The controller can pick armature voltage and field flux to balance those two loss terms, maximising efficiency at the chosen operating point.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.2 DC Machines · Page: 28
"The loss in DC machines is minimized when armature circuit-dependent losses equal the field circuit dependent losses"
Indirect c-crc-016
Why does moving the armature winding into the stator simplify AC machines?
In AC machines the armature circuit sits in the stationary stator instead of the rotor, so commutators and brushes (needed in DC machines to flip rotor current) are no longer required. This eliminates brush wear and the electromagnetic interference associated with mechanical commutation.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.3 Three-Phase AC Machines · Page: 29
"The advantage gained in having the armature circuit in the stator is the elimination of the commutator and brushes of the DC machines."
Basic c-crc-017
What is synchronous speed in a three-phase AC machine?
Synchronous speed is the rotational speed at which the stator's three-phase mmf wave rotates around the air gap. It equals the angular frequency of the applied stator voltage, and the resulting mmf has a constant peak amplitude that circles the stator at this speed.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.3.4.3 Resultant mmf in a Balanced System · Page: 39
"rotates around the stator circumference at a constant speed equal to the angular speed of the applied stator voltages. This speed is known as the synchronous speed."
Basic c-crc-018
What is a squirrel-cage induction motor?
A squirrel-cage induction motor has a rotor made of short-circuited copper or aluminium bars set axially around stacked laminations, connected at each end by end rings shaped like a squirrel cage. Its rugged construction and low cost make it the workhorse of industry.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.4 Induction Machines · Page: 42
"The rotor windings consist of short-circuited copper bars that form the shape of a squirrel cage."
Basic c-crc-019
What is slip in an induction motor?
Slip is the difference between the rotor speed and the stator's synchronous speed, expressed as a fraction of the synchronous speed. The rotor must spin slightly slower than the field for the rotor bars to cut flux, induce a voltage, and produce torque.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: — · Page: 43
"The slip speed expressed as a fraction of the synchronous speed is known as the slip"
Indirect c-crc-020
Why is an induction motor usually run at small slip values?
Operating at small slip keeps the rotor frequency low, so the rotor leakage reactance has little effect and the motor stays in the linear part of its torque-speed curve. This avoids the heavy losses, voltage drops, and heating that come with high-slip operation.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: — · Page: 45
"operating the machine at small slip values improves the efficiency"
Medium c-crc-021
How much vehicle range can regenerative braking typically add?
Regenerative braking can extend the driving range of an electric vehicle by roughly 10 to 15 percent. Not all of the kinetic energy is captured because sudden stops would demand power far higher than the propulsion motor's rating, so mechanical brakes are still required.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.4.4 Regenerative Braking · Page: 52
"Regenerative braking can increase the range of electric vehicle by a small percentage (about 10%–15%)."
Basic c-crc-022
When does an induction machine work as a generator during braking?
An induction machine acts as a generator when its rotor turns faster than the synchronous speed, giving it a negative slip. The induced rotor currents reverse polarity and the electromagnetic torque becomes negative, opposing rotation and decelerating the vehicle while feeding energy back.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.4.4 Regenerative Braking · Page: 52
"The induction machine works as a generator when it is operated with a negative slip"
Basic c-crc-023
What is a four-quadrant drive in EV motor control?
A four-quadrant drive is a motor controller that can deliver positive or negative torque at positive or negative shaft speed. This lets the same machine run forward or in reverse and switch smoothly between motoring and regenerative braking modes, which EVs and HEVs always require.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.4.4 Regenerative Braking · Page: 52
"the electric motor is controlled by the drive to deliver positive or negative torque at positive or negative speed"
Indirect c-crc-024
Why do permanent magnet machines avoid the rotor copper losses found in induction motors?
In a PM machine the rotor field comes from permanent magnets rather than from coil currents. Because no rotor windings need to be energised, there is no resistive (copper) loss on the rotor, and there is no separate field exciter circuit to maintain.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.5 Permanent Magnet Machines · Page: 54
"This configuration eliminates the rotor copper loss as well as the need for maintenance of the field exciting circuit."
Medium c-crc-025
What are the three common types of magnets used in PM machines?
Permanent magnet motors typically use ferrites, samarium cobalt, or neodymium-iron-boron magnets. Ferrites are cheap but weak; samarium cobalt gives much higher flux density at higher cost; neodymium-iron-boron offers the strongest residual flux density (1.1 to 1.25 tesla) but is sensitive to temperature.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.5.1 Permanent Magnets · Page: 54
"The common types of magnets used in PM machines are the ferrites, samarium cobalt (SmCo), and neodymium-iron-boron (NdFeB)."
Indirect c-crc-026
Why is the interior PM machine well suited to EV applications needing flux weakening?
In an interior PMSM the magnets are buried inside the rotor, so the quadrature-axis inductance can be much larger than the direct-axis inductance. This larger difference enables flux-weakening operation, giving a wide constant-power speed range and reducing the need for multiple transmission gears.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.5.3 PMSM Models · Page: 60
"The larger difference in the d and q-axes inductances make the interior PM more suitable for flux weakening operation"
Basic c-crc-027
What distinguishes a PM brushless DC motor from a PMSM?
PM brushless DC motors have trapezoidal back-EMF waveforms produced by concentrated stator windings, while PMSMs use sinusoidally distributed windings and have sinusoidal back-EMFs. The BLDC motor only needs six discrete rotor positions per electrical revolution, simplifying its control compared to the PMSM.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.5.4 PM Brushless DC Motors · Page: 62
"The trapezoidal-shaped back-emf waveforms in these machines are due to the concentrated windings of the machine used instead of the sinusoidally distributed windings used in the PMSMs."
Indirect c-crc-028
Why do PMSMs require a high-resolution position sensor?
A PMSM produces smooth torque by precisely shaping the stator currents so they stay aligned with the rotor magnet field. That alignment requires accurate knowledge of rotor angle, so a high-resolution position sensor (and current sensors) feed information back to the digital controller.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.5.2 PM Synchronous Motors · Page: 57
"The smooth torque output is maintained in these machines by shaping the motor currents, which requires a high-resolution position sensor and current sensors."
Medium c-crc-029
What are the three regions of an SRM's torque-speed envelope?
An SRM drive has a constant torque region below the base speed (current and torque limited), a constant power region where conduction angle is increased as speed rises, and a high-speed natural region where torque falls roughly as one over speed squared.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 6. Electric Machines · Section: 6.6.3.4 Torque-Speed Characteristics · Page: 73
"The torque–speed plane of an SRM drive can be divided into three regions"
Basic c-crc-030
What is aerodynamic drag on a vehicle composed of?
Aerodynamic drag on a vehicle is made of two parts: shape drag, due to high-pressure zones in front and low-pressure zones behind the body, and skin friction, caused by shear stress in the boundary layer. Shape drag accounts for over 90 percent of total drag.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 2. Fundamentals of Conventional Vehicles and Powertrains · Section: 2.2.1 Aerodynamic Drag · Page: 81
"The external aerodynamic resistance is comprised of two components, shape drag and skin friction."
Indirect c-crc-031
Why does a rolling tyre create a retarding force on a moving vehicle?
When a tyre rolls, hysteresis in the rubber makes the contact patch's normal pressure higher in front and lower behind. That shifts the road's reaction force ahead of the wheel centre, creating a moment that opposes the wheel's motion - the rolling resistance.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 2. Fundamentals of Conventional Vehicles and Powertrains · Section: 2.2.3 Rolling Resistance · Page: 81
"The normal force due to the road is shifted from the center of the tire in the direction of motion. This shift produces a moment that exerts a retarding torque on the wheel."
Basic c-crc-032
What is gradeability for a vehicle?
Gradeability is the maximum slope that a vehicle can start climbing from a standstill while all of its wheels remain on the gradient. It depends on the available tractive effort versus the combined resistance forces acting on the vehicle at start-up.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 2. Fundamentals of Conventional Vehicles and Powertrains · Section: 2.5.2 Gradeability · Page: 84
"The gradeability of a vehicle is the maximum gradient on which the vehicle can start climbing from stand-still with all the wheels of the vehicle on the gradient at the time of start."
Indirect c-crc-033
Why is proper brake balance important when designing a regenerative braking system?
Maximum braking deceleration is only achieved when all four tyres reach the peak friction level at the same time. If the front or rear axle locks up first, those wheels lose cornering grip, the vehicle becomes unstable, and the full braking potential is wasted.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 2. Fundamentals of Conventional Vehicles and Powertrains · Section: 2.6 Braking Performance and Distribution · Page: 84
"the vehicle will not achieve the maximum braking deceleration unless all four tires are brought to the peak friction level simultaneously"
Medium c-crc-034
How much of total braking force may sit on the front axle in a high-performance car?
In high-performance vehicles, as much as 80 percent of the braking force can act on the front axle. This concentration on the front wheels creates a much larger opportunity to recapture energy at the front when designing a regenerative braking system, compared with a rear-wheel layout.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 2. Fundamentals of Conventional Vehicles and Powertrains · Section: 2.6 Braking Performance and Distribution · Page: 84
"In high-performance vehicles, up to 80% of the braking force may be on the front axle"
Indirect c-crc-035
Why is a continuously variable transmission attractive for fuel economy?
A CVT provides an effectively infinite number of gear ratios within its range, so the engine can be held at its most economical speed across a wide span of vehicle speeds. That lets the powertrain track an ideal torque-speed profile that fixed-ratio gearboxes cannot match.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 2. Fundamentals of Conventional Vehicles and Powertrains · Section: 2.7.2.3 Continuously Variable Transmission · Page: 88
"This allows the engine to operate under the most economical conditions over a wide range of vehicle speeds."
Indirect c-crc-036
Why combine a battery with an ultracapacitor in an EV energy storage system?
A battery provides high energy density but cannot easily handle sharp bursts of current. Pairing it with an ultracapacitor lets the capacitor supply or absorb high-power transients during acceleration and braking, reducing battery stress, extending battery life, and improving overall energy capture.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 8. Hybrid Energy Storage Systems · Section: — · Page: 92
"Battery/UC hybrid operation provides an improved solution over the stand-alone battery design in terms of improved power management and control flexibility."
Basic c-crc-037
What is battery C-rate?
The C-rate is a parameter expressing how intensely a battery is being discharged relative to its capacity. Low C-rates tend to lengthen battery life span, so designers try to avoid instantaneous high-power charge or discharge pulses, which raise stress, heat, and internal resistance.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 8. Hybrid Energy Storage Systems · Section: — · Page: 92
"Battery C-rate is defined as the parameter, which expresses battery discharge intensity"
Medium c-crc-038
What is the main drawback of the passive parallel battery and ultracapacitor topology?
In the passive parallel configuration the battery and ultracapacitor share a bus with no controller between them, so the battery cannot have its current shaped or limited. Whenever the ultracapacitor draws or supplies current, the battery follows the same profile for voltage equalisation, increasing battery stress.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 8. Hybrid Energy Storage Systems · Section: 8.1.1 Passive Parallel Configuration · Page: 92
"Battery current is, therefore, not effectively controlled"
Indirect c-crc-039
Why is the parallel-connected multi-converter topology said to be the most flexible?
Because each storage device has its own bidirectional DC/DC converter, the battery and ultracapacitor voltages are fully decoupled from the DC link and from each other. Power flows and controls are independent, which improves stability, efficiency, and reliability since one source can keep operating if another fails.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 8. Hybrid Energy Storage Systems · Section: 8.1.5 Multiple Parallel-Connected Converters Configuration · Page: 95
"This topology offers the highest flexibility and provides better functionality than that of the cascaded converters topology."
Basic c-crc-040
How does a flywheel energy storage system store energy?
A flywheel stores energy kinetically as a large rotating disk with a very high moment of inertia, spinning between roughly 20,000 and 50,000 rpm. A motor-generator either speeds up the flywheel to store energy or is driven by it to release energy when needed.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 8. Hybrid Energy Storage Systems · Section: 8.2.1 Flywheel ESS · Page: 103
"a flywheel stores energy in a kinetic device rather than in an electrochemical or electrostatic device"
Indirect c-crc-041
Why must superconducting magnetic energy storage operate at very low temperatures?
SMES coils only act as superconductors and avoid ohmic losses when chilled to very low temperatures. A cryogenic refrigeration system is therefore required, and its energy use and complexity cut the overall efficiency, which is a serious obstacle to using SMES at vehicle scale.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 8. Hybrid Energy Storage Systems · Section: 8.2.3 Superconducting Magnetic ESS · Page: 106
"needing to be operated at very low temperatures for their coils to act as a superconducting material and reduce ohmic losses"
Medium c-crc-042
Among the simulated battery/UC topologies, which gave the lowest DC link voltage ripple?
The parallel-connected multi-converter topology gave the smallest DC-link voltage ripple, with a maximum of 400.7 V and minimum of 397.6 V (about 0.8 percent). The passive parallel and cascaded converter topologies each saw roughly 2.4 to 2.5 percent ripple over the same drive cycle.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 8. Hybrid Energy Storage Systems · Section: 8.4.3 Simulation of Parallel-Connected Multiconverters · Page: 118
"the DC link voltage sees a maximum of 400.7 V and a minimum of 397.6 V, resulting in a maximum ripple percentage of 0.8%"
Basic c-crc-043
What is a solar powered charging station?
A solar powered charging station, or SPCS, is an EV charging site whose electricity is generated by solar panels. The panels typically also shade the parking area, and most installations are tied to the local electrical grid so power is available even when sunlight is not.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 3. Solar Powered Charging Stations · Section: — · Page: 126
"Solar powered charging stations (SPCSs) are one of the important developments related to the electrification of transportation."
Indirect c-crc-044
Why are parking lots a particularly suitable place to install solar panels?
There are far more parking spaces than vehicles in the United States, and many spaces sit empty across stadiums, churches, shopping centres, and workplaces. Covering these unused spaces with panels adds clean generation, provides shade, and could supply a meaningful share of national electricity.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 3. Solar Powered Charging Stations · Section: — · Page: 132
"there are many more parking spaces than vehicles because there are always many empty parking spaces at any given time"
Basic c-crc-045
What is Level 1 EV charging?
Level 1 EV charging uses a standard 120-volt AC household outlet through a cord usually supplied with the vehicle. It adds about 5 miles of range, or roughly 2 kWh, per hour - similar to what a single parking space's solar panels produce.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 3. Solar Powered Charging Stations · Section: 3.4 Electric Vehicle Supply Equipment · Page: 132
"Level 1 charging often adds about 5 miles of range or about 2 kWh per hour to the batteries."
Medium c-crc-046
How much range can DC fast charging add in 20 minutes?
DC fast chargers (Level 3) are designed to deliver rapid charging over 20 to 30 minutes, ending at about three-quarters of full charge. In that window they can add roughly 50 to 70 miles of driving range to a typical electric vehicle.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 3. Solar Powered Charging Stations · Section: 3.4 Electric Vehicle Supply Equipment · Page: 132
"With fast charging 50–70 miles of range are added in 20 min."
Basic c-crc-047
What is acid rain and what causes it?
Acid rain forms when nitrogen dioxide released by combustion reacts with atmospheric water to make nitric acid, which then comes down dissolved in rainfall. It damages forests in industrialised countries and corrodes historical marble monuments, and sulfur dioxide from fuels makes a similar contribution.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Environmental Impact and History of Modern Transportation · Section: 1.1.1 Nitrogen Oxides · Page: 139
"It also reacts with atmospheric water to form nitric acid (HNO3), which dilutes in rain. This phenomenon is referred to as "acid rain""
Indirect c-crc-048
Why is carbon monoxide so dangerous to people?
Carbon monoxide attaches to the haemoglobin in blood cells in place of oxygen, starving the body's organs of the oxygen they need. The bond is far stronger than oxygen's, so normal body chemistry cannot break it - victims must be treated in pressurised chambers.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Environmental Impact and History of Modern Transportation · Section: 1.1.2 Carbon Monoxide · Page: 139
"Once carbon monoxide reaches blood cells, it attaches to the hemoglobin in place of oxygen"
Medium c-crc-049
What share of world oil consumption did transportation account for in 1997?
The transportation sector consumed about 49 percent of the oil used in the world in 1997, making it the largest single user of petroleum. Most projected growth in industrialised-country oil demand also comes from transportation, since few economical alternatives existed at the time of the forecast.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Environmental Impact and History of Modern Transportation · Section: 1.5 Importance of Different Transportation Development Strategies · Page: 145
"the transportation sector is the primary user of petroleum, consuming 49% of the oil used in the world in 1997"
Basic c-crc-050
Who built the first electric vehicle and when?
The first electric vehicle was built by Frenchman Gustave Trouve in 1881. It was a tricycle powered by a 0.1-horsepower DC motor fed by lead-acid batteries, and together with its driver weighed roughly 160 kilograms - far slower than later gasoline cars would be.
Source: Hybrid and Electric Vehicles Freebook (compilation of selected chapters)
Chapter: 1. Environmental Impact and History of Modern Transportation · Section: 1.6 History of EVs · Page: 151
"The first EV was built by Frenchman Gustave Trouvé in 1881. It was a tricycle powered by a 0.1-hp direct current (DC) motor fed by lead-acid batteries."

3. Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge

SME Education Foundation · SME (Society of Manufacturing Engineers) · 50 Q&As

Basic c-sme-001
What weight does the SME EV Body of Knowledge give to Manufacturing Foundations and Awareness?
The SME EV Body of Knowledge assigns Manufacturing Foundations and Awareness a weight of 15 percent of the total competency map. That share reflects how much of a learner's effort should go into foundational shop-floor knowledge before tackling EV-specific topics in detail.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: — · Page: 2
"1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness"
Basic c-sme-002
How important does SME rate General OSHA Standards and Regulations for EV manufacturing?
SME rates General OSHA Standards and Regulations as a High importance topic. The expected competency level is Remember and Understand, meaning a learner should recall the rules and grasp why they exist rather than apply them in advanced engineering analysis tasks.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.1 General OSHA Standards/Regulations · Page: 2
"1.1. General OSHA Standards/Regulations"
Basic c-sme-003
Under SME's OSHA subtopics, what does PPE stand for?
Under SME's OSHA subtopics, PPE stands for Personal Protective Equipment. It refers to gear such as gloves, safety glasses, insulated boots and arc-rated clothing that workers must wear to reduce injury risk on an EV manufacturing shop floor every day.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.1.3 Personal Protective Equipment (PPE) · Page: 2
"Personal Protective Equipment (PPE)"
Basic c-sme-004
What safety subtopic does SME list right after Personal Protective Equipment?
Right after Personal Protective Equipment, SME lists Lockout/Tagout as the next OSHA subtopic. Lockout/Tagout covers procedures for de-energising and labelling equipment so workers cannot be hurt while servicing machines that still have stored electrical or mechanical energy inside them.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.1.4 Lockout/Tagout · Page: 2
"Personal Protective Equipment (PPE) 1.1.4. Lockout/Tagout"
Basic c-sme-005
Does the SME EV Body of Knowledge call out high-voltage safety as a separate topic?
Yes, SME calls out High Voltage Safety as its own subtopic under OSHA Standards, along with linked items for High Voltage Cables and a Safety Switch. This emphasis reflects the unique shock hazards present around traction battery packs and inverters.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.1.8 High Voltage Safety · Page: 2
"1.1.8. High Voltage Safety"
Basic c-sme-006
What competency level does SME assign to Measurement?
SME assigns Measurement a Medium importance and an Apply and Analyse competency level. So a trainee should not only recall measurement basics but actually use measuring tools, read results correctly and analyse what those numbers mean for a real build.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.2 Measurement · Page: 2
"1.2. Measurement"
Basic c-sme-007
How does SME rate Print Reading for EV manufacturing learners?
SME rates Print Reading at Medium importance and at the Apply and Analyse competency level. Learners are expected to interpret engineering drawings well enough to act on them, not just recognise the symbols and basic line conventions used on a print.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.3 Print Reading · Page: 2
"1.3. Print Reading"
Basic c-sme-008
Where does Fluid Mechanics sit in SME's importance ranking?
Fluid Mechanics sits at Low importance in SME's ranking, with a Remember and Understand competency level. Learners need to know the basics of fluid behaviour, such as flow and pressure, but they are not expected to do detailed engineering calculations on the topic.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.4 Fluid Mechanics · Page: 2

Basic c-sme-009
What competency does SME ask of learners for Direct Current Electricity?
For Direct Current Electricity, SME asks learners to reach an Apply and Analyse competency level at Medium importance. They should be able to set up DC circuits, take readings and interpret what voltage, current and resistance values are telling them about a system.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.6 Direct Current Electricity · Page: 2

Basic c-sme-010
Which three quantities does SME list as sub-items under Ohm's Law?
SME lists three sub-items under Ohm's Law: Voltage, Current and Resistance. These are the three quantities tied together by the law itself, so the curriculum makes sure each is learned before students apply the relationship to real EV circuits and components.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.7 Ohm Law · Page: 2

Indirect c-sme-011
Why does SME place Situational Awareness at the Evaluate Problems and Create Solutions level?
Situational Awareness is placed at the Evaluate Problems and Create Solutions level because spotting hazards on a live EV line is not just memory work. A technician has to read the surroundings in real time, judge risks and choose a safe response immediately.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 1. Manufacturing Foundations/Awareness · Section: 1.9 Situational Awareness · Page: 2

Basic c-sme-012
How does SME rate the importance of Industry 4.0 and SMART Manufacturing?
SME rates Introduction to Industry 4.0 and SMART Manufacturing as Low importance, with a Remember and Understand competency. Learners need to be familiar with smart-factory concepts and basic terminology, but deep technical mastery is not expected at this stage of training.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge

Basic c-sme-013
How much of the SME EV Body of Knowledge is devoted to the Electric Vehicle Overview section?
The Electric Vehicle Overview section is given 20 percent of the total SME EV Body of Knowledge. That is the second-largest share in the curriculum and signals that learners should spend significant time on basic EV concepts and definitions early on.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 2. Electric Vehicle Overview · Section: — · Page: 2
