Basic c-sme-014
What two vehicle types does SME compare under 'What are Electric Vehicles'?
Under What are Electric Vehicles, SME explicitly compares the Electric Vehicle, abbreviated EV, against the Internal Combustion Engine vehicle, abbreviated ICE. Learners are expected to grasp the differences in propulsion type, energy source and emissions between the two designs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 2. Electric Vehicle Overview · Section: 2.1 What are Electric Vehicles? · Page: 2
"Electric Vehicle (EV) vs. Internal Combustion Engine (ICE)"
Basic c-sme-015
Which four electric vehicle types does SME list under Types of Electric Vehicles?
SME lists four electric vehicle types: Battery Electric Vehicle, Plug-in Hybrid Electric Vehicle, Hybrid Electric Vehicle and Fuel Cell Electric Vehicle. Each represents a different way of supplying energy to the wheels and shapes its own design and refuelling profile.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 2. Electric Vehicle Overview · Section: 2.2 Types of Electric Vehicles · Page: 3
"Battery Electric Vehicle (BEV)"
Basic c-sme-016
What share of the SME EV Body of Knowledge is given to Components of Electric Vehicles?
Components of Electric Vehicles is given the largest share, 25 percent, of the SME EV Body of Knowledge. That weight tells trainees that most of their study time should be spent on the physical parts that make an EV actually move.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: — · Page: 3
"3. Components of Electric Vehicles"
Basic c-sme-017
Which two battery chemistries does SME mention under Battery Selection?
Under Battery Selection, SME mentions two chemistries: Lithium-ion and Lithium Polymer. Both store energy by moving lithium ions, but they use different electrolyte and packaging styles, and a learner is expected to recognise where each one is typically applied.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.2 Battery Selection · Page: 3
"Lithium-ion 3.2.2. Lithium Polymer"
Basic c-sme-018
Which three battery cell formats does SME include under Battery Cells?
Under Battery Cells, SME includes three formats: Cylindrical Cells, Prismatic Cells and Pouch Cells. Each format wraps the same internal layers in a different outer shape, affecting how the cells are packed, cooled and protected inside a battery module assembly.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.3 Battery Cells · Page: 3
"Cylindrical Cells 3.3.2. Prismatic Cells"
Basic c-sme-019
What does the abbreviation BMS stand for in the SME taxonomy?
In the SME taxonomy, the abbreviation BMS stands for Battery Management System. It is the electronics that watch every cell, balance their charge, cut the pack off in faults and let the rest of the vehicle know what the battery is doing.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.4 Battery Management System (BMS) · Page: 3
"Battery Management System (BMS)"
Basic c-sme-020
Which three subtopics does SME group under Battery State Determination?
SME groups three subtopics under Battery State Determination: User Interface, Electrical Control and Safety Protection. Together they cover how the BMS tells the driver what is happening, how it controls the pack electrically and how it intervenes when something goes wrong.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.4.1 Battery State Determination · Page: 3
"Battery State Determination"
Basic c-sme-021
What does SME list as the basic items a BMS should monitor?
Under Battery Monitoring, SME lists Current, Voltage, Temperature and Data Acquisition as the items a BMS should track. These four signals together give the system enough information to judge battery health, performance and safety in real time during driving and charging.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.5 Battery Monitoring · Page: 3
"Temperature 3.5.4. Data Acquisition"
Indirect c-sme-022
Why does SME flag Thermal Management as High importance under Battery Monitoring?
Thermal Management is flagged as High importance because battery cells lose life or even catch fire if they run too hot. Keeping pack temperatures inside a narrow window is therefore a safety task, not just a comfort or performance tweak for the driver.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.5.6 Thermal Management · Page: 4
"3.5.6. Thermal Management"
Basic c-sme-023
What does SME call the section covering the EV's drive system?
SME calls the drive system the EV Traction or Propulsion System. It groups together the EV Motor, the Direct Current Motor and the Alternating Current Motor, since these are the main motor types that turn stored electrical energy into wheel rotation.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.6 EV Traction/Propulsion System · Page: 4
"EV Traction/Propulsion System"
Basic c-sme-024
What does the abbreviation SCR mean in SME's EV Speed and Power Controller topic?
In SME's EV Speed and Power Controller topic, the abbreviation SCR means Silicon-Controlled Rectifier. It is a solid-state switch used in power electronics to control how much current flows to the motor, and so how quickly the vehicle accelerates from rest.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.7 EV Speed and Power Controller · Page: 4
"Silicon-Controlled Rectifiers (SCR)"
Basic c-sme-025
Which two braking systems does SME list under EV Braking Systems?
SME lists two braking systems under EV Braking Systems: a Regenerative Braking System and a Traditional Braking System. EVs usually combine both, using the motor to slow the car and feed energy back to the battery, while friction brakes handle harder stops.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.8 EV Braking Systems · Page: 4
"Regenerative Braking System"
Basic c-sme-026
What does the abbreviation MCB mean under SME's EV Charging Station Components?
Under SME's EV Charging Station Components, MCB means Miniature Circuit Breaker. It is a small automatic switch that opens when too much current flows through it, protecting downstream wiring and chargers from overload or short-circuit damage if a fault occurs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.9 EV Charging Station Components · Page: 4
"Miniature Circuit Breakers (MCB)"
Basic c-sme-027
Why does SME mention Surge Protection Devices among charging station components?
SME lists Surge Protection Devices among the charging station components because power-line spikes from lightning or grid faults can destroy the sensitive electronics inside a charger. Surge protectors shunt that excess energy safely away before it ever reaches the charging unit.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.9.4 Surge Protection Devices · Page: 4
"Surge Protection Devices"
Basic c-sme-028
Which component does SME list as 3.10.4 in its EV Charging Systems table?
SME lists Onboard Charger as item 3.10.4 in its EV Charging Systems table. The onboard charger sits inside the vehicle and converts the alternating current from a wall socket into the direct current that the traction battery actually accepts during charging.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.10 EV Charging Systems and Technology · Page: 4
"3.10.4. Onboard Charger"
Basic c-sme-029
What does SME list as item 3.10.2 in EV Charging Systems and Technology?
SME lists DC to DC Converter as item 3.10.2. This converter takes the high-voltage direct current from the traction pack and steps it down to the lower voltages needed to run lights, infotainment and other onboard accessories on the vehicle.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.10 EV Charging Systems and Technology · Page: 4
"3.10.2. DC/DC Convertor"
Indirect c-sme-030
Why does the SME charging table include Thermal System as a charging component?
The charging table includes Thermal System because fast charging dumps large amounts of power into a pack and the resulting heat must be carried away. Without coolant flow the cells would overheat, throttle their charging speed and lose useful service life over time.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.10.5 Thermal System (Cooling) · Page: 4
"3.10.5. Thermal System (Cooling)"
Basic c-sme-031
Which three charging station tiers does SME describe at items 3.10.9 through 3.10.11?
Items 3.10.9 to 3.10.11 describe three charging station tiers: a Level 1 Charging Station, a Level 2 Charging Station and a Level 3 Charging Station. The tiers move from slow home outlets up to fast public chargers that refill a pack in minutes.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.10 EV Charging Systems and Technology · Page: 5
"3.10.11. Level 3 Charging Station"
Basic c-sme-032
What does SME include alongside the wired charger tiers in its charging-systems list?
Alongside the Level 1, 2 and 3 wired chargers, SME includes a Wireless Charging Station in the list. Wireless charging uses a coil in the ground and a matching coil under the car, transferring energy by magnetic induction with no cable plugged in.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 3. Components of Electric Vehicles · Section: 3.10.12 Wireless Charging Station · Page: 5
"3.10.12. Wireless Charging Station"
Basic c-sme-033
What weight does SME give to EV Manufacturing Processes in its curriculum?
SME gives EV Manufacturing Processes a weight of 10 percent of the curriculum. That share covers the practical shop methods, such as joining, welding, assembly and finishing, that physically turn raw parts into a finished and tested electric vehicle on the line.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 4. EV Manufacturing Processes · Section: — · Page: 5
"4. EV Manufacturing Processes 10%"
Basic c-sme-034
Which welding method does SME single out in its EV Manufacturing Processes section?
Within EV Manufacturing Processes, SME singles out Laser Welding Technology as its own subtopic at Medium importance. Laser welding is used heavily in EV manufacture for joining battery tabs and other small metal parts where precision and clean heat input really matter.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 4. EV Manufacturing Processes · Section: 4.3 Laser Welding Technology · Page: 5
"4.3. Laser Welding Technology"
Basic c-sme-035
Where does Adhesives appear in SME's manufacturing-processes list?
Adhesives appears as item 4.8 in SME's manufacturing-processes list, at Medium importance. Bonded joints made with structural glues are common in EV bodies, where they replace some welds and rivets to save weight and to seal joints against moisture and dust.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 4. EV Manufacturing Processes · Section: 4.8 Adhesives · Page: 5
"4.8. Adhesives"
Basic c-sme-036
How much weight does SME place on Robotics in its EV competency map?
SME places 15 percent of its total weight on Robotics in the EV competency map. That share equals Manufacturing Foundations, signalling that hands-on robot skills are now treated as a core element of modern EV production work alongside traditional craft skills.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: — · Page: 5
"5. Robotics 15%"
Basic c-sme-037
What does the SME taxonomy call a Cobot?
The SME taxonomy calls a Cobot a Collaborative Robot. Cobots are designed to share the same workspace with humans, slowing or stopping automatically on contact so operators can hand them parts or guide them without being shut behind a safety fence first.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: 5.1 Robot Types · Page: 5
"Collaborative Robots (Cobots)"
Basic c-sme-038
What does SCARA stand for in SME's robot-types list?
In SME's robot-types list, SCARA stands for Selective Compliance Assembly Robot Arm. It is a four-axis arm that is stiff vertically but able to swing freely in the horizontal plane, making it popular for high-speed pick-and-place assembly tasks on production lines.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: 5.1.4 SCARA · Page: 5
"Selective Compliance Assembly Robot Arm (SCARA)"
Basic c-sme-039
What name does SME give to a Delta-style robot in its taxonomy?
SME gives the Delta-style robot the formal name Parallel Robot in its taxonomy, listed at item 5.1.10. Parallel robots use several linked arms moving the same end effector, giving very high speed and stiffness over a relatively small working volume.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: 5.1.10 Parallel Robot (Delta Robot) · Page: 5
"Parallel Robot (Delta Robot)"
Basic c-sme-040
What does SME describe as a Light Curtain in its robot-safety list?
SME describes a Light Curtain as a presence-sensing safety device in its robot-safety list. It is a wall of invisible infrared beams across an opening, and if anything breaks the beams the nearby robot stops immediately, replacing a physical fence in many cells.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: 5.2 Types of Safety Devices & Barriers · Page: 6
"5.2.8. Light Curtain"
Basic c-sme-041
What does an e-stop do, according to SME's robot-safety list?
According to SME's robot-safety list, an e-stop is an emergency stop button. Pressing one immediately cuts power or motion to a robot or cell, giving operators a fast, single-action way to halt a machine if something dangerous is unfolding on the floor.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: 5.2.7 e-stops · Page: 6
"5.2.7. e-stops"
Basic c-sme-042
Which standards bodies does SME list under Robot Safety Guidelines and Standards Awareness?
SME lists OSHA, ANSI/RIA, ISO, UL, IEC and NIOSH under Robot Safety Guidelines and Standards Awareness. Learners are expected to know that several different bodies set complementary rules covering workplace safety, robot-specific design and electrical-product certification of equipment.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: 5.5 Robot Safety Guidelines & Standards Awareness · Page: 6
"OSHA, ANSI/RIA, ISO, UL, IEC, NIOSH"
Basic c-sme-043
Which four kinds of robot accidents does SME list under Types of Accidents Caused by Robots?
SME lists four kinds of robot accidents: Impact or Collision, Trapping, Crushing and Equipment-related. Together these capture the main ways a human can be hurt by an industrial arm, whether by being struck, pinned, squashed or hit by malfunctioning tooling parts.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 5. Robotics · Section: 5.5.2 Types of Accidents Caused by Robots · Page: 6
"Impact/Collison 5.5.2.2. Trapping"

What weight does SME give to Additive Manufacturing in its EV curriculum?
SME gives Additive Manufacturing a small weight of 5 percent in its EV curriculum. The section is mostly Low importance and Remember and Understand, because three-dimensional printed parts are still a niche use in mass EV production rather than a mainstream method.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge

Basic c-sme-045
How much weight does SME give to Lean Manufacturing in its EV curriculum?
SME gives Lean Manufacturing a weight of 2.5 percent in its EV curriculum. Although the share is small, the section covers core efficiency ideas such as 5S principles, the seven forms of waste and continuous improvement that every modern factory expects.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge

Basic c-sme-046
What do the five S's of SME's Lean Manufacturing principle stand for?
The five S's of SME's Lean Manufacturing principle stand for Sort, Set in Order, Sweep, Standardize and Sustain. They form a workplace organisation routine that keeps tools, parts and information arranged so workers can find what they need without wasted motion.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 7. Lean Manufacturing · Section: 7.1.1 5S Principles · Page: 7
"5S Principles (Sort, Set in Order, Sweep, Standardize, Sustain)"
Basic c-sme-047
What does TQM stand for in SME's Quality section?
In SME's Quality section, TQM stands for Total Quality Management. It is the broader management approach in which every department, not just inspection, is held responsible for delivering products that meet customer expectations the first time, every time, on every build.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 8. Quality · Section: 8.1 Total Quality Management (TQM) · Page: 7
"Total Quality Management (TQM)"
Basic c-sme-048
What is Metrology, as used in SME's Quality section?
Metrology, as used in SME's Quality section at item 8.4, is the science of measurement itself. Trainees are expected to understand how measuring tools are calibrated, traced to standards and used so that inspection results are accurate and trustworthy on every part.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 8. Quality · Section: 8.4 Metrology · Page: 7
"8.4. Metrology"
Indirect c-sme-049
Why does SME treat Effective Communication and Working in Teams as Essential Skills?
SME treats Effective Communication and Working in Teams as Essential Skills because EV production lines mix electricians, mechanics, robot programmers and quality staff. Without clear handoffs and shared language, even small misunderstandings can cause expensive defects or serious workplace safety incidents.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge
Chapter: 9. Essential Skills · Section: 9.1 Effective Communication / 9.2 Working in Teams · Page: 7
"9.1. Effective Communication"

Which two SME sections together account for almost half of the EV competency weights?
The Components of Electric Vehicles section at 25 percent and the Electric Vehicle Overview section at 20 percent together account for 45 percent of SME's weights, just under half. The combined share signals that EV-specific content is the curriculum's main centre of gravity.
Source: Electric Vehicle Body of Knowledge

4. Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)

Prateek Joshi & Carishma Gokhale-Welch · National Renewable Energy Laboratory (NREL) · 50 Q&As

Basic c-nrel-fund-001
Who authored the NREL Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles slide deck?
The NREL Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles slide deck was authored by Prateek Joshi and Carishma Gokhale-Welch of the National Renewable Energy Laboratory in November 2022. It was prepared as a primer rather than a fully comprehensive reference on every EV topic.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: Front matter · Section: — · Page: 2
"Prateek Joshi and Carishma Gokhale-Welch National Renewable Energy Laboratory November 2022"
Basic c-nrel-fund-002
Which university first hosted the course that produced this NREL slide deck?
The course that produced this NREL slide deck was first hosted by the Bangladesh University of Engineering and Technology, abbreviated BUET, in October 2022. It was an Energy Fundamentals Course aimed at postgraduates and working professionals from Bangladesh's energy sector.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: Front matter · Section: — · Page: 2
"Energy Fundamentals Course hosted by the Bangladesh University of Engineering and Technology (BUET)"
Basic c-nrel-fund-003
Which US agency partnered with NREL to organise the EV fundamentals course?
The United States Agency for International Development, known as USAID, partnered with NREL to help organise the course. The collaboration was meant to share US EV knowledge with engineering students and professionals in countries that are still building out their electric transport markets.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: Front matter · Section: — · Page: 2
"partnership with the United States Agency for International Development (USAID)"
Basic c-nrel-fund-004
What four top-level topics does the NREL EV fundamentals deck cover?
The NREL EV fundamentals deck covers four top-level topics: EV Trends, EV Technology, EV Charging and EV Policies. Each section breaks down further into either global and regional trends, vehicle types and opportunities, charging infrastructure and grid impact, or policy options and case studies.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: Table of Contents · Section: — · Page: 3
"1. EV Trends 2. EV Technology 3. EV Charging 4. EV Policies"
Basic c-nrel-fund-005
What two scales of EV trends does NREL break out in this deck?
NREL breaks out two scales of EV trends in this deck: global trends and regional trends. The split lets the deck show the world-wide picture of EV adoption first, then zoom in on country-by-country dynamics that vary a lot from one market to another.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: — · Page: 5
"a. Global trends b. Regional trends"
Basic c-nrel-fund-006
What time span does NREL's chart of global electric passenger car stock cover?
NREL's chart of global electric passenger car stock covers the period from 2011 to 2021, a decade in which the worldwide fleet of plug-in cars grew from a handful of pilot deployments to millions of units. The figure is sourced from Bloomberg New Energy Finance.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Global Trends 2021 EV Stock · Page: 5
"Global electric passenger car stock, 2011-2021"
Basic c-nrel-fund-007
Through which year does NREL's Bloomberg projection of EV stock run?
NREL's Bloomberg projection of global electric passenger car stock runs out to 2040. By stretching the timeline this far the chart shows roughly where today's adoption curve is heading even though the actual year-by-year outcome will depend heavily on policy choices.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Global Trends Projection · Page: 6
"Global electric passenger car stock projection, 2022-2040"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-008
Why does NREL say EVs typically cost more upfront than internal-combustion cars?
NREL says EVs typically cost more upfront than internal-combustion cars because of the cost of the battery. The battery pack is the most expensive single component on the vehicle, so until pack prices come down, sticker prices stay above an equivalent petrol car's.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Cost Declines in Batteries · Page: 7
"Higher upfront cost of most EVs compared to internal combustion engine (ICE) counterpart is due to cost of battery"
Basic c-nrel-fund-009
By how much have EV battery pack prices fallen since 2010, according to NREL?
EV battery pack prices have fallen 89 percent since 2010, according to NREL, despite recent supply-chain disruption. That long-running drop is the single biggest reason that EVs have moved from niche vehicles to mainstream products over little more than a decade in real terms.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Cost Declines in Batteries · Page: 7
"Battery pack prices have fallen 89% since 2010"
Basic c-nrel-fund-010
When does NREL expect EVs to reach unsubsidised price parity with ICE cars?
NREL expects EVs to reach unsubsidised upfront price parity with internal-combustion cars in most vehicle segments and markets by the late 2020s. Until then, government incentives are what bridges the gap for many buyers comparing sticker prices on the showroom floor.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Charging Infrastructure Expansion · Page: 8
"Unsubsidized upfront price parity expected in most vehicle segments and markets by the late 2020s"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-011
Why does NREL argue that EVs are already cheaper to own over their lifetime?
NREL argues EVs are already cheaper to own over their lifetime because they have lower fuel and maintenance expenses than the internal-combustion equivalent. Electricity per mile costs less than petrol, and an electric drivetrain has far fewer moving parts that need servicing as it ages.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Total cost of ownership · Page: 8
"lifetime operational cost of owning EVs is typically lower than the ICE counterpart due to reduced fuel and maintenance expenses"
Basic c-nrel-fund-012
By how much did public EV charging stations grow between 2015 and 2021?
Public EV charging stations grew by 40 percent between 2015 and 2021, according to NREL. The expansion was uneven across countries but shows that public infrastructure has been catching up with rising EV sales, particularly along major travel corridors and in cities.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Expansion of Charging Infrastructure · Page: 8
"40% increase in publicly available charging stations between 2015 and 2021"
Basic c-nrel-fund-013
What was the 2021 global average ratio of EVs to public charging points?
The 2021 global average was 10 EVs per public charging point. That ratio shows how heavily today's public network is shared, and it is one of the headline numbers used to track whether infrastructure is keeping up with vehicle adoption across the world.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Expansion of Charging Infrastructure · Page: 8
"2021 global average: 10 EVs per charging point"
Basic c-nrel-fund-014
What does Bloomberg project for EVs per ultra-fast charger by 2040?
Bloomberg projects between 100 and 300 EVs per ultra-fast charger by 2040, NREL reports. That much higher ratio than today reflects the expectation that drivers will charge at home most of the time and visit public ultra-fast chargers only on longer trips.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Regional Trends · Page: 9
"100-300 EVs per ultra-fast charger"
Basic c-nrel-fund-015
What 2030 EV sales target does India have for passenger cars?
India has set a 2030 EV sales target of 30 percent for passenger cars. That figure sits inside a wider national plan that also covers commercial vehicles and the smaller two- and three-wheelers that account for most road vehicles sold in India.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Regional Trends - India · Page: 9
"30% passenger cars"
Basic c-nrel-fund-016
What 2030 EV sales target does India have for commercial vehicles and two- or three-wheelers?
India targets 70 percent of commercial vehicle sales and 80 percent of two- and three-wheeler sales being electric by 2030. The higher share for small vehicles reflects how dominant scooters and rickshaws are in Indian traffic, and how readily they can be electrified.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Regional Trends - India · Page: 9
"70% commercial vehicles, and 80% of twoand three-wheelers"

What 2030 sales pledge has Toyota made for electrified vehicles?
Toyota has pledged that EVs will make up 40 percent of its annual sales by 2030, according to NREL. The figure includes the company's full range of battery and other electrified vehicles and is one example of the targets major automakers have published.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 1. EV Trends · Section: Regional Trends - Manufacturers · Page: 9
"Toyota: EVs constitute 40% of annual sales by 2030"

How many EV models is Honda planning by 2030, per NREL's notes?
Honda is planning 30 EV models and production of 2 million units by 2030, per NREL's notes. Combined with similar pledges from Nissan, who aims for 50 percent EV and hybrid sales by 2030, Japan's major automakers have set notable electrification targets in their respective announcements.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)

Basic c-nrel-fund-019
What does NREL list as the third top-level topic in this fundamentals deck?
NREL lists EV Charging as the third top-level topic in this fundamentals deck, after EV Trends and EV Technology and before EV Policies. The charging section is broken down further into charging infrastructure and the impact charging has on the electricity grid.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: Section roadmap · Section: — · Page: 11
"3. EV Charging"
Basic c-nrel-fund-020
How does NREL define a Hybrid Electric Vehicle in the drive-train slide?
NREL defines a Hybrid Electric Vehicle as a vehicle with an internal-combustion engine and an electric motor whose batteries are charged by the engine itself. There is no external charging port, so the driver tops it up only at a petrol pump.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Electric Drive Trains · Page: 12
"Hybrid Electric Vehicle"
Basic c-nrel-fund-021
What separates a Plug-in Hybrid Electric Vehicle from a Hybrid Electric Vehicle, per NREL?
A Plug-in Hybrid Electric Vehicle keeps both an internal-combustion engine and an electric motor, but its batteries are rechargeable from an external source. That extra charging option lets it drive on electricity alone for short trips before the engine has to step in.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Electric Drive Trains · Page: 12
"Plug-in Hybrid Electric Vehicle"
Basic c-nrel-fund-022
How does NREL describe a Battery Electric Vehicle in the drive-train slide?
NREL describes a Battery Electric Vehicle as a 100 percent electric motor driven vehicle whose batteries are rechargeable from an external source. With no internal-combustion engine on board, all of the energy used to move the vehicle has to come from the battery pack.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Electric Drive Trains · Page: 12
"Battery Electric Vehicle"
Basic c-nrel-fund-023
How is a Fuel Cell Electric Vehicle different in NREL's drive-train slide?
A Fuel Cell Electric Vehicle in NREL's drive-train slide is 100 percent electric motor driven, but its electricity comes from a fuel cell that converts hydrogen and oxygen into power. The car requires a hydrogen distribution infrastructure to refuel, which is still thin in most countries today.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Electric Drive Trains · Page: 12
"Fuel cell converts hydrogen and oxygen into electricity"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-024
Why does NREL say vehicle fleets are well suited to electrification?
NREL says vehicle fleets such as taxis, three-wheeler services and delivery vans are well suited to electrification because they have high kilometres travelled, fixed routes and predictable schedules. Those traits squeeze the most savings out of lower running costs and reduce the need for fast charging.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Fleet Electrification · Page: 12
"High vehicle-kilometers-traveled, fixed-route operation, and predictable schedules"
Basic c-nrel-fund-025
Which four EV benefits does NREL highlight on its opportunities slide?
NREL highlights reduced maintenance and fuel costs, increased fuel efficiency, reduced greenhouse gas emissions and economic and job opportunities as four EV benefits on its opportunities slide. The list captures both wallet-level savings and broader societal gains that policymakers care about.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Opportunities · Page: 13
"Reduced maintenance Increased fuel Reduced greenhouse Economic and job"
Basic c-nrel-fund-026
What four extra EV benefits round out NREL's opportunities slide?
Rounding out NREL's opportunities slide are zero tailpipe emissions with improved air quality, falling battery costs, enhanced energy security and performance benefits such as quiet operation. Together these complement the cost and emissions benefits already listed on the same slide.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Opportunities · Page: 13
"Zero tailpipe Falling costs for Enhanced energy Performance benefits"
Basic c-nrel-fund-027
Which five EV challenges does NREL list on its challenges slide?
NREL lists five EV challenges: increased electricity demand, higher upfront costs for some segments, charging infrastructure buildout, access to critical minerals for batteries and workforce development. Each of these has to be managed for EV adoption to scale smoothly across an economy in practice.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Challenges · Page: 14
"Increased electricity demand Higher upfront costs for some segments Charging infrastructure buildout Access to critical minerals for batteries Workforce development"
Basic c-nrel-fund-028
What does the acronym NZE stand for in NREL's projection scenarios?
In NREL's projection scenarios on the challenges slide, NZE stands for the net zero emissions by 2050 scenario. It sits alongside STEPS, the stated policies scenario, and APS, the announced pledges scenario. All three describe different futures for electricity demand and EV uptake.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 2. EV Technology · Section: Scenarios · Page: 14
"NZE: net zero emissions by 2050 scenario STEPS: stated policies scenario APS: announced pledges scenario"
Basic c-nrel-fund-029
What four purposes does NREL list for any type of EV charging station?
NREL lists four purposes for any EV charging station: connecting the EV to the grid, providing a dedicated circuit so the wiring is not overloaded, ensuring a safe connection before power flows and preventing damage to the EV battery during the charging cycle.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Purpose of Charging Stations · Page: 17
"Connects EV to grid Dedicated circuit prevents overloading Safe connection before power can flow Prevents EV battery damage"
Basic c-nrel-fund-030
What share of charging events typically happens at home, per NREL?
Per NREL, internationally 50 to 80 percent of all charging events happen at home. That dominance is why most established EV markets focused on residential charging first, and why a lack of home-charging availability is often called a barrier to wider EV adoption.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Residential Charging · Page: 17
"50%-80% of all charging events occurred at residences"
Basic c-nrel-fund-031
What does NREL abbreviate as EVSE in the residential charging slide?
In the residential charging slide, NREL abbreviates EVSE as Electric Vehicle Supply Equipment. It is the formal name for the cordset, wallbox or post that delivers electricity to a vehicle. Residential charging can use either Level 1 or Level 2 EVSE depending on outlet type.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Residential Charging · Page: 17
"Residential charging can use Level 1 or Level 2 EV supply equipment (EVSEs)"
Basic c-nrel-fund-032
How fast is Level 2 EVSE charging, per NREL's charging speed slide?
Per NREL's charging-speed slide, a Level 2 EVSE adds about 16 to 32 kilometres per hour of charging. The exact speed is often limited by the vehicle's onboard charger, but a typical rating is 7.2 kilowatts at 240 volts of alternating current.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Charging speeds · Page: 18
"Level 2 EVSE 16–32 km per hour of charging"
Basic c-nrel-fund-033
How fast can a DC fast charger replenish an EV, per NREL?
Per NREL, a DC fast charger can replenish 95 to 128 kilometres of range per hour of charging at a typical rating of 50 kilowatts and 480 to 600 volts direct current. The top end of today's units now reaches up to 350 kilowatts of power.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Charging speeds · Page: 18
"DC Fast Charger 95–128 km per hour of charging"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-034
Why does NREL note that DC fast chargers are incompatible with many two- and three-wheelers?
NREL notes DC fast chargers are incompatible with many two- and three-wheelers because those small vehicles use lower-voltage battery systems that cannot accept the high-power DC output. They are also too small to need that speed, so the equipment cost would not be justified.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: DC Fast Charger · Page: 18
"Incompatible with many 2and 3-wheelers"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-035
Why does NREL say battery swapping is more compatible with renewable energy than wired EVSE?
NREL says battery swapping is more compatible with renewable energy than wired EVSE because packs can be charged whenever wind or solar output is high and held until a rider needs one. The vehicle does not have to wait at the station while charging happens.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Battery Swapping · Page: 19
"More compatible with renewables than EVSE"
Basic c-nrel-fund-036
Which three battery-swap network operators does NREL name?
NREL names three large battery-swap network operators: Gogoro in Taiwan, Immotor in China and KYMCO also in Taiwan. Their networks let scooter riders trade a depleted pack for a charged one at a kiosk in less time than it takes to refuel a petrol scooter.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Battery Swapping · Page: 19
"Largest networks operated by Gogoro (Taiwan), Immotor (China), KYMCO (Taiwan)"
Basic c-nrel-fund-037
Which four motorcycle makers does NREL say have formed a swappable battery consortium?
NREL says Honda, KTM, Piaggio and Yamaha have formed a swappable battery consortium to agree common standards. A shared standard means a single pack design can fit different brands of scooter, which makes swap stations more useful and helps the technology scale.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Battery Swapping · Page: 19
"Honda, KTM, Piaggio, and Yamaha have formed a swappable battery consortium"
Basic c-nrel-fund-038
Which charging standard does NREL list for North America?
NREL lists SAE J1772 as North America's charging standard. It uses a 5-pin alternating-current port known as Type 1 for slower charging, and pairs with a 7-pin direct-current port called the Combined Charging Standard 1, abbreviated CCS1, for fast charging.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Common Standards · Page: 20
"SAE J1772 – North America"
Basic c-nrel-fund-039
What standard family does NREL list for Europe and emerging markets?
NREL lists IEC 61851 and IEC 62196 as Europe and emerging markets' charging standards. They use a 7-pin alternating-current port called Type 2 for slower charging and a 9-pin direct-current port called the Combined Charging Standard 2, or CCS2, for faster charging.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Common Standards · Page: 20
"IEC 61851/62196 Europe and emerging markets"
Basic c-nrel-fund-040
Which charging standards does India accept, according to NREL?
According to NREL, India accepts a mix of charging standards: Bharat Standards for low-power charging, CCS, CCS2, CHAdeMO and Tesla. The variety reflects that India imports vehicles from many regions and is still settling on which standards its public network should converge on.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Standards in India · Page: 21
"India has Bharat Standards (low power), CCS, CCS2, CHAdeMO, and Tesla"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-041
Why does NREL describe parked cars as underutilised assets for the grid?
NREL describes parked cars as underutilised assets because vehicles in the United States sit parked roughly 95 percent of the time. That long idle window means an EV plugged in for hours could deliver grid services, like absorbing solar peaks or supporting renewable integration.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Managing Grid Impacts · Page: 22
"Parked \~95% of the time (in United States)"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-042
Why does NREL argue that EVs are not just a burden to the grid?
NREL argues EVs are not just a burden to the grid because flexible charging can satisfy a driver's mobility needs while also supporting the grid and the integration of renewable energy. Flexibility is secondary to mobility but is enabled by the right charging infrastructure choices.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 3. EV Charging · Section: Managing Grid Impacts · Page: 22
"flexible EV charging can satisfy mobility needs while also supporting the grid and integration of renewable energy"
Medium c-nrel-fund-043
Which incentive does NREL's effectiveness table say boosts US plug-in EV purchases most?
In NREL's effectiveness table, high-occupancy vehicle lane access is the strongest lever, lifting plug-in EV per-capita purchases by 8.3 percent. Rebates of $1,000 raise sales 4.8 percent, sales tax waivers 3.6 percent and a $1,000 tax credit 2.3 percent by comparison.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 4. EV Policies · Section: EV Purchase Incentives: Effectiveness in the United States · Page: 25
"High-occupancy vehicle lane access"
Basic c-nrel-fund-044
How much funding does India's FAME II programme commit to EV purchase incentives?
India's FAME II programme commits $1.4 billion in EV purchase incentives for 1.6 million electric vehicles and hybrids between 2019 and 2024. The programme also includes $133 million for charging infrastructure and direct subsidies for nearly 6,000 electric buses so far.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 4. EV Policies · Section: Case Study: India · Page: 26
"Purchase incentives of \$1.4B USD for 1.6M EVs and hybrids"
Indirect c-nrel-fund-045
Why does NREL say India's EV adoption is running behind its FAME II schedule?
NREL says India's EV adoption is running behind the FAME II schedule possibly because the country has no zero-emission vehicle sales requirements or ICE phase-out targets. Industry voices also blame aggressive localisation rules set before the market was large enough to absorb them.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 4. EV Policies · Section: Case Study: India · Page: 26
"Possibly due to no zero-emission vehicle sales requirements or ICE phase-out targets"
Basic c-nrel-fund-046
How many EVs and public chargers does NREL list for Barbados?
NREL lists 430 EVs on the road in Barbados, served by 45 public chargers and 200 private chargers. Those figures give the country the highest number of EVs per capita in the Caribbean despite being a small island state with a modest total vehicle fleet.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 4. EV Policies · Section: Case Study: Barbados · Page: 27
"430 EVs on the road, 45 public chargers, 200 private chargers"
Basic c-nrel-fund-047
By how much did Barbados cut its EV import taxes?
Barbados cut its EV import taxes from 45 percent down to 10 percent, NREL reports. That steep drop is part of the country's pilot package alongside pilot projects, EV maintenance courses for technicians and an open charging-market policy that admits independent operators.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 4. EV Policies · Section: Case Study: Barbados · Page: 27
"Reduced import taxes on EVs (from 45% to 10%)"
Basic c-nrel-fund-048
How many EVs did New Zealand sell in 2021, per NREL's case study?
Per NREL's case study, New Zealand sold 10,574 EVs in 2021. The country's Emission Reduction Plan also promotes walking, cycling and public transit alongside EVs, signalling that electrification of cars is only one piece of the country's wider transport decarbonisation strategy.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 4. EV Policies · Section: Case Study: New Zealand · Page: 28
"10,574 EVs sold in 2021"
Basic c-nrel-fund-049
What emissions threshold defines a New Zealand Clean Car Discount Programme rebate?
Under New Zealand's Clean Car Discount Programme, vehicles emitting less than 146 grams of carbon dioxide per kilometre qualify for a rebate, while vehicles above that limit pay a fee. The scheme applies to both new and used vehicles and covers a wide market range.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)
Chapter: 4. EV Policies · Section: Case Study: New Zealand · Page: 28
"Rebates for vehicles (new and used) emitting less than 146 grams of CO2 per kilometer"
Medium c-nrel-fund-050
Which NREL reference does this deck cite for projecting US end-use electrification costs to 2050?
This deck cites the NREL Electrification Futures Study by Jadun and colleagues, published as report NREL/TP-6A20-70485 in 2017. That study projects end-use electric technology costs and performance through 2050 and is the source for several of the deck's electricity demand and battery cost figures.
Source: Fundamentals of Electric Vehicles (EVs)

"Electrification Futures Study: End-Use Electric Technology Cost and Performance Projections through 2050"

5. EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle

NREL · National Renewable Energy Laboratory (NREL) · 50 Q&As

Basic c-nrel-batt-001
Why are lithium-ion batteries currently the only choice for electric vehicle batteries?
Lithium-ion batteries are picked for EVs because they store a lot of energy and power for their size, last a long time, are built in modular packs, and have become relatively cheap. Other chemistries like lead-acid cannot match this combination of strengths in cars.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.1.2 Current Lithium-Ion Battery Technologies and Materials · Page: 13
"LIBs are the main choice for consumer electronics, electric-drive vehicles, and grid energy storage due to their high energy and power, longevity, modularity, and relatively low cost."
Basic c-nrel-batt-002
How large is a typical EV battery pack compared to a hybrid car battery?
Hybrid car batteries are small, holding only 0.6 to 1.4 kilowatt-hours of energy, while a full electric vehicle pack holds 40 to 100 kilowatt-hours. That means an EV pack stores roughly 30 to 150 times more energy than the battery in a typical hybrid.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: — · Page: 11
"These battery sizes range from 0.6–1.4 kWh, whereas an electric vehicle (EV) LIB size ranges from 40–100 kWh."
Indirect c-nrel-batt-003
Why is cobalt considered the highest supply risk for EV batteries?
Cobalt is the highest supply risk because reserves are limited, mining concentrates in just a few regions, and the practices used to extract it raise serious environmental and human-rights concerns. Prices can also spike unexpectedly, so manufacturers are racing to reduce or remove cobalt.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.1.3 Key Lithium-Ion Battery Materials · Page: 13
"Cobalt is the highest material supply risk for EVBs due to a variety of factors, including resource availability, mining practices, and environmental impact."
Basic c-nrel-batt-004
How much do annual lithium-ion battery demands forecast to reach by 2030?
BloombergNEF projects that the world will need over 2 terawatt-hours of lithium-ion batteries every year by 2030. To get a sense of scale, that is roughly twenty times more battery capacity than was used in 2020, driven mostly by EV adoption.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.1.1 Electric Vehicle Batteries · Page: 13
"Annual demand for LIBs is projected to exceed 2 TWh by 2030 (BloombergNEF 2019)."
Basic c-nrel-batt-005
What does end-of-life mean for an EV battery according to the United States Advanced Battery Consortium?
The US Advanced Battery Consortium defines end-of-life as the point where the battery has lost more than 20 percent of either its original capacity or its original power. Until that point, the pack is still considered fit to power a car normally.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.2 Second Life · Page: 19
"a battery reaches its end of life when it has lost more than 20% of capacity or power"
Basic c-nrel-batt-006
How long do EV manufacturers typically warranty their batteries for?
Most EV makers cover the battery under warranty for 8 to 10 years from purchase. During that period, the manufacturer takes responsibility for any needed repairs or replacements, giving the owner some financial assurance against early degradation or sudden failure of the pack.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.2 Second Life · Page: 19
"EV manufacturers provide battery warranties for 8–10 years (Najman 2021), taking responsibility for any repairs or replacements."
Indirect c-nrel-batt-007
Why might an EV battery last 12 to 16 years inside a car?
Carmakers build in a safety margin so the pack performs well even after some degradation. After the 8 to 10 year warranty, experts say batteries often keep working for another 2 to 6 years, giving a real-world life of roughly 12 to 16 years in the vehicle.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.2 Second Life · Page: 19
"EVBs can perform well for another 2–6 years beyond warranty, giving a battery life of 12–16 years in a vehicle"
Basic c-nrel-batt-008
What is a second-life battery?
A second-life battery is an EV battery that is no longer suitable for powering a car but still has enough capacity left to be useful elsewhere. They typically go into stationary energy storage applications such as backing up homes or the electricity grid for another decade.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.2.1 Second-Life Battery Market · Page: 19
"Second-life batteries are end-of-first-use EVBs that have use beyond that in a car"
Basic c-nrel-batt-009
How long can a second-life battery continue to operate after leaving its vehicle?
After being repurposed out of a car, a second-life battery can keep working for another 10 years or more in less demanding roles. Its remaining capacity is usually more than enough to support stationary energy storage uses such as renewable power buffering.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.2.1 Second-Life Battery Market · Page: 19
"the second-life battery can continue to work for another 10 years or more"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-010
Why might lithium iron phosphate batteries be a poor candidate for recycling today?
Lithium iron phosphate, or LFP, packs contain little to no nickel or cobalt in the cathode. Recovered iron has low market value, so the cost of recycling them often exceeds what the recovered materials are worth, leaving recyclers with a net loss.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.2.2 Value of Second-Life Batteries · Page: 19
"LIBs such as lithium iron phosphate batteries that have low or no nickel or cobalt content in the cathodes are usually of negative value when recycled"
Basic c-nrel-batt-011
Which battery safety standard covers second-life EV conversion to stationary storage?
Underwriters Laboratories created the UL 1974 standard specifically for second-life conversions, where used EV batteries are repurposed as stationary energy storage. Related standards include UL 1973 for the energy storage system itself and UL 9540a for fire prevention testing on those systems.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.2.3 Second-Life Battery Market Evolution and Challenges · Page: 19
"UL 1974 (second-life EV conversion to stationary energy storage), UL 9450 Energy Storage, and UL 9450a (fire prevention) protocols are very expensive"
Basic c-nrel-batt-012
What are the three main lithium-ion battery recycling technologies?
The three major recycling approaches are pyrometallurgy, which uses high-temperature smelting; hydrometallurgy, which uses chemical leaching with acids or other fluids; and direct recycling, which keeps the cathode material intact rather than breaking it down to elemental metals.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.3 End-of-Life Lithium-Ion Battery Recycling Technologies · Page: 19
"there are three major technologies currently in various stages of commercialization: pyrometallurgy, hydrometallurgy, and direct recycling"
Basic c-nrel-batt-013
What is pyrometallurgy in the context of battery recycling?
Pyrometallurgy is the high-temperature smelting of batteries in a furnace to pull out metals and intermediate compounds. The inputs can be whole batteries or shredded black mass, and the outputs are metal alloys and a glassy waste byproduct called slag.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.3.1 Pyrometallurgy · Page: 19
"Pyrometallurgy is the process of high-temperature thermal treatment of batteries in a furnace to extract metals and intermediate compounds"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-014
Why is lithium often lost in standard pyrometallurgical recycling?
During smelting, lighter impurities float to the top of the melted metal and form a layer called slag or dross. Lithium compounds, being light, end up trapped in this slag. The slag is poured off, so the lithium is usually discarded unless extra hydrometallurgical steps are added.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.3.1 Pyrometallurgy · Page: 19
"the dross also captures the much lighter (in terms of density) lithium compounds. The dross is then poured off"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-015
Why are hydrometallurgy plants considered easier to build than pyrometallurgy plants?
Hydrometallurgy uses chemical leaching at low temperatures rather than energy-hungry smelting, so the plants are smaller, use much less energy, and need less capital investment. Permitting tends to be simpler too, which speeds up construction in the United States and Canada.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.3.2 Hydrometallurgy · Page: 19
"Hydrometallurgical plants use much less energy than pyrometa llurgy plants. In addition, the plant size can be much smaller"
Basic c-nrel-batt-016
What is direct recycling of lithium-ion batteries?
Direct recycling recovers cathode material while keeping its chemical structure intact, instead of breaking it down into elemental metals and rebuilding the cathode from scratch. Skipping these steps makes it potentially the cheapest and lowest-carbon recycling route once mature.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.3.3 Direct Recycling · Page: 19
"Direct recycling involves recovery of cathode while maintaining its molecular structure, rather than breaking it down into constituent metals"
Basic c-nrel-batt-017
What share of total lithium-ion battery recycling cost comes from transportation?
Roughly half of the cost of recycling any kind of lithium-ion battery is spent on shipping. Batteries are bulky, heavy, and often classified as hazardous material, which forces special packing, low truckload counts, and long trips to scarce recycling facilities.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.4.2 Transportation Costs · Page: 23
"About 50% or more of the cost of recycling any type of LIB is transportation (Dai et al. 2019)"
Medium c-nrel-batt-018
How much cheaper is rail than truck for long-distance battery transport, and what emissions benefit does it bring?
In 2021, transcontinental rail shipping in the United States ran about 30 percent cheaper than equivalent truck routes. On a Los Angeles to Syracuse trip, rail also avoided around 4,410 pounds of greenhouse gas emissions, or about 1.6 pounds per mile.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.4.4 Reducing Transportation Costs and Impacts · Page: 23
"rail would prevent generation of about 4,410 pounds of greenhouse gas emissions compared to truck transit over the 2,768-mile trip, or 1.6 pounds of carbon dioxide per mile"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-019
What is thermal runaway in a lithium-ion battery?
Thermal runaway is a chain reaction inside a cell where heat triggers a chemical reaction that creates more heat, pushing temperatures higher in milliseconds. The cell can reach around 400 degrees Celsius and release its stored energy suddenly, often starting a fierce fire.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.2 Thermal Materials · Page: 23
"Thermal runaway is a chain reaction within a battery cell that can be very difficult to stop once it has started."
Basic c-nrel-batt-020
What temperature can a battery cell reach during thermal runaway?
A cell undergoing thermal runaway can hit temperatures of about 752 degrees Fahrenheit, which equals 400 degrees Celsius. Those temperatures cause the cell to release gases and can ignite a fire so hot it is nearly impossible to put out using normal methods.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.2 Thermal Materials · Page: 23
"This chain reaction creates extremely high temperatures (around 752°F, or 400°C)."
Medium c-nrel-batt-021
What fraction of total battery mass do the cells themselves account for, and why does that matter for recycling?
Cells make up 50 to 60 percent of the total mass of an EV battery pack. Because they hold most of the valuable cathode metals, recyclers focus on getting cells out cleanly. The rest of the pack mass is modules, casings, wiring, and electronics.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.1 Disassembly Constraints · Page: 23
"Modules Different electrical designs Cells (50-60% of total battery mass) Different mechanical designs High voltage bus bars"
Medium c-nrel-batt-022
How much of each metal can EU recyclers recover from a lithium-ion battery?
European Union figures suggest that hydrometallurgy or pyrometallurgy can recover up to 90 percent of cobalt, nickel, manganese, and aluminum from a lithium-ion battery, plus up to 35 percent of the lithium. Graphite recovery is also possible depending on the process.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.1 Disassembly Constraints · Page: 23
"Lithium (up to 35%) Additional challenges with cylindrical cells(unwinding spira sheets of cathode, node and separator) Cobalt (up to 90%)"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-023
Why do composite plastics make EV battery packs harder to recycle?
Polycarbonate blends used in packs are lightweight, stable, and often flame-retardant, but those very properties make them hard to break down back into original feedstock. They can hinder pack repair, cell reuse, and full recycling of plastics, though metals can still be recovered.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.3 Plastics & Composites · Page: 27
"these thermoplastics can help reduce battery weight and provide some thermal protection, unless carefully selected, these materials are often difficult or not practical to recycle to original materials"
Basic c-nrel-batt-024
What is a battery-as-a-service business model?
Under battery-as-a-service, you buy the car but not the battery. Instead, you pay the manufacturer or a battery company a monthly fee for the use of the pack. This lowers the upfront price of the EV and lets the owner handle replacement and end-of-life issues.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.6.1 Battery as a Service · Page: 27
"the consumer can purchase battery services from the vehicle OEM or battery asset company monthly rather than purchasing the battery with the car"
Medium c-nrel-batt-025
How much revenue can battery leasing add per vehicle, according to McKinsey?
The McKinsey Institute estimates that a successful battery leasing program could add more than 1,000 US dollars per vehicle in revenue over an assumed 5-year lease term. The model also gives the manufacturer ownership for second-life resale into stationary storage.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.6.2 Battery Leasing · Page: 27
"OEMs could add more than \$1,000 in revenue per vehicle through a successful battery leasing program during an assumed lease term of 5 years"
Basic c-nrel-batt-026
What is an environmental handling fee in EV battery management?
An environmental handling fee is a one-time recycling charge added to the price of a new EV. A third party holds the money and uses it later to pay for safely recycling the battery once it leaves the market, removing that worry from the manufacturer.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.6.3 Environmental Handling Fee · Page: 27
"This model puts the responsibility for recycling the battery on the user of the vehicle by charging them a fee at time of purchase"
Basic c-nrel-batt-027
What does a battery management system, or BMS, actually do?
A BMS is the brain of a rechargeable battery. It watches and controls how the cells charge and discharge, keeping the pack safe and healthy. In an EV, it shares vital data such as temperature, current, voltage, and state of charge with the car's diagnostics system.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.2.2 Accessing Battery SOH and SOC When the BMS Is Intact · Page: 35
"It controls and monitors the charge and discharge of rechargeable batteries in EVs, along with cellphones, laptops, and myriad consumer devices."
Indirect c-nrel-batt-028
What is coulomb counting and why is it slow for sorting used batteries?
Coulomb counting measures how much electric charge flows into and out of a cell during full charge-discharge cycles to find its remaining capacity. It is very accurate but needs one or two complete cycles, expensive lab gear, and trained operators, which adds time and cost.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.2.4 Battery State of Health Capture Outside the Vehicle · Page: 35
"coulomb counting, which essentially completes one to two complete charge/discharge cycles and measures the electrons in and electrons out"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-029
How does ultrasonic testing speed up grading of used EV batteries?
Ultrasonic testing uses sound waves to assess a cell's state of health in just a few seconds, matching the accuracy of lab-grade cycling equipment. Non-technical operators can run it, which dramatically lowers the cost of preparing used batteries for second-life applications.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.2.4 Battery State of Health Capture Outside the Vehicle · Page: 35
"a rapid battery testing technology has been developed using ultrasonic techniques that can perform SOH evaluation with a similar result to lab-grade cycling equipment within a few seconds"
Basic c-nrel-batt-030
What top three pieces of information did automakers and suppliers most want about used EV batteries?
The Suppliers Partnership survey found the most valuable information to be the battery's chemistry, the safety and disassembly instructions plus tools required, and the state of health. Knowing these three lets handlers move and process used packs safely and efficiently.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.1.1 Life Cycle Stakeholders Survey Results · Page: 30
"The top data points identified by responders in the SP survey were: 1. Chemistry 2. Key disassembly and safety instructions and tools required 3. State of health."
Basic c-nrel-batt-031
What is the Battery Passport concept promoted by the Global Battery Alliance?
The Battery Passport is a digital record system that securely shares information about each EV battery. It traces where minerals were sourced, tracks the battery through its life, and documents recycling and carbon footprint, giving every stakeholder verifiable data.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.4.3 Global Battery Alliance · Page: 40
"the Battery Passport, which would provide for securely sharing information and data to identify, validate and track EVB responsible sourcing of minerals"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-032
Why is private blockchain more practical than public blockchain for battery data sharing?
Public blockchains like Bitcoin require enormous computing power for mining. Private enterprise blockchains such as Hyperledger Fabric Raft do not, using around 10 billion times less energy per transaction. That makes them realistic for supply-chain traceability of batteries.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.3.2 Data Sharing Throughout Battery Life Cycles · Page: 35
"Hyperledger Fabric Raft, a type of blockchain framework supporting private solutions, uses 10 billion times less energy per transaction than Bitcoin"
Medium c-nrel-batt-033
How much did Chinese government invest in lithium battery industry buildout?
Chinese authorities spent somewhere between 60 and 100 billion US dollars over the past decade growing the domestic lithium-ion industry. The money subsidised cheap electric cars priced around 4,500 US dollars, mining infrastructure, and refining capacity, making China the global leader.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.4.2 Chinese Initiatives · Page: 40
"the Chinese government has spent somewhere between \$60 billion and \$100 billion increasing the domestic market for lithium batteries"
Basic c-nrel-batt-034
What does the Inflation Reduction Act offer buyers of qualifying EVs?
Under the 2022 US Inflation Reduction Act, an EV can earn 3,750 US dollars for meeting battery critical-minerals sourcing rules and another 3,750 US dollars for battery component assembly, up to 7,500 US dollars total. The previous 200,000-vehicle cap per automaker was removed.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.4.5 United States Government · Page: 40
"may be eligible for a tax credit of \$3,750 for critical minerals, \$3,750 for battery components assembly, or a total of up to \$7,500"
Basic c-nrel-batt-035
What is California's target for zero-emission new car sales by 2035?
California's Executive Order N-79-20 requires that 100 percent of in-state sales of new passenger cars and light-duty trucks must be zero-emission by 2035. The state also aims for fully zero-emission medium- and heavy-duty fleets by 2045, with drayage trucks shifting earlier.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.4.6 US State Governments · Page: 40
"100% of in-state sales of new passenger cars and light-duty trucks will be zero-emission by 2035"
Basic c-nrel-batt-036
What does China's GB/T 3404-2017 standard require of EV makers?
Under GB/T 3404-2017, Chinese EV manufacturers are legally responsible for both recycling end-of-life batteries and judging whether they are suitable for second-life use. The standard also defines codes for tracing packs, modules, and cells through their entire life.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.5.1 China Producer Responsibility · Page: 40
"electric vehicle OEMs are legally responsible for both battery recycling and assessment of second-life potential"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-037
What does the German Battery Act require manufacturers to do when an EV battery is replaced?
Under the German Battery Act, which took effect on 1 January 2021, the carmaker must take back drive batteries at no charge whenever a pack falls below its guaranteed minimum capacity. The law also allows that battery to be reused in a second-life application instead of disposed.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.5.3 German Battery Act · Page: 46
"manufacturers of electric cars take batteries back from their vehicles at no charge or appoint a disposal partner"
Basic c-nrel-batt-038
What is California's Lithium-Ion Car Battery Recycling Advisory Group trying to achieve?
Formed in 2019 under Assembly Bill 2832, this group advises California's legislature with the aim of reusing or recycling as close to 100 percent as possible of every lithium-ion vehicle battery sold in the state, safely and at reasonable cost.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.5.5 California Environmental Protection Agency · Page: 46
"the goal of ensuring that as close to 100% as possible of lithium-ion vehicle batteries in the state are reused or recycled at end of life"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-039
Why did Massachusetts voters approve the 2020 Right to Repair law for vehicles?
Massachusetts voters backed expanded Right to Repair by 75 percent to 25 percent in November 2020. The law forces carmakers to share telematics data with vehicle owners and independent garages so they can diagnose and repair modern, electronics-heavy cars from 2022 onward.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.5.6 Massachusetts Right to Repair · Page: 46
"law by a margin of 75% to open car data to vehicle owners and garages"
Basic c-nrel-batt-040
What is RAIN RFID and how is it relevant to battery tracking?
RAIN RFID is an ultra-high-frequency radio-frequency identification tag standard that lets readers scan items wirelessly without batteries inside the tag. It is already widely used in the automotive industry for tyre tracking and is being explored for tagging EV battery packs.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.3.1 IoT Enabling Batteries and Critical Parts · Page: 35
"a radio frequency identification (RFID) or ultrahigh frequency RFID (RAIN) tag using various standards (either battery-assisted or passive)"
Basic c-nrel-batt-041
What is black mass in battery recycling?
Black mass is the dark, powdery material left after a lithium-ion cell is shredded, sieved, and separated from its casing and components. It contains the valuable cathode and anode materials, and recyclers refine it further using chemical or thermal methods to recover metals.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: Glossary · Section: — · Page: 47
"A mixture of grounded constituents of a lithium-ion battery cell after shredding, sieving, and separation."
Basic c-nrel-batt-042
What does the term digital twin mean for an EV battery?
A digital twin is a virtual representation of a physical battery and its components. It mirrors the real pack's identity, configuration, and condition in software, letting stakeholders query the asset's history and status without having to open or test the hardware itself.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: Glossary · Section: — · Page: 47
"In terms of electric vehicle batteries, a digital representation of the and components. battery"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-043
Why was nickel-metal-hydride battery recycling left out of the report's main scope?
Nickel-metal-hydride packs are tiny next to EV batteries and are already being refurbished and resold for hybrid use. The authors focus on lithium-ion batteries because, with the EV boom, the volume of end-of-life lithium-ion packs will dwarf the nickel-metal-hydride stream.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: — · Page: 11
"with large EV market penetration, the amount of end-of-life LIB would be much larger than those of NiMH batteries"
Medium c-nrel-batt-044
Which two lithium-ion cathode chemistries today generate positive recycling value?
Of five common cathode types, only two generally pay recyclers more than they cost to process: lithium cobalt oxide, known as LCO, and the nickel-rich mixes lithium nickel manganese cobalt oxide, or NMC, and lithium nickel cobalt aluminum oxide, or NCA, which earn positive value.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.4.1 Value or Cost? · Page: 20
"Positive Value Pricing</td></tr><tr><td>Cathode Acronym</td><td>Cathode Name and General Formulation"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-045
Why does the design of EV battery packs make them hard to disassemble for recycling?
Each carmaker builds packs differently in electrical layout, mechanical layout, and cell shape, so recyclers face non-uniform designs every time. Add sealed adhesives, rusted bolts, lack of labelling, and unknown chemistries, and stripping a pack safely becomes slow and costly.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.1 Disassembly Constraints · Page: 23
"non-uniformity in the design of battery packs isa challnge while disassembling battery packs for recycling"
Basic c-nrel-batt-046
What kind of bath chemistry is being developed to free cells from glued battery packs?
Researchers have developed a bath of swelling agents that soaks into glued cells. The chemistry makes urethane, acrylic, silicone, and epoxy adhesives expand until the bond breaks. Cells then pop free without manual prying, and the recycling solution can be reused many times.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.4 New Dismantling Solvents & Solutions · Page: 27
"These innovative materials swell the engineered adhesives (urethanes, acrylics, silicone, and epoxies) until the internal stresses within the base polymer exceed its bonding force"
Medium c-nrel-batt-047
How much new battery cathode material will global manufacturers need by 2030?
In 2020, lithium-ion batteries consumed about 400,000 tons of cathode material worldwide. By 2030 that figure is projected to climb to roughly 1.2 million tons each year, a tripling that reflects the explosion of EV demand and grid storage needs.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.1.1 Electric Vehicle Batteries · Page: 13
"In 2020, 400,000 tons of cathode materials were used in LIBs, a number that is projected to rise to about 1.2 million tons by 2030"
Basic c-nrel-batt-048
What does the European Commission's proposed Batteries Regulation include for recycled content?
The proposed EU Batteries Regulation would require manufacturers to declare how much recycled material their new batteries contain starting in 2025. Then, mandatory minimum percentages of recycled content for cells will phase in, rising in 2030 and increasing again in 2035.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 1 Reuse, Recycle, and Reimage · Section: 1.5.4 New Dismantling Solvents & Solutions · Page: 27
"requirements to declare levels of recycled content in batteries by 2025 and increase the levels required in 2030 and again in 2035"
Indirect c-nrel-batt-049
What did US auto recyclers value most highly when handling end-of-life EV batteries?
An Institute of Scrap Recycling Industries member survey found that 84 percent of auto recyclers rated safe-handling and removal information as extremely valuable. Market data ranked second and a battery's condition or state of charge ranked third, ahead of vehicle make and model.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: 2 Regulations, Initiatives, and Stakeholders Perspectives · Section: 2.1.1 Life Cycle Stakeholders Survey Results · Page: 31
"Sample Survey Results From Institute of Scrap Recycling Industries Members on the Value of Information About EVB Attributes"
Basic c-nrel-batt-050
Who founded the EverBatt model used to study battery recycling cost and impact?
EverBatt is a closed-loop battery recycling cost and environmental impacts model developed at Argonne National Laboratory and published as report ANL-19/16 by Dai and colleagues in 2019. Researchers use it to compare the costs and emissions of different recycling pathways.
Source: EV Li-Ion Battery Lifecycle
Chapter: References · Section: — · Page: 54
"EverBatt: A Closed-loop Battery Recycling Cost and Environmental Impacts Model. Lemont, IL: Argonne National Laboratory. ANL -19/16."

6. eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design

NREL · National Renewable Energy Laboratory (NREL) · 50 Q&As

Basic c-nrel-chip-001
What does the eCHIP acronym stand for in this NREL project?
eCHIP stands for the High-Power Electric Vehicle Charging Hub Integration Platform. It is a US Department of Energy funded project that builds an experimental testbed for direct-current, distribution-based fast charging hubs, run jointly by NREL, Argonne, and Oak Ridge labs.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: Executive Summary · Section: — · Page: 11
"the High-Power Electric Vehicle Charging Hub Integration Platform (eCHIP) project aims to create an experimental platform for integration and control approaches"
Basic c-nrel-chip-002
Which three US national laboratories collaborate on the eCHIP project?
The eCHIP project is run jointly by three national laboratories. The National Renewable Energy Laboratory, known as NREL, leads the integration testbed, Argonne National Laboratory handles the communication module, and Oak Ridge National Laboratory builds the high-power DC-DC charger module.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 1 Introduction · Section: — · Page: 11
"The eCHIP project is a multiyear effort conducted by Argonne National Laboratory (Argonne), National Renewable Energy Laboratory (NREL), and Oak Ridge National Laboratory (ORNL)"
Basic c-nrel-chip-003
What is the DC bus voltage used in the eCHIP testbed?
The eCHIP testbed operates on a 950-volt direct-current bus voltage. The bus links the grid-tied inverter to the various DC chargers, energy storage emulator, photovoltaic emulator, and building load emulator that together make up the integrated charging hub.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: Executive Summary · Section: — · Page: 11
"The important hardware ratings used within the scope of this report include 950-V DC bus voltage"
Basic c-nrel-chip-004
How powerful is the central inverter used in the eCHIP charging hub?
The grid-tied inverter inside the eCHIP testbed is rated for 660 kilowatts of power. It converts the alternating current from the utility grid into the direct current used by the chargers, storage, and emulated solar generation on the hub.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: Executive Summary · Section: — · Page: 11
