"a 660-kW grid-tied inverter, a 150-kW COTS charger, a 175-kW in-house developed DC-DC charger"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-005
Why is a DC-coupled charging hub more efficient than an AC-coupled one when batteries and solar are added?
Batteries, solar panels, and EV chargers all run natively on direct current. A DC hub links them with fewer conversion stages, since each device needs only one isolated DC-DC step rather than the multiple AC-DC and DC-AC stages an AC hub requires.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.1 DC Hub vs. AC Hub · Page: 13
"the EV chargers, energy storage, and PV sys­ tems can all connect to the bus with a single, isolated DC-DC conversion stage"
Basic c-nrel-chip-006
What voltage range do modern EV battery packs span, and why is that a charger design challenge?
Early EVs had packs around 300 to 400 volts, but newer cars use 800-volt systems. So fast chargers must handle a wide voltage range with multiple conversion stages, filtering, and isolation to safely deliver power across all vehicle types.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.1 DC Hub vs. AC Hub · Page: 13
"While early EVs had generally low battery pack voltage ranging from 300 V to 400 V, some recent EVs have nominal battery pack voltage as high as 800 V"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-007
Why are silicon carbide and gallium nitride devices important for DC charging hubs?
Silicon carbide and gallium nitride are wide-bandgap semiconductor materials that switch on and off very fast with low energy losses. They let designers shrink the heavy 60-hertz isolation transformer to a small, high-frequency unit, making compact and efficient DC-DC chargers feasible.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.1 DC Hub vs. AC Hub · Page: 13
"the recent rise of widebandgap semiconductor technologies such as sili­ con carbide (SiC) or gallium nitride (GaN) devices has enabled the effcient integration of high-frequency"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-008
Why can a DC hub's central inverter be sized smaller than an AC hub's inverters?
A DC hub uses one central inverter that handles the average charging demand of the whole site, since storage and chargers share the bus. An AC hub needs an inverter inside every charger sized for that charger's peak, so total inverter capacity is larger and more costly.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.1 DC Hub vs. AC Hub · Page: 15
"The central inverter and grid-connection transformer can be sized to meet the average charging demand, rather than the peak"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-009
Why is breaking DC current harder than breaking AC current?
Alternating current naturally crosses through zero amps roughly a hundred times per second, which extinguishes the arc inside a switch. Direct current never reaches zero on its own, so an arc keeps burning unless special DC breakers or solid-state circuit breakers force it out.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.1 DC Hub vs. AC Hub · Page: 15
"It is more challenging to safely interrupt DC current than AC, since DC current has no zero-crossings."
Indirect c-nrel-chip-010
Why are power electronics considered a reliability concern in a DC hub?
Unlike a passive transformer, the central inverter is full of fast-switching power electronics and complex control loops. That makes its statistical reliability lower than a transformer, and because the hub uses just one, a failure can take down the whole site.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.1 DC Hub vs. AC Hub · Page: 15
"The power electronics introduce signifcant reliability concern, since they are a single point of failure for the hub"
Basic c-nrel-chip-011
What are the two main DC bus topologies for a DC charging hub?
A DC charging hub can use a unipolar bus, with just a positive and negative wire, or a bipolar bus, which adds a neutral wire so loads can connect across half the voltage or the full voltage. Unipolar is still the more common design today.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.2 Different Types of DC Hub Topologies · Page: 15
"a DC hub can have a unipolar or bipolar DC bus. While unipolar remains the most common DC hub architecture"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-012
Why does a bipolar DC bus give better redundancy than a unipolar bus?
A bipolar bus has two independent poles either side of a neutral wire. If one pole fails, the other can keep carrying power at half rating. With unipolar there is just one positive-negative pair, so a single fault disrupts the entire hub instead.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.1.2 Different Types of DC Hub Topologies · Page: 15
"Improved redundant operation: If one pole is faulted, the other pole can remain operational."
Basic c-nrel-chip-013
What voltage are heavy-duty EVs expected to reach in the future?
Heavy-duty EVs are expected to use battery packs as high as 1,500 volts. Inverter technology at that level is already mature in the solar industry, but high-power isolated DC-DC converters at 1,500 volts are still a new, developing technology.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.2 Overview of DC-DC Charger Topologies · Page: 16
"For HD EVs, the voltage is ex­ pected to reach 1,500 V."
Basic c-nrel-chip-014
What three isolated DC-DC converter topologies are commonly used in fast chargers?
The three common isolated DC-DC topologies are the LLC, the dual-active bridge or DAB, and the CLLC. All three connect two active bridges through a medium-frequency transformer, and each manages voltage, current, and isolation in slightly different ways.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.2 Overview of DC-DC Charger Topologies · Page: 16
"There are predominantly three types of topologies to implement isolated DC-DC chargers"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-015
Why did the eCHIP team pick the dual-active bridge topology for their charger?
The DAB has strong, flexible control, smaller filter capacitors than rivals, and is naturally bidirectional, which is essential for vehicle-to-grid. Its main weakness, transformer DC bias from imbalance, can be solved through clever control software rather than hardware additions.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.2 Overview of DC-DC Charger Topologies · Page: 17
"the concerns with the DAB converter can be addressed through controls, so it was chosen for the charger."
Indirect c-nrel-chip-016
Why is detecting electrical faults harder on DC systems than on AC?
AC systems give protection devices frequency and phase angle information to work with. DC has neither, and power electronics often limit the fault current to less than twice rated. With smaller signals to detect, fault location becomes much trickier on a DC bus.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.3 DC Hub Protection Overview · Page: 18
"the ab­ sence of frequency and phasor information in DC systems makes it diffcult for fault detection and localization."
Basic c-nrel-chip-017
What three functions must any DC hub protection system perform?
A DC charging hub's protection system must do three things to operate safely. It needs to detect when a fault has happened, then isolate the faulted section from the rest of the network, then reconfigure the system so the unaffected parts can keep running.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.3 DC Hub Protection Overview · Page: 18
"the protection system needs to perform three functions: i) fault detection, ii) fault isolation, and iii) fault reconfguration"
Basic c-nrel-chip-018
What are the three main fault types in a DC charging hub?
The three main fault types are pole-to-pole faults, where the positive and negative wires touch directly, pole-to-ground faults, where a wire touches the grounded chassis, and AC grid faults arriving from upstream. Pole-to-ground is the most common in practice.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.3.1 Fault Types in a DC Charging Hub · Page: 23
"The major system-level possible fault types in a DC charging hub (based on unipolar confguration) are pole-pole, pole-ground, and AC grid faults"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-019
Why are pole-to-pole faults considered the most severe in a DC hub?
A pole-to-pole fault is essentially a direct short across the DC bus with very low resistance. That causes huge fault currents driven both by capacitor discharge and by current flowing through the converter diodes, making it the most damaging fault in the hub.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.3.1 Fault Types in a DC Charging Hub · Page: 23
"These types of faults are the most severe faults for a DC hub, as the fault current is very high due to low impedance."
Basic c-nrel-chip-020
Which industries already have mature DC distribution standards that EV charging can borrow from?
Standards already exist for DC distribution in data centres, residential and commercial buildings, solar photovoltaic systems, offshore wind collection, railway traction networks, and marine and shipboard microgrids. These give EV charging hub designers concepts to adapt rather than write from scratch.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.4 DC Power Distribution Standards in Other Industries · Page: 23
"data centers, buildings, PV applica­ tions, offshore DC wind power collection, DC power distribution in rail, and on-board marine DC microgrid"
Basic c-nrel-chip-021
What is the Open Charge Point Protocol used for?
The Open Charge Point Protocol, or OCPP, is the de-facto open communication standard for EV charging stations. It lets a charge point talk to a central management server to start and stop sessions, share status, and update firmware, no matter which manufacturer built the hardware.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.5.1 Open Charge Point Protocol · Page: 23
"The OCPP protocol is an open standard that allows monitoring, confguration, and management of EV charging sta­ tions."
Basic c-nrel-chip-022
How does the MQTT protocol move data between devices?
MQTT uses a publish-and-subscribe model. Each device sends, or publishes, messages to named topics on a central broker, while other devices listen by subscribing to the topics they care about. The broker then forwards each message to the right subscribers.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.5.4 Message Queuing Telemetry Transport · Page: 23
"The protocol operates on a publish/subscribe model where clients publish messages to topics and other clients subscribe to those topics to receive the messages."
Basic c-nrel-chip-023
What is OpenADR and why does it matter for charging hubs?
Open Automated Demand Response, or OpenADR, is a vendor-neutral signalling protocol. Grid operators use it to tell large customers, including EV charging hubs, when to ease back on power use during peak demand. It also supports pricing signals that the hub can react to.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 2 Background and Objectives · Section: 2.5.6 Open Automated Demand Response · Page: 23
"OpenADR is an open, standardized communication protocol for demand response (DR) management"
Medium c-nrel-chip-024
What power ratings do the two candidate inverters in the eCHIP testbed have?
Two commercial inverters were chosen. The Anderson AC2660P is rated at 660 kilowatts and is used for initial control testing. The EPC Power CAB1000 reaches 1,043 kilowatts and will support advanced uses like vehicle-to-everything, grid islanding, and reactive-power support later in the project.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.1.1 Inverter Selection · Page: 24
"Table 2. Inverters Used in the DC Hub"
Basic c-nrel-chip-025
What is the DC-REDB at NREL's Energy Systems Integration Facility?
The DC Research Electrical Distribution Bus, or DC-REDB, is a three-wire DC backbone with positive, negative, and ground conductors. It runs through several labs inside the Energy Systems Integration Facility, connecting different DC resources together, and is rated for 1,000 volts maximum.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.1.2 DC Bus Selection · Page: 25
"wire (positive, negative, ground) system with three-pole switches and rated for maximum voltage of 1,000 V DC."
Medium c-nrel-chip-026
How much power can the COTS Tritium PKM150 charger deliver, and to how many EVs?
The Tritium PKM150 is a commercial DC-DC charger that can simultaneously feed up to two EVs at a combined output of 150 kilowatts. One outlet is a CCS plug rated to 350 amps at 920 volts, the other is a CHAdeMO plug rated to 125 amps at 500 volts.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.1.3 COTS DC-DC Charger · Page: 25
"capable of simultaneously charging up to two EVs with an aggregate charging power of 150 kW"
Basic c-nrel-chip-027
How does the eCHIP testbed emulate a solar photovoltaic array?
A Magna-Power MTA1000-250 DC power supply rated at 250 kilowatts is used to mimic a real solar array. The supply runs in current-control mode, and the energy management system sends it new current set-points every second using a one-second-resolution real PV power profile.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.1.5 PV Emulation · Page: 25
"A Magna-Power MTA1000-250 MT Series VI DC power supply is used to emulate PV generation."
Medium c-nrel-chip-028
How much building load can the load bank used in the eCHIP testbed dissipate?
The Simplex Mars resistive load bank can absorb up to 505.5 kilowatts at 1,000 volts DC and 505.5 amps DC. It burns the power as heat in switchable resistive elements, and the resolution of control is limited to about 0.5 kilowatts per step.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.1.6 Building Load Emulation · Page: 25
"The load bank is rated at 505.5 kW, 1,000 V DC, and 505.5 A DC."
Medium c-nrel-chip-029
What charging powers do the two test EVs in eCHIP support?
The Hyundai Ioniq 5 has an 800-volt pack and can pull up to 235 kilowatts when fast charging. The Nissan Leaf uses a 348-volt pack and tops out at 40 kilowatts. The pair gives the testbed both an 800-volt-class and a lower-voltage vehicle to exercise.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.1.7 Electric Vehicles · Page: 25
"The Ioniq 5 has a nominal pack voltage of 800 V with a maximum charging power capability of 235 kW."
Basic c-nrel-chip-030
What is the UPER charger developed by Oak Ridge National Laboratory?
UPER stands for Universal Power Electronics Regulator. It is a custom dual-active-bridge DC-DC charger built at Oak Ridge that connects the DC bus to the vehicle. The first prototype is rated at 175 kilowatts and 1,000 volts and is designed to be scaled up to half a megawatt.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.2 ORNL-Developed DC-DC Charger Topology · Page: 25
"The isolated DC-DC DAB converter is referred to here as a Universal Power Electronics Regulator (UPER), interfacing the DC distribu tion bus and the vehicle."
Medium c-nrel-chip-031
What efficiency target and switching frequency does the UPER charger aim for?
The UPER 1000-volt-class charger targets an efficiency above 99 percent across its bidirectional operation. It runs at a switching frequency of 20 kilohertz, picked deliberately to keep the acoustic noise out of the audible range and improve user comfort.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.2 ORNL-Developed DC-DC Charger Topology · Page: 26
"The switching frequency has been chosen to be 20 kHz to reduce the acoustic noise."
Indirect c-nrel-chip-032
Why does the UPER charger use a transformer tap to serve both 400-volt and 800-volt cars?
A dual-active-bridge converter struggles to keep zero-voltage switching across very wide output ranges. By adding a tap on the secondary side of the medium-frequency transformer, the UPER swaps to the right turns ratio for either a 400-volt or 800-volt pack, preserving efficiency.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.2 ORNL-Developed DC-DC Charger Topology · Page: 26
"The tap is used to provide correct voltage to either a 400-V class vehicle or an 800-V class vehicle."
Basic c-nrel-chip-033
What is the SpEC module developed by Argonne?
The Smartgrid EV Communication, or SpEC, module is a small communication controller built by Argonne. It acts as the supply-equipment communications controller for a DC fast charger, translating ISO 15118 and DIN 70121 messages between the vehicle and the charger's power electronics.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.3 ANL-Developed SpEC Module Integration Specifications · Page: 26
"The Smartgrid EV Communication (SpEC) module developed by Argonne is a smart EV communication controller that enables DC fast charging communication between an EV and the charger."
Basic c-nrel-chip-034
How does the SpEC module physically talk to the EV during a charging session?
The SpEC module sits at the charger end and exchanges messages with the car over power line communication, or PLC. The PLC signals travel down the control pilot wire inside the standard CCS connector, so no extra cable is needed to handle ISO 15118 messages.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.3 ANL-Developed SpEC Module Integration Specifications · Page: 27
"the communication be­ tween them is via power line communication (PLC) over the CCS connector’s control pilot line."
Basic c-nrel-chip-035
What is the role of a site energy management system, or SEMS?
A SEMS is the brain of a charging hub. It monitors, controls, and optimises how energy flows between chargers, batteries, solar, and the grid. The goal is to cut energy consumption, lower costs, and coordinate the interactions of all the components on the site.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.1 Background and Objective Definition · Page: 35
"SEMS involves the implementation of strategies aimed at reducing energy consumption, increasing effciency, minimizing costs, and defning interactions between hub components."
Basic c-nrel-chip-036
What are the three common objectives of a site energy management strategy?
The three common SEMS goals are reducing the time it takes to charge an EV, minimising the cost of charging for both driver and operator, and optimising load and energy sharing between the hub's chargers, energy storage, generation, and other loads.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.1 Background and Objective Definition · Page: 35
"Some of the common objectives of an SEMS strategy, along with their implementation challenges and requirements, are detailed below."
Indirect c-nrel-chip-037
Why does adding battery storage and solar generation improve a SEMS's resilience?
Renewables and batteries give the hub a decentralized power source, so if the utility grid drops out the hub can keep critical loads alive on its own. It also reduces dependence on a single supply path, lowering the chance of total outage during disturbances.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.2.1 SEMS Performance Metrics · Page: 35
"Incorporating renewables and ESS into an SEMS can provide a decentralized source that can continue to provide power during grid outages."
Indirect c-nrel-chip-038
What are the trade-offs of a centralized SEMS controller?
A central SEMS controller can optimise the whole site because it sees every measurement in real time. But that one controller becomes a single point of failure, may become a performance bottleneck under load, and is harder to scale up as new chargers are added.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.2.2 SEMS Controller Architecture · Page: 35
"this architecture can also introduce single point of failure, as the entire system may be disrupted if the central controller fails or becomes overwhelmed"
Basic c-nrel-chip-039
What is droop control in a decentralized DC charging hub?
Droop control is a simple rule that lets each device decide its own power level from the DC bus voltage alone. The device follows a piecewise-linear curve, so no central controller or fast communication is needed. It is the classic decentralized scheme for shared DC buses.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.2.2 SEMS Controller Architecture · Page: 35
"The traditional droop controller is good example of a decentralized scheme where the power-set points are piece­ wise linear functions of the bus voltage."
Indirect c-nrel-chip-040
What is the distributed SEMS architecture meant to combine?
Distributed SEMS sits between fully centralized and fully decentralized. Devices decide their own set-points like droop control, but they also exchange information occasionally so the controller can adapt. That gives most of the optimisation benefit while keeping resilience if the network goes down.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.2.2 SEMS Controller Architecture · Page: 35
"by using a decentralized approach in conjunction with a communication capability that is in between individual units and a central server. This is known as distributed architecture."
Medium c-nrel-chip-041
How many DC fast chargers does Electrify America operate and with how much battery storage?
Electrify America has installed over 3,500 DC fast chargers spread across roughly 800 sites in the United States. The company has also rolled out about 30 megawatts of battery energy storage at more than 140 of those fast-charging sites to help manage demand.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.3.1 Current Implementation Status · Page: 35
"Electrify America, for example, has installed over 3,500 DC fast chargers at 800 sites"
Basic c-nrel-chip-042
What does the MING stack stand for in IoT software?
MING is an open-source toolchain for Internet-of-Things applications: MQTT as the messaging broker, InfluxDB as the time-series database, Node-RED as the visual flow tool for transforming data and protocols, and Grafana as the dashboard for visualising the data.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.3.3 An Open-Source SEMS Platform · Page: 35
"MING stands for MQTT (communication broker), InfuxDB (time-series database), Node-RED (transform data/protocols), and Grafana (visualize data)."
Basic c-nrel-chip-043
What is CIP.io and where does the eCHIP project plan to run it?
CIP.io is an open-source Internet-of-Things integration platform developed by Argonne in 2016 and built on the MING stack. eCHIP plans to deploy it on a small computer such as an Intel NUC or Dell OptiPlex micro to host the open-source SEMS.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 4 Site Energy Management System · Section: 4.3.4 Open-Source SEMS Implementation · Page: 35
"an IoT Common Integration Platform called CIP.io (pronounced “sip-e-o”), was developed in 2016 by ANL"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-044
How does the SEMS dispatch energy when an EV, battery storage, and solar are all on the DC hub?
The rule-based controller serves EV charging power first from solar, then from the battery storage, and only if those are not enough does it pull from the central inverter and the grid. Any surplus solar goes first to the battery, then back out to the grid.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 5 Component and System Hardware · Section: 5.1.4 DC Hub with EV, Battery ESS, and PV Emulation · Page: 38
"EV charging power is frst supplied by the PV generation, then the ESS, then the inverter only if the PV generation and ESS capacity are insuffcient."
Medium c-nrel-chip-045
What happened in the demand-response test when the SEMS reduced inverter capacity by 50 percent?
When an OpenADR signal cut available inverter capacity from 150 down to 75 kilowatts, the energy storage emulator discharged at its rated power to make up the gap. The Hyundai Ioniq 5 continued charging at about 125 kilowatts during this demand-response event.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 5 Component and System Hardware · Section: 5.1.3 DC Hub with EV and Battery ESS Emulation · Page: 38
"The available inverter capacity is reduced by the SEMS by 50% from 150 kW to 75 kW."
Basic c-nrel-chip-046
What is the role of an EV charging emulator in the eCHIP testbed?
The custom EV charging emulator looks identical to a real car from the charger's perspective, but the power that goes in is sent back to the utility connection instead of an actual battery. It can mimic packs up to 1,000 volts and 500 kilowatts continuously.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 3 Architecture and Design Parameters · Section: 3.1.7 Electric Vehicles · Page: 25
"the charging power is being fed back to the utility connection rather than an EV and its battery"
Basic c-nrel-chip-047
At what voltage and current was the assembled UPER charger first tested?
The fully assembled 175-kilowatt, 1000-volt-class UPER charger was first powered and tested at a bus voltage of 950 volts and an output current of 150 amps. That operating point corresponds to roughly 150 kilowatts of steady-state power transfer to the load.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 5 Component and System Hardware · Section: 5.2 ORNL UPER DC-DC Charger Testing Results · Page: 40
"the charger is powered and tested at 950 V and 150 A, which approximately corresponds to 150 kW of steady-state operation."
Basic c-nrel-chip-048
What vehicle did Argonne use to demonstrate bidirectional vehicle-to-grid charging?
Argonne teamed up with Lion Electric for a vehicle-to-grid demonstration at the Fall 2023 EVs@Scale Semi-Annual meeting. Engineers paired an AeroVironment ABC-170 power source with the SpEC II module and a Lion electric bus to switch between charging and discharging in real time.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 5 Component and System Hardware · Section: 5.3 Bidirectional Power Transfer Demonstration · Page: 42
"we successfully conducted a V2G session with the Lion Bus, demon­ strating rapid switching between charging and discharging in real time"
Indirect c-nrel-chip-049
What is the ISO 15118-2 standard and why was an implementation a milestone?
ISO 15118-2 is the international standard for vehicle-to-grid communication. Argonne built a bidirectional power transfer stack of ISO 15118-2 for the SpEC II controller, which is a crucial step to enable V2G capability on SpEC-based DC chargers in the field.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 5 Component and System Hardware · Section: 5.3 Bidirectional Power Transfer Demonstration · Page: 41
"creating an ISO 15118-2 bidirectional power transfer (BPT) stack for the SpEC II communication controller, a crucial step towards enabling V2G capabilities"
Basic c-nrel-chip-050
What future work does the eCHIP report identify?
Future eCHIP work will demonstrate more advanced SEMS controllers focused on optimised, distributed site operation. The team also plans to integrate the in-house ORNL UPER DC-DC charger with Argonne's SpEC module into the NREL hub, and to add more chargers covering vehicle-to-everything use cases.
Source: eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design
Chapter: 6 Conclusion and Future Work · Section: — · Page: 44
"Future work will include demonstration of more advanced SEMS controllers that will focus on optimized and dis­ tributed operation of the site components."

7. Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management

Bidzina Kekelia & Xuhui Feng · National Renewable Energy Laboratory (NREL) / ASME InterPACK 2023 · 50 Q&As

Basic c-nrel-motor-001
Which NREL laboratory team produced this thermal-management tutorial?
The tutorial was produced by Bidzina Kekelia and Xuhui Feng from the Advanced Power Electronics and Electric Machines group inside NREL's Center for Integrated Mobility Sciences. It was presented at the ASME InterPACK conference in San Diego in October 2023.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Tutorial Outline · Section: — · Page: 3
"Bidzina Kekelia and Xuhui Feng Advanced Power Electronics and Electric Machines"
Basic c-nrel-motor-002
How many top-level topics does the NREL motor tutorial outline contain?
The NREL motor tutorial outline contains seven top-level topics, ranging from vehicle thermal management systems and motor and power electronics components, through integration techniques and cooling approaches, to design workflows, experimental characterisation and a closing review of challenges and summary.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Tutorial Outline · Section: — · Page: 3
"Tutorial Outline 1 Vehicle Thermal Management Systems"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-003
Why does an electric-drive vehicle need several separate thermal management systems?
An electric-drive vehicle uses several separate thermal management systems because different subsystems, such as the battery, the motor and the power electronics, all have their own temperature limits. One shared loop cannot satisfy every constraint at once without damaging some components.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 1. Vehicle Thermal Management Systems · Section: — · Page: 3
"Multiple separate thermal management systems to manage temperature constraints for different vehicle subsystems"
Basic c-nrel-motor-004
What three kinds of power electronics does NREL list as critical inside an EV?
NREL lists three kinds of power electronics as critical inside an EV: inverters, converters and chargers. Together with the electric machines themselves, they steer how power flows from the battery to the wheels and back during regenerative braking events.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 2. Power Electronics and Electric Motor Components · Section: — · Page: 5
"Power electronics (inverters, converters, chargers) and electric machines (motors)"
Basic c-nrel-motor-005
Across which three vehicle types does NREL say power electronics control flow?
NREL says power electronics control flow across three vehicle types: hybrid, battery electric and fuel cell. Each of these uses an electric machine for at least part of its propulsion, so each one needs power electronics to manage the energy supply correctly.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 2. Power Electronics and Electric Motor Components · Section: — · Page: 5
"across a range of applications (hybrid, battery electric, fuel cell)"
Basic c-nrel-motor-006
What does the US DRIVE 2025 cost target ask for an electric traction drive system?
The US DRIVE 2025 cost target asks for an electric traction drive system to reach $6 per kilowatt. That figure represents a 50 percent reduction in cost and is meant to make electrified powertrains price-competitive with conventional internal-combustion drivelines.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 2. Power Electronics and Electric Motor Components · Section: U.S. DRIVE 2025 Targets · Page: 9
"Electric Traction Drive System Cost \$6/kW (50% reduction)"
Basic c-nrel-motor-007
What power density does US DRIVE want from a 2025 electric traction drive?
US DRIVE wants a 2025 electric traction drive to reach 33 kilowatts per litre of power density. That is an 850 percent increase over earlier targets and pushes designers towards much smaller drive units squeezed into the same vehicle space.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 2. Power Electronics and Electric Motor Components · Section: U.S. DRIVE 2025 Targets · Page: 9
"Power density 33 kW/L (850% increase)"
Basic c-nrel-motor-008
What reliability target does US DRIVE set for an electric traction drive?
US DRIVE sets a reliability target of three hundred thousand miles for an electric traction drive system. That is a 100 percent increase on earlier targets and asks the drive to last roughly as long as the rest of the vehicle around it.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 2. Power Electronics and Electric Motor Components · Section: U.S. DRIVE 2025 Targets · Page: 9
"Reliability/lifetime 300,000 miles (100% increase)"
Basic c-nrel-motor-009
What power level does the US DRIVE traction drive target call for?
The US DRIVE traction drive target calls for a power level of 100 kilowatts. That figure is the peak output the drive must deliver, sized to match the propulsion demands of a typical light-duty electric passenger vehicle under hard acceleration.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 2. Power Electronics and Electric Motor Components · Section: U.S. DRIVE 2025 Targets · Page: 9
"Power level 100 kW"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-010
Why does ARPA-E care about electric drives for narrow-body airplanes?
ARPA-E cares about electric drives for narrow-body airplanes because that class typically carries 100 to 200 passengers and is a large share of aviation fuel use. Electrifying it would cut a meaningful chunk of total air-travel emissions if drives can be made light enough.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: DOE ARPA-E Aviation Electric-Drive Efforts · Section: — · Page: 9
"Single-aisle (narrow-body) airplanes with 100–200 passengers"
Basic c-nrel-motor-011
What four physical integration styles does NREL list for combining motor and inverter?
NREL lists four physical integration styles for combining the motor and inverter: separate enclosures, radial integration, axial integration and putting the inverter inside the motor. Each style trades package size against ease of cooling and ease of service.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 3. Integrated Traction Drive and Integration Techniques · Section: — · Page: 11
"Separate enclosures Radial integration Axial integration Inside motor"
Basic c-nrel-motor-012
Which dielectric fluids does NREL identify as originally meant for battery cooling?
NREL identifies AC100 and Alpha 6 as dielectric fluids that were originally developed for battery thermal management. These non-conductive oils can now also touch motor and inverter parts directly, which is something water-glycol coolants cannot safely do without insulation in between.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: — · Page: 13
"Originally for battery thermal management: AC100, Alpha 6"
Basic c-nrel-motor-013
What family of dielectric fluids does NREL mention from a major oil brand?
NREL mentions the Mobil EV family of fluids as a commercially available line of dielectric coolants for electric vehicles. Several other formulations from various suppliers are still under development or are proprietary, so the market in EV-specific fluids is still maturing.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: — · Page: 13
"Mobil EV family of fluids"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-014
Why are refrigerant-based two-phase coolers rare in today's automotive power electronics?
Refrigerant-based two-phase coolers are rare in today's automotive power electronics because they are not yet widely adopted. The plumbing and seals needed to handle a boiling and condensing refrigerant safely inside a moving vehicle remain a barrier compared with simpler single-phase liquid loops.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: Refrigerants for two-phase cooling · Page: 13
"Not yet widely adopted in current automotive power electronics applications"
Basic c-nrel-motor-015
Which coolant fluid is used in the first manufacturer configuration NREL reviews where motor and inverter are separate?
In the first manufacturer configuration NREL reviews, the motor and inverter are kept in separate housings and cooled with water and glycol mix. Water-glycol is the standard automotive coolant because it has good heat capacity and resists freezing.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: — · Page: 14
"Motor and inverter separate"
Basic c-nrel-motor-016
How does the GM Chevy Bolt cool its drive system, according to NREL?
According to NREL, the GM Chevy Bolt keeps its motor and inverter separate or remote and uses a hybrid coolant mix of oil and water-glycol. An integrated oil-to-glycol heat exchanger lets the two loops trade heat with each other inside the drive unit.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: GM Chevy Bolt · Page: 15
"Integrated oil-glycol heat exchanger"
Basic c-nrel-motor-017
Which Tesla and BMW models does NREL cite when comparing cooling housings?
NREL cites Munro and Associates' 2020 teardown that compares the cooling-strategy housings of the Tesla Model 3 motor against the BMW i3 motor. That source is the basis for several of NREL's manufacturer-by-manufacturer cooling tables in this tutorial.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: Cooling-strategy comparison · Page: 15
"Comparing the Cooling Strategy Housings of Motors for Tesla Model 3 vs BMW i3"
Basic c-nrel-motor-018
Where does NREL show the inverter mounted in the radial-integration configuration on page 16?
In the radial-integration configuration on page 16, NREL shows the inverter radially mounted on one side of the motor. Both the motor stator housing and the inverter share the same water-and-glycol coolant loop, simplifying the plumbing inside the package.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: Radial integration example · Page: 16
"Inverter radial mount on one side of motor"
Medium c-nrel-motor-019
How does the cooling configuration on page 17 differ from the one on page 16?
The page 17 configuration also mounts the inverter radially on one side of the motor with water-glycol coolant, but adds air cooling and indirect water-glycol cooling for the rotor end plates plus water-glycol on the rotor shaft. Page 16 has no rotor cooling.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: Radial-mount variation · Page: 17
"Inverter radial mount on one side of motor"
Basic c-nrel-motor-020
What does NREL describe as a WEG heat exchanger on page 18?
On page 18, NREL describes a WEG heat exchanger as a water-ethylene-glycol unit that cools an oil jet. The oil sprays directly onto the stator end windings, then passes its heat into the water-glycol loop through the heat exchanger before recirculating.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: Hybrid oil-WEG cooling · Page: 18
"Oil jet cooled with water-ethylene- glycol (WEG) heat exchanger"
Basic c-nrel-motor-021
Which lubricant does NREL list as the oil-side coolant in the axial-mount configuration on page 19?
In the axial-mount configuration on page 19, NREL lists ATF 9, an automatic transmission fluid, as the oil-side coolant. The oil itself is then cooled by a WEG heat exchanger, so heat ends up rejected to the vehicle's water-glycol radiator loop.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: Axial-mount inverter example · Page: 19
"Oil (ATF 9)"
Basic c-nrel-motor-022
On NREL's page 20 example, which parts of the motor are cooled by oil?
On NREL's page 20 example, oil cools the stator housing, the stator end winding, the rotor shaft and the inverter itself. The same oil is then sent through a water-ethylene-glycol heat exchanger to reject its heat to the rest of the cooling system.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: Axial-mount oil cooling · Page: 20
"Oil cooled with WEG heat exchanger"
Basic c-nrel-motor-023
How does the page 21 CSI Power Electronics configuration cool its rotor?
On page 21, the CSI Power Electronics configuration uses a radial mount with water-glycol coolant for the stator and inverter, but cools the rotor with air. Air cooling the rotor end plates and shaft avoids sliding seals and complicated rotating coolant joints.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: CSI Power Electronics · Page: 21
"Rotor cooled with air"
Basic c-nrel-motor-024
What integrated drive design does NREL highlight from Oak Ridge National Laboratory?
NREL highlights Oak Ridge National Laboratory's outer-rotor motor with an integrated inverter. It uses a single water-ethylene-glycol cooling loop, a cylindrical housing with internal coolant channels for a six-phase inverter, and ceramic heat exchangers embedded between the stator windings.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: ORNL outer-rotor design · Page: 22
"Outer-Rotor Motor With Integrated Inverter"
Basic c-nrel-motor-025
How many T-shape heat exchangers does ORNL use in its stator cooling assembly?
ORNL uses eighteen T-shape heat exchangers in its stator cooling assembly. They are attached to a shared coolant distribution manifold, so a single inlet feeds all of them and the cooling load is spread evenly around the motor stator.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 4. Review of Integration and Cooling Approaches · Section: ORNL stator cooling assembly · Page: 22
"Stator cooling assembly with 18 T-shape heat exchangers"
Basic c-nrel-motor-026
What kind of inverter housing concept does Bidzina Kekelia present on page 24?
On page 24, Bidzina Kekelia presents a design concept for a cylindrical inverter housing with cooling fluid channels built into the walls. The walls themselves carry the coolant, so the inverter electronics shed heat directly into the housing as they switch.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 5. Thermal Management System Design Workflow · Section: — · Page: 24
"Design concept of a cylindrical inverter housing with cooling fluid channels in the walls"
Basic c-nrel-motor-027
What three sources does NREL list for finding how much heat a motor produces?
NREL lists three sources for finding how much heat a motor produces: the electromagnetic analysis of the design, the MotorCAD design tool and physical testing of a built motor. Designers typically use all three so the answers can be cross-checked.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 5. Thermal Management System Design Workflow · Section: Questions To Start Design · Page: 28
"From the electromagnetic (EM) analysis From MotorCAD design tool From testing"
Basic c-nrel-motor-028
What three temperatures does NREL say a designer must know at the start?
NREL says a designer must know three temperatures at the start of a thermal design: the motor temperature limit, the coolant temperature, and the ambient temperature. Together they bound how much heat the cooling system actually needs to move to keep the motor safe.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 5. Thermal Management System Design Workflow · Section: Questions To Start Design · Page: 28
"Motor temperature limit Coolant temperature Ambient temperature"
Basic c-nrel-motor-029
What three cooling methods does NREL list when starting a motor thermal design?
When starting a motor thermal design, NREL lists three cooling methods to choose from: air, liquid and hybrid. Liquid options include water, water-ethylene-glycol mix, engine oil and lubricants, each with its own trade-off between heat capacity and material compatibility.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 5. Thermal Management System Design Workflow · Section: Which cooling method · Page: 28
"Air Liquid (water, WEG, engine oil, lubricant…) Hybrid"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-030
Why does NREL recommend a preliminary estimate before detailed thermal modelling?
NREL recommends a preliminary estimate before detailed thermal modelling because a quick analytical or empirical pass narrows the range of heat transfer coefficients and surface areas. That trims the field of candidate cooling methods early, saving time on detailed simulations that would never work anyway.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 5. Thermal Management System Design Workflow · Section: Preliminary Estimate · Page: 28
"Preliminary study is needed before detailed model-based design"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-031
What two modelling approaches does NREL contrast for thermal management design?
NREL contrasts two modelling approaches for thermal management design: a one-dimensional thermal network that is hard to build but runs very fast, and three-dimensional numerical tools, namely thermal finite element analysis and computational fluid dynamics, which are slower but more detailed.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 5. Thermal Management System Design Workflow · Section: Modeling and Validation · Page: 28
"1D thermal network Hard to develop Fast calculation 3D numerical tools"
Basic c-nrel-motor-032
What machine specific-power target does NREL list for an aircraft propulsion design?
NREL lists a machine specific-power target of 20 kilowatts per kilogram for an aircraft propulsion design. That figure measures how much output the motor delivers per unit of mass, which matters most when the drive has to be carried into the sky.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Case Study: Electric System for Commercial · Section: Design Specifications and Parameters · Page: 28
"Machine specific power"
Basic c-nrel-motor-033
What peak power does NREL's commercial aircraft case study aim for?
NREL's commercial aircraft case study aims for a peak power of 250 kilowatts and a continuous power of 83 kilowatts. The big gap between the two figures reflects that an aircraft only needs full power briefly during take-off and climb.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Case Study: Electric System for Commercial · Section: Design Specifications and Parameters · Page: 28
"Peak power"
Basic c-nrel-motor-034
What machine efficiency does NREL's aircraft case study require?
NREL's aircraft case study requires a machine efficiency greater than 95 percent. That high efficiency keeps wasted heat low, which directly reduces the size and weight of the cooling system the airplane has to lift along with the motor itself.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Case Study: Electric System for Commercial · Section: Design Specifications and Parameters · Page: 28
"Machine efficiency"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-035
Why does NREL only model one-eighteenth of the aircraft electric machine?
NREL only models one-eighteenth of the aircraft electric machine because the design has structural symmetry. Cutting it down to a single repeating slice still captures the physics but shrinks the computational job, so each design iteration runs much faster than it otherwise could.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Estimate Cooling Needs and Conditions · Section: — · Page: 29
"Due to structural symmetry, 1/18 of electric machine (motor) was extracted for analysis"
Basic c-nrel-motor-036
Which loss component is largest inside one slice of the modelled aircraft motor?
The largest loss component inside one slice of the modelled aircraft motor is the AM coil, which dissipates 794 watts. That figure dwarfs the other losses, so cooling that coil well is the first priority in sizing the thermal management system.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Estimate Cooling Needs and Conditions · Section: Loss Breakdown in 1/18 of the Machine · Page: 29
"AM coil"
Basic c-nrel-motor-037
How much heat does the stator core lose in NREL's aircraft motor slice?
In NREL's aircraft motor slice, the stator core loses 277 watts. That is the second-largest contribution, well behind the AM coil. The magnets and friction-and-windage losses come in much smaller, at 36.7 and 68 watts respectively, with heat pipes carrying 94.5 watts.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Estimate Cooling Needs and Conditions · Section: Loss Breakdown in 1/18 of the Machine · Page: 29
"Stator core"
Basic c-nrel-motor-038
Which part of the aircraft motor coil design does NREL describe as critical to characterise?
NREL describes the additively manufactured coil with an embedded heat pipe as the critical part to characterise. The diameter of that heat pipe sets the coil geometry and so the heat losses, which makes the heat pipe a load-bearing design choice.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Preliminary Tests · Section: — · Page: 30
"additively manufactured coil with embedded heat pipe is the essential part of TMS"
Basic c-nrel-motor-039
What two interface materials does NREL test for thermal contact in the heat pipe rig?
NREL tests two interface materials for thermal contact resistance at the heat pipe: thermal paste and a boron nitride coating. Whichever interface is used decides how easily heat crosses from the coil into the heat pipe before the coolant carries it away.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Preliminary Tests · Section: Thermal contact resistance · Page: 30
"Thermal paste Boron nitride coating"
Basic c-nrel-motor-040
What kinds of properties does NREL include in its 3D thermal finite-element model?
NREL's three-dimensional thermal finite-element model includes potting and insulation layers and material properties such as density and thermal conductivity. It can run as steady-state or transient and can apply uniform or non-uniform heat losses, depending on what the engineer needs to predict.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Numerical Simulations · Section: — · Page: 31
"Include potting and insulation layers Material properties (density, thermal conductivity, etc.)"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-041
Why does NREL list CFD as more demanding than simple thermal analysis?
NREL lists CFD as more demanding because it takes longer to develop and needs careful knowledge of model parameters and settings. The reward is higher accuracy and location-by-location detail on temperature, heat transfer coefficient and heat flux that simpler tools cannot provide.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Modeling Results and Iterations · Section: — · Page: 33
"More time to develop Require knowledge for model parameters/setting Higher accuracy"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-042
How does NREL close the loop between thermal modelling and electromagnetic design?
NREL closes the loop by feeding the temperature predicted in each layer back into the electromagnetic design. The electromagnetic team uses those temperatures to tune the heat losses, and the cycle repeats so cooling and motor design evolve together rather than separately.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Modeling Results and Iterations · Section: — · Page: 33
"Temperature in each layer can be fed back into EM for tuning the heat losses"
Basic c-nrel-motor-043
What three goals does NREL list for its electric motor research programme?
NREL's electric motor research programme has three goals: understand material and interface properties as a function of temperature, develop and evaluate advanced fluid-based cooling strategies, and use modelling to guide advanced motor design and development for future drive units.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 6. Experimental Characterization of Materials and Coolant HTCs · Section: Electric Motor Research · Page: 36
"Develop and evaluate advanced fluid-based cooling strategies"
Basic c-nrel-motor-044
What variable does NREL identify as having a strong influence on the heat transfer coefficient in jet impingement tests?
In NREL's jet impingement tests, the target surface temperature has a strong influence on the heat transfer coefficient. Charts at surface temperatures of 90, 100, 110 and 120 degrees Celsius all show the HTC rising as jet velocity climbs from one to ten metres per second.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: Heat Transfer Comparison · Section: Center Impingement · Page: 42
"Temperature iomf tphaects the HTC"
Basic c-nrel-motor-045
What does CTE stand for in NREL's tutorial summary?
In NREL's tutorial summary, CTE stands for Coefficient of Thermal Expansion. A mismatch in CTE between cooling-system components causes them to expand and contract by different amounts when temperatures cycle, leading to stresses, leaks and eventual mechanical failure inside the drive.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 7. Challenges and Summary · Section: Remaining Challenges and Barriers · Page: 46
"Coefficient of thermal expansion (CTE) mismatch"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-046
Why does NREL flag leak-free sealing as a particular challenge for integrated drives?
NREL flags leak-free sealing as a particular challenge because an integrated traction drive packs cooling channels right next to high-voltage electronics. Any leak of coolant inside the unit can short out the inverter, so sealing has to stay perfect through years of thermal cycling.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 7. Challenges and Summary · Section: Remaining Challenges and Barriers · Page: 46
"Leak-free sealing of cooling system components inside an integrated traction drive is challenging"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-047
Why does NREL conclude that active cooling is critical for future EV traction drives?
NREL concludes that active cooling is critical for future EV traction drives because tomorrow's drives will be even more power-dense than today's. Without fluid moving heat out actively, the small package needed to hit those targets simply cannot stay within safe operating temperatures.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 7. Challenges and Summary · Section: Summary · Page: 46
"Active cooling is critical for today’s (and especially future) powerdense EV traction drives"
Medium c-nrel-motor-048
Which coolant combination does NREL say most manufacturers rely on for EV traction drives?
NREL says most manufacturers rely on a combination of oil and water-glycol fluids for EV traction drives, even though their integration choices differ. Oil cools the high-temperature motor parts directly, then a water-glycol loop takes that heat to the radiator on the outside.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 7. Challenges and Summary · Section: Summary · Page: 46
"mostly rely on a combination of oil and water/glycol fluids"
Medium c-nrel-motor-049
Why does NREL describe direct driveline fluid cooling as one of the most effective single-phase methods?
NREL describes direct driveline fluid cooling as one of the most effective single-phase methods because the coolant touches hot parts directly rather than going through a housing wall. Cutting out that thermal barrier lets more heat move per square centimetre, so the drive can be smaller.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 7. Challenges and Summary · Section: Summary · Page: 46
"Direct driveline fluid cooling is potentially one of the most effective (single-phase) thermal management solutions"
Indirect c-nrel-motor-050
Why does NREL call wider adoption of EV-specific dielectric fluids paramount for future drives?
NREL calls wider adoption of EV-specific dielectric fluids paramount because such fluids let one coolant touch electronics and motor parts directly without a metal barrier. That allows smaller, lighter integrated drive units to hit aggressive volumetric power density targets without overheating.
Source: Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management
Chapter: 7. Challenges and Summary · Section: Summary · Page: 46
"Development and wide adoption of EV-specific dielectric fluids is paramount"

8. Global EV Outlook 2024

International Energy Agency · IEA · 50 Q&As

Basic c-iea-out-001
How many electric cars were sold globally in 2023 and what share of all car sales did that represent?
Almost 14 million new electric cars were registered worldwide in 2023, accounting for about 18% of every car sold that year. The share was up from 14% in 2022 and only 2% in 2018, showing how quickly the market has grown over five years.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 17
"Electric cars accounted for around 18% of all cars sold in 2023, up from 14% in 2022 and only 2% 5 years earlier, in 2018."
Basic c-iea-out-002
Which three regions accounted for nearly all electric car sales in 2023?
China, Europe and the United States together made up about 95% of global electric car sales in 2023. Roughly 60% of new electric cars were sold in China, just under 25% in Europe and around 10% in the United States, leaving the rest of the world a small share.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 19
"just under 60% of new electric car registrations were in the People’s Republic of China (hereafter “China”), just under 25% in Europe, and 10% in the United States – corresponding to nearly 95% of global electric car sales combined."
Basic c-iea-out-003
How many new electric cars were registered in China in 2023?
In China, new electric car registrations reached 8.1 million in 2023, about 35% higher than the previous year. Electric models drove all of China's car-market growth, because sales of conventional petrol and diesel cars actually fell by 8% during the same year.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024

How many electric cars did the United States sell in 2023?
About 1.4 million new electric cars were registered in the United States in 2023, more than 40% higher than in 2022. The Inflation Reduction Act tax credits and price cuts on popular models such as the Tesla Model Y helped drive the increase.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 19
"In the United States, new electric car registrations totalled 1.4 million in 2023, increasing by more than 40% compared to 2022."
Basic c-iea-out-005
Which European country had the highest electric car sales share in 2023?
Norway had Europe's highest share, with electric cars making up almost 95% of new car sales in 2023. Norway has long offered strong tax breaks for EVs, and its sales share kept rising even though the country's overall car market shrank that year.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 19
"In Norway, sales shares increased slightly despite the overall market contracting, and its sales share remains the highest in Europe, at almost 95%."
Indirect c-iea-out-006
Why did Germany's electric car sales share fall from 30% in 2022 to 25% in 2023?
Germany phased out its subsidies for plug-in hybrids at the start of 2023 and ended remaining electric-car subsidies in December 2023 after a court ruling on the Climate and Transformation Fund. Removing this purchase support cooled demand and pulled the overall electric sales share down by five points.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 19
"At the start of 2023, PHEV subsidies were phased out, resulting in lower PHEV sales compared to 2022, and in December 2023, all EV subsidies ended after a ruling on the Climate and Transformation Fund."
Basic c-iea-out-007
What is a fuel cell electric vehicle (FCEV), and how large is the global stock?
An FCEV runs on hydrogen, using a fuel cell to make electricity on board. By the end of 2023 there were about 87,600 FCEVs worldwide, with the stock growing roughly 20% in a year. Cars made up half of new sales, with trucks and buses accounting for most of the rest.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 21
"the global stock of fuel cell electric vehicles (FCEVs) increased by around 20% compared to 2022, reaching 87 600 by the end of the year."
Basic c-iea-out-008
How fast did electric car sales grow in Thailand during 2023?
Thailand's new electric car registrations more than quadrupled in 2023 to nearly 90,000, giving electric models a 10% share of all car sales. New subsidies, lower import and excise taxes, and the arrival of Chinese carmakers all helped drive the surge even as the wider market shrank.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 22
"In Thailand, electric car registrations more than quadrupled year-on-year to nearly 90 000, reaching a notable 10% sales share"
Basic c-iea-out-009
What share of cars sold in India in 2023 were electric?
About 2% of all new cars sold in India in 2023 were electric, with roughly 80,000 registrations — up 70% from the year before. Subsidies under the FAME II scheme, the PLI manufacturing scheme and new models from Tata, Mahindra and others all helped fuel the growth.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 22
"In India, electric car registrations were up 70% year-on-year to 80 000, compared to a growth rate of under 10% for total car sales. Around 2% of all cars sold were electric."
Indirect c-iea-out-010
Why has EV adoption been slow in Brazil despite its clean power mix?
Since the late 1970s Brazil has prioritised ethanol-based fuels made from its sugar cane crop, as a way to keep oil imports down. The existing refuelling network and competitive cost of ethanol have given biofuels a head start, slowing the shift to plug-in electric cars in the country.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car sales · Page: 26
"EV adoption has been slow thus far, given the national prioritisation of ethanol-based fuels since the late 1970s as a strategy to maintain energy security in the face of oil shocks."

How many electric cars were sold globally in the first quarter of 2024?
More than 3 million electric cars were sold worldwide in the first three months of 2024, about 25% more than in the same period of 2023. China alone added roughly half a million extra sales compared with a year earlier, and smaller markets outside the top three grew over 50%.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024

"Electric car sales remained strong in the first quarter of 2024, surpassing those of the same period in 2023 by around 25% to reach more than 3 million."

What was the IEA's estimate for total electric car sales in 2024?
The IEA estimated that around 17 million electric cars would be sold in 2024, more than one in five of all cars sold worldwide. This would beat 2023's record by over 20%, with most of the extra sales coming from China and the rest of the world catching up quickly.

Basic c-iea-out-013
How many different electric car models were on sale globally in 2023?
Around 590 electric car models were available globally in 2023, about 15% more than in 2022. Two-thirds of them were SUVs, pick-up trucks or other large cars. Based on manufacturer announcements the number could climb to roughly 1,000 different electric models by 2028.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024

Indirect c-iea-out-014
Why are carmakers focusing on large electric SUVs rather than small models?
Big vehicles bring carmakers bigger profit margins, which matters because most makers still lose money on EVs. Regulatory rules also favour larger cars: US tax credits allow electric SUVs priced up to USD 80,000 versus USD 55,000 for sedans, and buyers willingly pay more for longer range.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car availability and affordability · Page: 31
"Under the US IRA, electric SUVs can qualify for tax credits as long as they are priced under USD 80 000, whereas the limit stands at USD 55 000 for a sedan, creating an incentive to market SUVs"
Medium c-iea-out-015
How much critical-mineral demand could be avoided if all 2023 electric SUVs had been medium-sized cars instead?
Replacing every electric SUV sold in 2023 with a medium-sized electric car would have saved around 60 GWh of batteries. That equates to roughly 6,000 tonnes of lithium, 30,000 tonnes of nickel, 7,000 tonnes of cobalt and 8,000 tonnes of manganese — without much loss of driving range.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car availability and affordability · Page: 33
"around 60 GWh of battery equivalent could have been avoided globally, with limited impact on range. Accounting for the different chemistries used in China, Europe, and the United States, this would be equivalent to almost 6 000 tonnes of lithium, 30 000 tonnes of nickel, almost 7 000 tonnes of cobalt, and over 8 000 tonnes of manganese."
Basic c-iea-out-016
How much has the average driving range of battery electric cars improved since 2015?
The sales-weighted average range of battery electric cars grew almost 75% between 2015 and 2023, thanks to bigger batteries and better technology. Small cars stayed near 150 km, while medium cars and SUVs jumped to roughly 380 km, easing worries about long-distance journeys.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car availability and affordability · Page: 36
"the sales-weighted average range of battery electric cars grew by nearly 75% between 2015 and 2023, although trends vary by segment."
Basic c-iea-out-017
What is total cost of ownership (TCO) when comparing electric and petrol cars?
Total cost of ownership adds together the upfront purchase price, any subsidies and the running costs over time — fuel or electricity, maintenance, insurance and depreciation. Electric cars usually cost more to buy but less to fuel and service, so TCO captures the full economic comparison.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car availability and affordability · Page: 36
"lifetime operating costs, such as fuel costs, insurance, maintenance and depreciation, which together make up the total cost of ownership (TCO)."
Basic c-iea-out-018
What share of electric cars sold in China in 2023 were cheaper than equivalent petrol or diesel cars?
The IEA estimates that more than 60% of the electric cars sold in China in 2023 were already cheaper than the average internal combustion engine equivalent. The share has grown rapidly from under 10% in 2018, helped by fierce price competition and big drops in battery costs.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 1. Trends in electric cars · Section: Electric car availability and affordability · Page: 41
"We estimate that around 55% of the electric cars sold in China in 2022 were cheaper than their average ICE equivalent, up from under 10% in 2018. Given the further price declines between 2022 and 2023, we estimate that this share increased to around 65% in 2023."

China sells nearly 50 small electric models priced under CNY 100,000 (USD 15,000). In the United States in 2023 the cheapest electric cars cost around USD 30,000 and only 5% were cheaper than equivalent petrol cars, leaving a wide gap with mass-market combustion options at USD 20,000.

How big was the used electric car market in 2023?
The market for second-hand electric cars reached about 800,000 vehicles in China, 400,000 in the United States and over 450,000 across six big European countries. Used EV sales in the US are expected to grow another 40% in 2024 as prices fall and federal rebates apply.

China sold nearly 6 million electric two-wheelers in 2023 — roughly 78% of the global total — while India sold about 880,000 and Southeast Asian nations sold 380,000. For three-wheelers India overtook China in 2023 with over 580,000 sales, helped by FAME II subsidies and tax rebates.

Why are electric three-wheelers cheaper to own than petrol versions in India?
Even though an electric auto-rickshaw costs about 55% more to buy than a petrol one, fuel and maintenance savings make it more than 50% cheaper to run over an eight-year life. Subsidies and tax rebates help, but the savings still beat petrol by 40% even without them.

How many electric buses were sold worldwide in 2023?

How fast did electric truck sales grow in 2023?
Global sales of electric trucks rose 35% in 2023 to about 54,000, exceeding electric bus sales for the first time. China led with 70% of these sales, while Europe nearly tripled to over 10,000 and the United States also tripled but only to roughly 1,200 trucks.

Indirect c-iea-out-025
Why do Chinese makers dominate the choice of electric heavy-duty vehicle models?
Chinese manufacturers produce around 430 different battery-electric heavy-duty vehicle models, far more than the 170 in North America and 120 in Europe. A long head-start in their massive home market for electric buses, plus growing sales abroad, has let them spread offerings across buses, medium and heavy trucks.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 3. Trends in heavy electric vehicles · Section: Electric heavy-duty vehicle model availability · Page: 64
"Chinese OEMs currently produce by far the largest number of models of battery electric HDVs – 430 in total – with a particular focus on buses suitable for urban public transport"
Basic c-iea-out-026
How is most electric car charging actually done today?
Most owners charge their cars at home — typically overnight in a private parking space. Home charging is the cheapest and most convenient option, taking advantage of low overnight electricity prices. As a result there are almost ten times as many private chargers worldwide as public ones.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 4. Trends in electric vehicle charging · Section: Charging for electric light-duty vehicles · Page: 68
"Home charging is currently the most common means of charging electric cars. EV owners with access to a private parking space that can be equipped for charging can charge overnight"
Basic c-iea-out-027
How quickly did the global public charger network grow in 2023?
The world's public charging stock grew more than 40% in 2023 versus 2022, with fast chargers expanding even faster, at about 55%. By year-end fast chargers made up over 35% of all public chargers, and China alone hosted more than 85% of the world's fast charging points.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 4. Trends in electric vehicle charging · Section: Charging for electric light-duty vehicles · Page: 70
"The public charging stock increased by more than 40% in 2023, and the growth of fast chargers – which reached 55% outpaced that of slow chargers."
Indirect c-iea-out-028
What does the EU's Alternative Fuels Infrastructure Regulation require for highway chargers?
Under the EU's AFIR, member states must install public fast chargers every 60 km along the main Trans-European Transport Network corridors. The rules guarantee at least 1.3 kW of public charging capacity for each battery electric car and another 0.8 kW for each plug-in hybrid registered.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 4. Trends in electric vehicle charging · Section: Charging for electric light-duty vehicles · Page: 70
"the alternative fuels infrastructure regulation (AFIR), which will require public fast chargers every 60 km along the European Union’s main transport corridors"
Basic c-iea-out-029
What is the Megawatt Charging System (MCS) for trucks?
The Megawatt Charging System is a standard for very-high-power chargers aimed at electric heavy-duty trucks, delivering up to 3.75 megawatts. That level lets a long-haul truck's huge battery refill quickly enough to compete with diesel fuelling stops, and international bodies have started recognising the standard.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 4. Trends in electric vehicle charging · Section: Charging for electric heavy-duty vehicles · Page: 78
"the adoption of the megawatt charging system (MCS) – which allows charging capacity up to 3.75 MW – by international standardisation organisations such as SAE International and the International Organization for Standardization (ISO)."
Basic c-iea-out-030
What is battery swapping and where is it most widely used?
Battery swapping replaces a depleted pack with a fully charged one at a station, often in under five minutes. It is most developed in China, where as many as half of the electric heavy-duty trucks sold in 2023 were built to support swapping, supported by national and city policies.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 4. Trends in electric vehicle charging · Section: Charging for electric heavy-duty vehicles · Page: 78
"Battery swapping can be completed in as little as five minutes, can help to extend battery life through more controlled charging, and can spread power demand over a longer period"
Basic c-iea-out-031
How much total battery demand from electric vehicles was there in 2023?
Global EV battery demand topped 750 GWh in 2023, about 40% higher than the previous year. Electric cars drove 95% of that growth. China bought roughly 415 GWh, Europe 185 GWh and the United States about 100 GWh, with the rest of the world growing fastest from a small base.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 5. Trends in electric vehicle batteries · Section: Battery supply and demand · Page: 78
"Demand for EV batteries reached more than 750 GWh in 2023, up 40% relative to 2022"
Basic c-iea-out-032
How much lithium did electric vehicle batteries use in 2023?
Battery demand for lithium reached about 140,000 tonnes in 2023, accounting for 85% of total lithium use and rising more than 30% over 2022. Demand for cobalt from batteries hit 150,000 tonnes (70% of the total), while battery-related nickel demand approached 370,000 tonnes.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 5. Trends in electric vehicle batteries · Section: Battery supply and demand · Page: 81
"Battery demand for lithium stood at around 140 kt in 2023, 85% of total lithium demand and up more than 30% compared to 2022"
Basic c-iea-out-033
How much did lithium-ion battery pack prices change in 2023?
After a 7% rise in 2022 caused by turmoil in metal markets, lithium-ion battery pack prices fell almost 14% in 2023 as cobalt, graphite and manganese prices dropped. It was the largest annual battery-price decline since 2020, helping bring electric cars closer to price parity.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 5. Trends in electric vehicle batteries · Section: Battery prices · Page: 83
"This led to an almost 14% fall in battery pack price between 2023 and 2022, despite lithium carbonate prices at the end of 2023 still being about 50% higher than their 2015-2020 average."
Basic c-iea-out-034
What is a lithium iron phosphate (LFP) battery and how popular is it?
An LFP battery uses iron and phosphate in its positive electrode instead of nickel and cobalt, making it cheaper and longer-lasting at the cost of slightly less energy per kilogram. LFP supplied more than 40% of EV battery capacity worldwide in 2023, double its share in 2020.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 5. Trends in electric vehicle batteries · Section: Battery prices · Page: 85
"LFP has moved from a minor share to the rising star of the battery industry, supplying more than 40% of EV demand globally by capacity in 2023, more than double the share recorded in 2020."
Indirect c-iea-out-035
Why are sodium-ion batteries seen as a promising future option?
Sodium-ion batteries can be made on existing lithium-ion production lines but use no lithium at all, easing pressure on scarce minerals. If scaled up they could cost as much as 20% less than today's lithium batteries, suiting small urban EVs and stationary power storage applications.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 5. Trends in electric vehicle batteries · Section: Battery prices · Page: 86
"If brought to scale, sodium-ion batteries could cost up to 20% less than incumbent technologies and be suitable for applications such as compact urban EVs and power stationary storage"
Basic c-iea-out-036
Which two companies led global electric car sales in 2023?
BYD and Tesla led the global electric car market, together accounting for about 35% of all electric car sales in 2023. BYD overtook Tesla as the world's best-selling battery electric carmaker in the second half of the year, and its worldwide sales (BEV plus PHEV) topped 3 million.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 6. Trends in the electric vehicle industry · Section: Electric vehicle company strategy and market competition · Page: 91
"BYD and Tesla remain far ahead of the curve, together accounting for 35% of all electric car sales in 2023."

Tesla earned roughly USD 10,000 to USD 15,000 of profit per electric car sold in 2022-2023, mainly thanks to its focus on premium models. BYD made about USD 6,000 per car by selling cheaper models and keeping costs down through in-house battery supply chains.
