How many EVs did China export in 2023?
China exported about 1.2 million electric vehicles in 2023, part of a total of over 4 million cars shipped abroad. EV exports rose roughly 80% from 2022, helping China overtake Japan and Germany to become the world's largest car exporter, with Europe and Asia Pacific as main destinations.

Basic c-iea-out-039

Early-stage venture capital invested in EV and battery start-ups dropped about 20% to USD 1.4 billion in 2023, while later-stage growth-equity deals fell 35% to USD 10.1 billion. Charging start-ups raised USD 400 million and battery makers USD 260 million in early-stage rounds.

Basic c-iea-out-040
What are the three IEA scenarios used to project the future of electric mobility?
The IEA uses three scenarios: the Stated Policies Scenario (STEPS), which counts only laws already on the books; the Announced Pledges Scenario (APS), which assumes all government promises are kept; and the Net Zero Emissions by 2050 Scenario (NZE), a path consistent with limiting warming to 1.5C.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 7. Outlook for electric mobility · Section: Scenario overview · Page: 104
"Stated Policies Scenario (STEPS) and Announced Pledges Scenario (APS) consider historical data through the end of 2023, as well as stated policies and ambitions as of the end of March 2024. The Net Zero Emissions by 2050 Scenario (NZE Scenario)"
Basic c-iea-out-041
How large is the global electric vehicle fleet expected to be by 2035 under stated policies?
Under the Stated Policies Scenario the global EV stock excluding two- and three-wheelers grows from under 45 million in 2023 to 250 million in 2030 and 525 million in 2035 — meaning more than one in four vehicles on the world's roads would be electric.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 7. Outlook for electric mobility · Section: Vehicle outlook by mode · Page: 104
"the stock of EVs across all modes except for two/three-wheelers (2/3Ws), grows from less than 45 million in 2023 to 250 million in 2030 and reaches 525 million in 2035."
Basic c-iea-out-042
What share of new car sales in China could be electric by 2025?
China's Automotive Industry Green and Low-Carbon Development Roadmap 1.0 anticipates that passenger new energy vehicle sales could reach a 50% share as early as 2025, a full decade ahead of the previous 2035 target. Sales then keep rising to about two-thirds in 2030 and 85% in 2035.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 7. Outlook for electric mobility · Section: Vehicle outlook by region · Page: 118
"passenger new energy vehicle (NEV) sales could reach a 50% share as soon as 2025, as stated in the recent Automotive Industry Green and Low-Carbon Development Roadmap 1.0"
Indirect c-iea-out-043
How much has been invested in EV and battery manufacturing in 2022 and 2023?
Reported industry announcements from 2022 and 2023 totalled more than USD 275 billion for EV manufacturing and USD 195 billion for batteries, of which roughly USD 190 billion has already been committed. This boom in capital signals strong industry confidence in a rapid electrification path.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 7. Outlook for electric mobility · Section: The industry outlook · Page: 121
"reported investment announcements from 2022 and 2023 alone exceed USD 275 billion in EVs and USD 195 billion in batteries, with around USD 190 billion of the total already committed."
Basic c-iea-out-044
How many public chargers are expected globally by 2035?
Under the Announced Pledges Scenario the world will need around 25 million public chargers by 2035 — about six times the four million in service at end-2023. The number could already pass 15 million by 2030 as charging buildouts try to keep pace with rapid EV uptake.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 8. Outlook for electric vehicle charging infrastructure · Section: Light-duty vehicle charging · Page: 126
"the global number of public charging points exceeds 15 million by 2030, up four-fold compared to the almost 4 million operating in 2023. By 2035, this number reaches almost 25 million in the APS, a sixfold increase relative to 2023."
Medium c-iea-out-045
Why could daytime charging of electric trucks help integrate solar power?
Solar panels generate the most electricity around midday and afternoon. Charging trucks at loading docks or highway stops during those hours absorbs that solar output, balancing supply and demand and reducing the need to curtail excess solar — turning a potential grid headache into useful flexibility.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 8. Outlook for electric vehicle charging infrastructure · Section: Heavy-duty vehicle charging · Page: 135
"Daytime charging can more directly support solar PV integration, as loading dock or en-route charging increases demand between midday and the afternoon, when solar PV production is high"
Basic c-iea-out-046
How much will global EV battery demand grow by 2035?
EV battery demand grows about seven times by 2035 under the Stated Policies Scenario, nine times in the Announced Pledges Scenario, and twelve times in the Net Zero Scenario. In the APS in 2035, weekly battery demand will match a full year's demand back in 2019.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 9. Outlook for battery and energy demand · Section: Battery demand · Page: 142
"In the STEPS, EV battery demand grows fourand-a-half times by 2030, and almost seven times by 2035 compared to 2023. In the APS and the NZE Scenario, demand is significantly higher, multiplied by five and seven times in 2030 and nine and twelve times in 2035"
Basic c-iea-out-047
How much battery recycling capacity existed in 2023, and how much is planned by 2030?
Global battery recycling capacity reached more than 300 GWh per year in 2023, of which over 80% sat in China. If announced projects all proceed, capacity could exceed 1,500 GWh by 2030, with 70% in China and roughly 10% each in Europe and the United States.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 9. Outlook for battery and energy demand · Section: Battery demand · Page: 145
"Global recycling capacity reached over 300 GWh/year in 2023, of which more than 80% was located in China"
Basic c-iea-out-048
What share of total electricity demand will EVs use by 2035?
In 2023 electric vehicles took just 0.5% of the world's electricity. By 2035 that share rises to roughly 8% under the Stated Policies Scenario and almost 10% under the Announced Pledges Scenario. The United States and Europe show the largest jumps to around 14-15%.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 9. Outlook for battery and energy demand · Section: Electricity demand · Page: 148
"EVs accounted for about 0.5% of the world’s total final electricity consumption in 2023"
Basic c-iea-out-049
How much oil demand will EVs displace by 2035?
Growing EV fleets will displace about 6 million barrels of oil per day in 2030 and 11-12 million by 2035, with most savings coming from cars, then trucks, buses and two-wheelers. Global demand for oil-based road transport fuels is expected to peak around 2025.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 9. Outlook for battery and energy demand · Section: Oil displacement · Page: 151
"the projected EV fleet displaces 6 million barrels per day (mb/d) of diesel and gasoline in 2030, a sixfold increase on displacement in 2023. By 2035, even less oil is needed for road transport, with displacement reaching 11 mb/d in the STEPS and 12 mb/d in the APS."
Medium c-iea-out-050
How do the lifetime emissions of a battery electric car compare with a petrol car?
A medium-sized battery electric car sold in 2023 emits about half as much greenhouse gas over its life as an equivalent petrol car when production, electricity generation and tailpipe emissions are all counted. By 2035, with cleaner grids, a petrol car emits more than two-and-a-half times as much.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024
Chapter: 10. Outlook for emissions reductions · Section: Lifecycle impacts of electric cars · Page: 155
"the lifecycle emissions of a medium-size battery electric car are about half of those of an equivalent ICEV that is running on oil-based fuels"

9. Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide

various · EV Knowledge Guide (June 2022) · 50 Q&As

Basic c-evg-001
What does AC stand for in EV terminology?
AC stands for alternating current. It refers to a charge of electricity that regularly changes direction along the wire. AC is the most common type of power supplied to homes and businesses, so home outlets generally deliver electricity in this form by default.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Glossary · Page: 5
"AC (Alternating Current): A charge of electricity that regularly changes direction."
Basic c-evg-002
What does DC stand for in EV terminology?
DC stands for direct current. It refers to a charge of electricity that flows in just one direction along the wire, without reversing. This is the type of power supplied by a battery, so a vehicle's pack inherently delivers DC.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Glossary · Page: 5
"DC (Direct Current): A charge"
Indirect c-evg-003
Why is a BEV electric motor much more efficient than an internal combustion engine?
BEV electric motors turn about 85 to 90 percent of the electricity they receive into useful rotation at the wheels. An internal combustion engine is only around 25 percent efficient, because most of the fuel energy escapes as wasted heat and noise.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: BEV vs ICE · Page: 5
"the electric motors convert 85-90% of the energy into turning the wheels."
Basic c-evg-004
What is the efficiency of an internal combustion engine vehicle, according to the guide?
An internal combustion engine vehicle is only about 25 percent efficient at using the energy stored in its fuel to move the car. The other 75 percent of the chemical energy in the fuel escapes as wasted heat and noise.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: ICE · Page: 5
"ICE vehicles are only about 25% efficient at utilizing the stored energy in the fuel"
Basic c-evg-005
How is the energy stored in an EV battery typically measured?
The amount of electric energy stored in an EV battery is normally measured in kilowatt-hours, written as kWh. One kilowatt-hour is the energy used by a one-kilowatt appliance running for an hour, so a larger kWh figure means more driving range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: kWh · Page: 5
"The amount of electric energy stored in an EV battery is typically measured in kilowatt-hours."
Basic c-evg-006
What voltage does a Level 1 EV charger use?
Level 1 charging uses a common household outlet supplying up to 120 volts. This is the same socket type used for everyday appliances, which means the owner can begin charging on day one without installing any dedicated electrical equipment at home.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Level 1 Charging · Page: 5
"Charging an EV using a common household outlet up to 120 volts."
Basic c-evg-007
How long does a Level 1 charger take to fully refill an EV?
Level 1 charging is the slowest method available to an EV owner. Using a regular 120-volt household outlet, it can take roughly 9 to 12 hours or even more to fully recharge a battery electric vehicle from empty to full.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Level 1 Charging · Page: 5
"This is the slowest method of charging and can take up to 9-12 hours"
Basic c-evg-008
What voltage does a Level 2 EV charger use?
A Level 2 charger uses an installed station at 240 volts to top up the battery. That is twice the voltage of a household outlet, which is why most EV manufacturers recommend Level 2 charging to owners for everyday home use.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Level 2 Charging · Page: 5
"Charging your EV using an installed charging station at 240 volts."
Indirect c-evg-009
How long does Level 2 charging typically take for a BEV versus a PHEV?
Level 2 charging can fully refill a BEV battery in roughly 5 to 10 hours, depending on the model and the charger output. For a PHEV, which has a much smaller battery, the same Level 2 charger can finish the job in just 2 to 4 hours.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Level 2 Charging · Page: 5
"Level 2 charging can fully charge an EV within 5-10 hours for BEVs, and 2-4 hours for PHEVs"
Basic c-evg-010
What is another common name for Level 3 charging?
Level 3 charging is also known as DC fast charging, or DCFC for short. It is the fastest charging method available for an EV because it uses much higher power and higher voltage than a Level 2 station does.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Level 3 Charging · Page: 5
"Also known as “DC fast charging” or “DCFC”, this is the fastest method of charging for all EVs"
Basic c-evg-011
How quickly can a Level 3 charger top an EV up to 80 percent?
A Level 3 fast charger can bring an EV battery up to 80 percent capacity in about 30 minutes or less. That makes it the practical option for long road trips when drivers need to recover range quickly during a short stop.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Level 3 Charging · Page: 5
"Level 3 charging can charge an EV battery to 80% in about 30 minutes or less."
Indirect c-evg-012
Why are Level 3 charging stations still relatively uncommon?
Level 3 chargers only work with certain types of EVs that support fast charging. They are also more expensive and need much more electrical power than Level 2 stations, so installers tend to deploy them more sparingly along highway corridors.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Level 3 Charging · Page: 5
"they’re more expensive and require more power than Level 2 charging."
Indirect c-evg-013
What is a networked EV charging station?
A networked charging station can talk with other stations and to a server or cloud over a cellular or wireless link. That lets owners report on usage, show real-time charging status, do remote troubleshooting, and accept pay-for-use charging from drivers.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Networked Charging · Page: 5
"EV charging stations with the ability to communicate to other stations and/or to a server or the cloud"
Basic c-evg-014
What is a PHEV?
PHEV stands for plug-in hybrid electric vehicle. It is like a regular hybrid but has a larger battery that can be plugged in for recharging. Most PHEVs can drive 25 to 75 kilometres on the battery alone before the engine turns on.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: PHEV · Page: 5
"PHEVs are like HEVs but have larger batteries that can be plugged in for recharging."
Indirect c-evg-015
How does regenerative braking benefit an EV driver?
Regenerative braking slows the moving EV by capturing kinetic energy and storing it back in the battery as electricity. That extends the driving range on each charge and reduces friction-brake wear, leading to less frequent and less costly repair work over time.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 2.0 Glossary of Terms · Section: Regenerative Braking · Page: 5
"regenerative braking extends the EV driving range and reduces brake wear leading to less frequent and less"
Medium c-evg-016
How quickly did EV registrations grow in Canada from 2020 to 2021?
About 74,000 new EVs hit Canadian roads in 2021, making up 3.79 percent of all new vehicle registrations that year. That was a 51 percent increase in registrations compared with 2020, indicating very rapid early adoption of the technology among Canadian drivers.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 3.0 Benefits · Section: 3.1 Vehicle of the future · Page: 5
"EVs made up 3.79% of all new vehicle registrations in 2021, a 51% increase in registrations compared to 2020"
Indirect c-evg-017
What is the iZEV federal incentive available at point of sale in Canada?
Through the federal iZEV programme, buyers receive an extra incentive of 2,500 to 5,000 dollars at the point of sale per vehicle. Municipalities can stack this incentive with the provincial EVM rebate, reaching up to about 19,000 dollars total on a passenger vehicle.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 3.0 Benefits · Section: 3.2 Funding available · Page: 5
"an additional incentive of"
Medium c-evg-018
By how much can switching to an EV cut annual fuel and maintenance costs in Alberta?
In Alberta, operating an EV instead of a conventional vehicle can lower yearly fuel and maintenance costs by up to 72 percent. The exact savings depend on the vehicle type chosen and on the current local cost of fuel and electricity.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 3.0 Benefits · Section: 3.4 Operational benefits · Page: 5
"could reduce annual fuel and maintenance costs up to 72%"
Basic c-evg-019
How many fewer moving parts does a typical EV drivetrain have compared with a gasoline car?
A typical EV drivetrain has around 90 percent fewer moving parts than a comparable internal combustion engine drivetrain. That reduces the amount of routine maintenance required and helps keep total ownership costs down for the driver over the life of the vehicle.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 3.0 Benefits · Section: 3.4 Operational benefits · Page: 5
"Typical EV drivetrains have 90% fewer moving parts"
Medium c-evg-020
How quickly does a Nissan Leaf BEV pay back its extra manufacturing emissions?
A battery electric vehicle typically offsets its excess manufacturing emissions within the first 6 to 16 months of operation. After that, the absence of tailpipe emissions means it keeps emitting far less than an equivalent gasoline car would across its life.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 3.0 Benefits · Section: 3.4 Operational benefits · Page: 5
"BEVs typically offset their excess manufacturing emissions within the first 6-16 months of operation"
Indirect c-evg-021
What happens to EV batteries when they reach the end of their first life?
When a battery is replaced, it is not dumped in landfill, since that is illegal. Manufacturers repurpose batteries in second-life applications such as renewable energy storage and battery backup systems, where they can serve for roughly another decade before recycling.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 3.0 Benefits · Section: Battery end of life · Page: 6
"they are not dumped into landfills (it is illegal to do so)"
Basic c-evg-022
How far can a new BEV typically drive on a single charge in Alberta?
According to the guide, new battery electric vehicles can travel up to 400 kilometres or more on a single charge. That comfortably covers the average Albertan commuter's daily needs and is steadily reducing what used to be called range anxiety among drivers.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: 4.1 Can EVs travel far distances? · Page: 6
"New BEVs can travel up to 400+ km on a single charge"
Indirect c-evg-023
How much battery capacity does a typical EV lose each year?
A US study found that the average EV battery loses about 1 percent of its cycling capacity per year over a 10-year span. Real-world degradation varies with how the driver uses the vehicle and how often they charge to full each time.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: 4.2 How long do EV batteries last? · Page: 6
"the average battery cycling capacity loss over a 10-year timeframe was about 1% pe r year"
Indirect c-evg-024
When is it considered time to retire an EV battery?
Rather than a fixed timeframe, an EV battery should be retired only when its remaining capacity can no longer cover the driver's typical daily needs. As long as the daily commute fits inside what's left of the pack, the battery still works fine.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: 4.2 How long do EV batteries last? · Page: 6
"the retirement of an EV battery should occur when the battery no longer satisfies the daily travel needs of a driver"
Basic c-evg-025
What are some best practices to keep an EV battery healthy?
The guide recommends limiting vehicle use during very high temperatures, avoiding parking in direct sun on hot days, avoiding deep discharges where most of the pack is drained, and avoiding aggressive driving. It also suggests using Level 3 fast charging only when necessary.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: Battery care · Page: 8
"Limit the frequency of deep battery discharges where most of the battery capacity is drained"
Indirect c-evg-026
Why does an EV need less maintenance than a gasoline car?
An EV has very few moving parts, no oil changes to perform, and no spark plugs to replace. That means much less routine maintenance is needed compared with a conventional vehicle, which translates into real financial savings for the owner over time.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: 4.3 What kind of maintenance is required? · Page: 8
"There are no oil changes or spark plugs replacements needed."
Indirect c-evg-027
Why do EVs perform well in cold winter weather compared with gasoline vehicles?
An EV has no oil and no combustion engine, so the cold cannot thicken its oil or stop the engine from turning over. The battery can still start the vehicle on the coldest days, and resistance heating warms the cabin almost instantly without idling.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: 4.4 Do they work in the winter? · Page: 8
"With an EV, there is no oil or combustion engine"
Medium c-evg-028
How much can cold-weather heating reduce an EV's battery range?
Running resistance heating warms the cabin almost immediately, but it does consume battery energy. The guide notes that heating use can draw down the pack by as much as 30 to 40 percent in some cases, although the typical daily commute is still manageable.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: 4.4 Do they work in the winter? · Page: 8
"in some cases, upwards of 30 to 40%"

What share of new cars sold in Norway in March 2019 were fully electric?
In March 2019, almost 60 percent of all new cars sold in Norway were fully electric. The guide uses this fact as evidence that EV adoption can succeed in cold winter climates similar to Alberta's, where ICE vehicles sometimes struggle to start.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide

Basic c-evg-030
How can EV drivers maximize their cold-weather range?
Drivers can keep the EV stored in a heated garage, plug it in when not in use, limit the cabin heater while driving, and switch to eco-mode to adjust performance parameters. These small habits help preserve battery energy for actual driving.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 4.0 FAQ · Section: Cold-weather tips · Page: 8
"Keep your EV stored in a garage (ideally heated)"

Indirect c-evg-034
Why is lifecycle analysis important when comparing EVs and ICE vehicles?
Manufacturing the battery for an EV releases more CO2 than building a gasoline car, but ICE vehicles emit far more during use due to constant tailpipe pollution. Looking at the full lifecycle lets a fair comparison emerge across both manufacturing and operating emissions.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide

Basic c-evg-035
What does the Level 1 charger physically connect to in a home?
A Level 1 charger is a regular 120-volt household plug, used with an adapter to connect to an electric vehicle. The Level 1 cordset typically comes bundled with the purchase of a passenger EV, so the owner has it ready on delivery day.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide

"A Level 1 charger is a regular 120-volt household plug that utilizes an adapter to charge an electric vehicle."
Basic c-evg-036
What standard connector does a Level 2 charger use in Canada and the US?
Level 2 charging stations use the SAE J1772 plug, the standard adopted by Canadian and American EV manufacturers for cross-compatibility. Because nearly every vehicle on the road in those countries supports it, public Level 2 stations typically share this same plug type.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 5.0 Charging 101 · Section: Level 2 chargers · Page: 10
"a standard connector (SAE J1772 plug) adopted by Canadian and American electric vehicle manufacturers"
Indirect c-evg-037
What household appliance shares the same outlet voltage as a Level 2 EV charger?
A Level 2 charging station plugs into the same 240-volt outlet used by a clothes dryer or an electric oven. Because most homes already have that circuit available, installation is often straightforward and avoids any major electrical panel rework for the homeowner.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 5.0 Charging 101 · Section: Level 2 chargers · Page: 10
"plug into the same 240V outlet that a clothes dryer or oven would use"
Basic c-evg-038
What two plug types do Level 3 chargers commonly use?
Level 3 chargers use the CHAdeMO connector and the SAE Combo CCS, which stands for combined charging system. Older EVs may not be able to use them at all, but fast-charging capability is rapidly becoming standard equipment on newer EV models.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 5.0 Charging 101 · Section: Level 3 chargers · Page: 10
"This type of charger utilizes the CHAdeMO and SAE Combo CCS"
Indirect c-evg-039
Why should EV drivers check charging-station compatibility before driving to one?
Not every vehicle works with every charger type. For example, the Chevrolet Volt, a plug-in hybrid, is not compatible with Level 3 fast charging stations. Checking ahead avoids arriving at a station only to find that the vehicle cannot use it.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 5.0 Charging 101 · Section: 5.3 Locating charging stations · Page: 12
"Some vehicles, like the Chevrolet Volt (a PHEV), are not compatible with Level 3 stations."
Indirect c-evg-040
What is OCPP and why does it matter for EV charging stations?
OCPP stands for Open Charge Point Protocol, an open syntax language for talking between networked stations and management systems. Choosing an OCPP-compliant station lets the owner freely switch networks later, avoiding being locked into one vendor's fees and infrastructure.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
Chapter: 5.0 Charging 101 · Section: 5.5 Open Source Charging Stations · Page: 12
"Open Charge Point Protocol or OCPP is a syntax language that is used to communicate with other networked charging stations"
Indirect c-evg-041
Where do fast charging stations make the most operational sense?
Fast chargers fit best at sites where the vehicle will only be parked for about 30 minutes, such as highway rest stops and downtown cafes. Level 2 stations suit locations where drivers will linger for hours, like shopping malls, gyms, or parks.
Source: Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide

10. Electric Vehicle Basics

US Department of Energy · US Department of Energy (DOE) · 50 Q&As

Basic c-doe-001
What does the term 'EV' cover according to the US DOE?
The label EV is used by the DOE for vehicles that run on electricity as their primary fuel or to improve efficiency. It includes all-electric vehicles, also called battery electric vehicles or BEVs, and plug-in hybrid electric vehicles, called PHEVs.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Overview · Page: 2
"EVs include all-electric vehicles, also referred to as battery electric vehicles (BEVs), and plug-in hybrid electric vehicles (PHEVs)."
Basic c-doe-002
What driving feel do EVs offer compared with gasoline cars?
EVs are known for delivering instant torque the moment the driver presses the pedal, plus a quiet ride. There is no engine roaring under the hood, which makes the cabin much calmer than in a typical gasoline-powered vehicle on the road.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Overview · Page: 2
"EVs are known for providing instant torque and a quiet driver experience."
Indirect c-doe-003
How do fuel cell electric vehicles differ from battery electric vehicles?
Fuel cell electric vehicles use a propulsion system similar to BEVs, but the onboard energy is stored as hydrogen rather than in a battery. A fuel cell then converts that hydrogen into electricity to drive the motor, instead of drawing from a plug-charged pack.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Overview · Page: 2
"fuel cell electric vehicles, which use a propulsion system similar to electric vehicles, where energy stored as hydrogen is converted to electricity by the fuel cell."
Basic c-doe-004
How are batteries in all-electric vehicles recharged?
Batteries in all-electric vehicles are recharged by plugging the vehicle into an outside electric power source. They can also be topped up by regenerative braking, which captures energy that would otherwise be wasted as heat in the brake hardware itself.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: All-Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"an electric power source and can also be charged through regenerative braking."
Basic c-doe-005
Do all-electric vehicles produce tailpipe emissions while driving?
No, an all-electric vehicle has no exhaust pipe and emits nothing at the wheels itself. There are still life-cycle emissions tied to producing the electricity that charges it, but the vehicle itself emits zero pollutants directly during normal use on the road.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: All-Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"All-electric vehicles produce no tailpipe emissions, although there are “life cycle” emissions associated with the electricity production."
Basic c-doe-006
What driving range do most new BEVs offer on a single charge?
Most new battery electric vehicles are designed to travel between 110 and over 300 miles on a full charge, depending on the specific model chosen. Actual range varies with how the car is driven and the weather conditions during the trip itself.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: All-Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"Most new BEVs are designed to travel between 110 and over 300 miles on a fully charged battery, depending on the model."
Indirect c-doe-007
Why is the 100-mile reference distance for EV range significant for US drivers?
Roughly 90 percent of all US household trips cover less than 100 miles in a single journey. So a BEV with a 110-plus-mile range can comfortably handle the vast majority of everyday driving without any worry about recharging mid-trip on the road.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: All-Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"90% of all U.S. household trips cover less than 100 miles."
Indirect c-doe-008
Why do extreme temperatures tend to reduce an EV's range?
In very hot or cold weather the battery has to power the cabin climate-control system as well as the drive motor. Heating or cooling the cabin draws extra energy from the same pack, which means fewer kilowatt-hours are left to push the car forward.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: All-Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"Extreme temperatures tend to reduce range because energy from the battery powers climate control systems in addition to powering the motor."
Basic c-doe-009
Which driving habits can reduce an EV's range?
Speeding, aggressive acceleration, and carrying heavy loads can all cut the distance an EV achieves between charges on the road. These behaviours force the motor to draw more current from the battery, draining the pack faster than gentler driving would do.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: All-Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"Speeding, aggressive driving, and heavy loads can also reduce range."
Basic c-doe-010
What does regenerative braking do on an electric vehicle?
Regenerative braking lets the EV capture energy normally lost when slowing down to a stop. It does this by running the electric motor in reverse as a generator and feeding the recovered electricity back into the battery to extend the driving range.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Regenerative Braking · Page: 2
"Regenerative braking allows EVs to capture energy normally lost during braking by using the electric motor as a generator and storing that captured energy in the battery."
Basic c-doe-011
How is a PHEV powered?
A plug-in hybrid uses a battery to drive an electric motor and also carries a conventional engine that burns another fuel, usually gasoline. The car can run on stored electricity for short trips and then switch to the engine when the battery runs low.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Plug-In Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"PHEVs use batteries to power an electric motor and use another fuel, such as gasoline, to power a conventional engine."
Basic c-doe-012
What is the all-electric driving range of a typical PHEV?
A typical plug-in hybrid can travel roughly 15 to 60 miles or more on the battery alone, depending on the specific model chosen. After that, the conventional engine kicks in to provide extra range using the liquid fuel stored in the tank.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Plug-In Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"PHEVs have an all-electric driving range of about 15 to 60+ miles, depending on the model."
Indirect c-doe-013
Can a PHEV be driven without ever being plugged in?
Yes, a plug-in hybrid does not have to be plugged in before being driven and can run solely on conventional liquid fuel. However, skipping the charging step means the driver will not get maximum fuel economy or the full electric-driving benefit.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Plug-In Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"PHEVs don’t have to be plugged in before driving. They can also be fueled solely with conventional fuel."
Indirect c-doe-014
When does the engine in a PHEV typically switch on?
The engine turns on when the battery is mostly depleted, during rapid acceleration, at high cruising speeds, or when the cabin needs intense heating or air conditioning. Otherwise the car prefers to use the electric motor for typical daily driving.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Plug-In Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"The engine will then power on when the battery is mostly depleted, during rapid acceleration, at high speeds, or when intensive heating or air conditioning is required."
Basic c-doe-015
Do PHEVs emit pollutants when running purely on the battery?
No, when a plug-in hybrid is drawing only on battery power, no tailpipe pollutants come out at all. Even once the gasoline engine kicks in, PHEVs typically burn less fuel and emit less than a comparable conventional car on the road.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Plug-In Hybrid Electric Vehicles · Page: 2
"When running on battery power alone, PHEVs produce no tailpipe emissions."
Basic c-doe-016
How many publicly available charging outlets exist across the United States?
The DOE notes there are more than 140,000 publicly available charging outlets across the country at present, and the network continues to grow. That widening network helps ease the worry of running out of charge on longer drives.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do These Vehicles Fuel Up? · Page: 2
"There are more than 140,000 publicly available charging outlets— and counting— across the country."
Indirect c-doe-017
What is 'range anxiety' and how is it being addressed?
Range anxiety is the fear of running out of charge before reaching a destination. Larger batteries on newer EVs and a fast-growing public charging network are steadily reducing this worry by giving drivers more miles per charge and more places to refill.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do These Vehicles Fuel Up? · Page: 2
"Technological advances such as larger batteries and growing access to charging are increasingly addressing “range anxiety,” or the fear of running out of charge."
Basic c-doe-018
What is the minimum time it can take to fully charge an EV battery?
Under the right conditions a battery can be topped up in as little as 30 minutes from empty. The exact time depends on the charger type, the size and state of the battery, and the rating of the vehicle's onboard charger hardware.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do These Vehicles Fuel Up? · Page: 2
"It may take as little as 30 minutes to fully charge an EV’s battery, but charging times vary based on the type or level of charging"
Basic c-doe-019
What kind of cordset is included with most new EVs?
Most EVs come with a 110-volt Level 1 cordset that simply plugs into a typical wall outlet at home. This basic cable allows the owner to begin charging on day one without needing to install any new electrical equipment in the house.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do These Vehicles Fuel Up? · Page: 2
"Most EVs come with a 110-volt “Level 1” cordset that can be plugged into a typical electrical outlet."
Indirect c-doe-020
Why is installing a Level 2 charger at home often straightforward?
Most American homes already have a 240-volt service available for appliances such as electric dryers and ranges. A Level 2 charging unit taps into that same circuit, so the upgrade often needs little or no extra electrical work to set up.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do These Vehicles Fuel Up? · Page: 2
"This can often be done with little or no required electrical upgrades, as most homes have 240-V service for appliances like dryers and electric ranges."
Basic c-doe-021
What is the lowest possible purchase price the DOE quotes for a Level 2 unit?
A Level 2 charging unit can be purchased for as little as 200 US dollars, according to the DOE document. It can be wall-mounted permanently in a building or kept portable, depending on the homeowner's preference and the home electrical setup.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do These Vehicles Fuel Up? · Page: 2
"A Level 2 unit can be portable or “hard wired” into a building"
Indirect c-doe-022
What are designated EV corridors in the United States?
These are stretches of highway where DC fast charging stations are being installed at regular intervals along the route. The Federal Highway Administration is setting up this network so drivers can complete long trips by topping up quickly along the way.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do These Vehicles Fuel Up? · Page: 2
"Designated EV corridors2 supported by DC fast charging stations are under development nationwide."
Basic c-doe-023
Why do EV owners typically charge at home rather than at public stations?
Home charging is generally more convenient and more cost-effective than using public stations on the road. Most EV owners therefore plug in overnight at home or during the workday at the office, treating public chargers mostly as a backup for trips.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Made Simple · Page: 2
"Most EV owners charge at home or at work because charging is more convenient and cost-effective than using public stations."
Indirect c-doe-024
Why are electricity prices considered an advantage of going electric?
Electricity prices are less volatile than gasoline and diesel prices, which can swing up and down with oil markets. That stability lets EV drivers forecast their fuelling expenses month to month with much more confidence than gasoline car owners can.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Made Simple · Page: 2
"electricity prices are less volatile than gasoline and diesel prices, so drivers can more easily forecast their fueling expenses."
Basic c-doe-025
What charging rate does a Level 1 station typically deliver?
A Level 1 station typically adds about 2 to 5 miles of driving range for every hour of charging the vehicle. That is slow, so it suits overnight top-ups for short daily commutes rather than recovering range quickly during the day.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"miles of range per hour of charging"
Basic c-doe-026
How much range does a Level 2 charger typically add per hour?
A Level 2 station adds roughly 10 to 30 miles of driving range every hour that the vehicle is plugged in. That makes it well suited for overnight home charging or a few hours plugged in at work, comfortably covering most daily commutes.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"Charging Options"
Basic c-doe-027
What does a DC fast charging station deliver in 30 minutes?
A DC fast charging station can add 100 to over 200 miles of driving range in roughly 30 minutes of plugged-in time. That makes it the practical option for highway road trips when drivers need to recover range quickly during a short stop.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"100-200+ miles of range in 30 minutes"
Medium c-doe-028
How does the equipment cost of a Level 1 setup compare with a DC fast charging unit?
A Level 1 setup is essentially free to as much as 1,800 US dollars to install at a site. A DC fast charging unit, by contrast, runs from 30,000 to over 120,000 dollars, because higher power ratings demand much more expensive hardware and wiring.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"Costs do not include the price of operation"
Basic c-doe-029
What is the typical power-output range of a Level 2 unit?
A Level 2 charging unit usually operates somewhere between 6.6 and 19.2 kilowatts of output power at the plug. The higher its power rating, the faster it charges the car and the more expensive the unit and its wiring tend to be.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"A Level 2 unit can range from 6.6 to 19.2 kW output."
Basic c-doe-030
What is the power range of a DC fast charging unit?
A DC fast charging unit can range from 25 kilowatts at the low end to 350 kilowatts at the high end of the scale. More powerful units add miles to the battery faster but also cost much more to buy and to install.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"A DCFC unit can range from 25 to 350 kW."
Indirect c-doe-031
Why does the onboard equipment matter for Level 1 and Level 2 charging?
Both Level 1 and Level 2 chargers deliver alternating current, but EV batteries store direct current internally. The vehicle's onboard charger therefore has to convert the incoming AC into DC before it can be used to refill the battery itself.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"vehicle’s onboard equipment converting AC to DC to charge the batteries"
Indirect c-doe-032
What makes DC fast charging faster than Level 1 or Level 2?
DC fast chargers send direct current straight into the battery, skipping the conversion step normally done by the car's onboard charger. With more raw power flowing in, the pack refills much faster than it would using AC charging alone.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"DC fast charging (DCFC)— provides DC power directly."
Basic c-doe-033
What is wireless or inductive EV charging?
Wireless charging equipment uses an electromagnetic field to transfer electricity from a pad to the vehicle without any cable. It is mostly used today at higher power levels for heavy-duty applications such as transit buses parked over an in-ground pad.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Charging Options · Page: 3
"Wireless or “inductive” charging equipment uses an electromagnetic field to transfer electricity to an EV without a cord."
Indirect c-doe-034
Why are EVs described as more than three times as efficient as gasoline cars?
Electric drivetrains turn a far larger share of their stored energy into actual motion at the wheels than internal-combustion engines do. The DOE notes that BEVs and PHEVs running in electric mode are more than three times as efficient as conventional vehicles.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Much Do the Vehicles Cost? · Page: 3
"electric drivetrains are more efficient, making BEVs (and PHEVs operating in electric mode) more than three times as efficient."
Medium c-doe-035
How much can a BEV driver save on fuel over 15 years?
The DOE estimates that a battery electric vehicle driver can save as much as 14,500 US dollars on fuel costs alone over a 15-year ownership period. That assumes electricity remains cheaper than gasoline on an energy-equivalent basis throughout the time owned.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Much Do the Vehicles Cost? · Page: 3
"BEV drivers can save as much as"
Basic c-doe-036
How do tailpipe emissions of all-electric vehicles compare to conventional cars?
All-electric vehicles produce zero tailpipe emissions whenever they are running on battery power alone. Conventional cars, by contrast, emit a steady stream of pollutants from the exhaust whenever the engine is operating, because they simply do not have an exhaust pipe.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do Their Emissions Compare? · Page: 3
"All-electric vehicles produce zero tailpipe emissions"
Indirect c-doe-037
What life-cycle emissions are tied to an EV?
Life-cycle emissions for an EV include those from generating the electricity that charges it and from manufacturing the vehicle itself. The amount depends largely on how clean the regional power grid is and how much a PHEV's engine is used over its life.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do Their Emissions Compare? · Page: 3
"Life cycle emissions are generated when fuel or electricity is produced, as well as during the manufacturing of the vehicle itself."
Medium c-doe-038
Roughly what share of conventional vehicle emissions do EVs and PHEVs produce?
Generally all-electric vehicles produce about one-third of the emissions of a conventional car, and PHEVs about half, when both air pollutants and greenhouse gases are counted across the full life cycle of fuel and electricity used by each one.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: How Do Their Emissions Compare? · Page: 3
"Generally, all-electric vehicles and PHEVs produce one-third to half the emissions of conventional vehicles, respectively"
Basic c-doe-039
Do EVs face the same safety standards as gasoline vehicles?
Yes, every EV sold in the United States undergoes the same rigorous safety testing as a conventional vehicle on the market. They must meet all Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standards, including special tests covering the high-voltage battery pack itself.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Safety and Maintenance · Page: 3
"All EVs undergo the same rigorous safety testing as conventional vehicles sold in the United States and must meet Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standards"
Indirect c-doe-040
Why do PHEVs have maintenance needs similar to conventional cars?
PHEVs still carry a conventional gasoline engine on top of their electric drive system. That engine needs oil changes, spark plug checks, and the other usual servicing tasks, so the overall maintenance schedule looks much like a regular gasoline-powered car.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Safety and Maintenance · Page: 3
"Because PHEVs have conventional engines, their maintenance requirements are similar to conventional vehicles."
Basic c-doe-041
What does 'mpge' mean as a rating for EVs?
EVs are not rated in miles per gallon but in miles per gallon of gasoline equivalent, or mpge for short. It expresses the distance the vehicle can travel on a quantity of electricity with the same energy content as one gallon of gasoline.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Benefits of Electric-Drive Vehicles · Page: 4
"EVs are rated not in miles per gallon (mpg) but miles per gallon of gasoline equivalent (mpge)."
Medium c-doe-042
How do per-mile fuel costs of EVs compare with gasoline sedans?
Conventional gasoline or diesel sedans typically cost about 10 to 15 cents per mile in fuel alone. All-electric vehicles, by contrast, come in much cheaper at roughly 2 to 6 cents per mile, sharply reducing day-to-day operating expense for owners.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Benefits of Electric-Drive Vehicles · Page: 4
"Compare to 10¢–15¢ per mile for conventional gasolineor diesel-powered sedans."
Basic c-doe-043
How long does an EV battery warranty typically last?
Manufacturers' EV battery warranties typically cover eight years or 100,000 miles, whichever comes first during the ownership period. Owners should still check with their specific manufacturer because warranty terms and conditions vary somewhat between different brands and models.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Benefits of Electric-Drive Vehicles · Page: 4
"A manufacturer’s warranty of a battery typically covers 8 years or 100,000 miles"
Basic c-doe-044
What is the expected lifetime of an EV battery under normal conditions?
EV batteries are expected to last 12 to 15 years under normal operating conditions in moderate climates. Very hot or very cold weather and aggressive use can shorten that lifespan somewhat compared to the typical industry estimate given by the manufacturer.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Benefits of Electric-Drive Vehicles · Page: 4
"the expected battery lifetime is 12 to 15 years under normal operating conditions and in moderate climates."
Indirect c-doe-045
Why do brake systems last longer in EVs than in conventional cars?
Regenerative braking does much of the slowing on an EV by running the motor in reverse as a generator. That reduces wear on the friction brake pads and rotors, so the brake hardware typically lasts longer than it would in a conventional vehicle.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Benefits of Electric-Drive Vehicles · Page: 4
"Brake systems on these vehicles typically last longer than conventional vehicles because regenerative braking reduces brake wear."
Indirect c-doe-046
Why do all-electric vehicles need less maintenance than PHEVs?
All-electric vehicles have no conventional engine, far fewer moving parts, and fewer fluids to change over time. PHEVs still carry an engine and its supporting hardware on board, so they need more routine servicing than their fully electric cousins do.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Benefits of Electric-Drive Vehicles · Page: 4
"All-electric vehicles lack conventional engines and have far fewer moving parts and fewer fluids to change, so they typically require less maintenance"
Indirect c-doe-047
Why must fleet planners think about time-of-use charges for medium and heavy-duty EVs?
Utilities often bill commercial customers differently based on when they draw power, and at what peak rate. Fleet managers should work with the utility to understand time-of-use and demand charges so they can schedule charging during the cheaper hours.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Considering an EV · Page: 4
"Determining when and how the vehicles will charge"
Basic c-doe-048
What auxiliary loads should fleet operators consider for medium and heavy-duty EVs?
Beyond moving the vehicle, energy is drawn for cabin heating and cooling, lights, and any power take-off or hydraulic equipment fitted to the truck. These loads can drain the pack, so they must be factored into duty-cycle planning ahead of time.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Considering an EV · Page: 4
"Examining auxiliary loads (e.g., heating/cooling, lights, power take-off/ hydraulics use)"
Indirect c-doe-049
Why does timing the purchase of charging units matter for fleet adoption?
Charging hardware must be ready on site when the new vehicles actually arrive at the depot. Timing the purchase and installation with vehicle delivery avoids leaving expensive trucks parked uncharged, and the process can be slow, particularly for municipal organisations.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Considering an EV · Page: 4
"Timing the purchase and installation of charging units with the delivery of vehicles"
Indirect c-doe-050
What infrastructure risk emerges when several heavy EVs charge at once?
Charging several heavy-duty EVs simultaneously at high power can dramatically increase a single site's electricity demand. Operators must study that load carefully to avoid overloading the local circuit and to anticipate any utility service upgrades the depot will need.
Source: Electric Vehicle Basics
Chapter: Electric Vehicle Basics · Section: Considering an EV · Page: 4
"Determining the impacts of increased electricity consumption, especially when several vehicles need to be charged simultaneously at high charging rates"

11. Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer

International Energy Agency · IEA · 50 Q&As

Basic c-iea-pol-001
What is Algeria's national legislation on imported used vehicles?
Algeria's national legislation, dating from 2021, bans the import of vehicles more than three years old. This rule helps push the country's fleet towards newer and cleaner cars, reducing pollution from older vehicles that no longer meet modern environmental standards on the road.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Africa — Algeria · Page: 1
"Ban on imports more than 3 years old."
Basic c-iea-pol-002
What EV tax breaks does Angola offer?
Angola offers a 50 percent reduction in both import duty and vehicle tax for electric vehicles, set in national legislation in 2022. The lower taxes make EVs noticeably cheaper to buy locally, helping kick-start the country's transition away from gasoline cars.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Africa — Angola · Page: 1
"50% reduction of both import duty and vehicle tax for EVs."
Basic c-iea-pol-003
What government fleet target has Antigua and Barbuda set?
Antigua and Barbuda has set a national target to transition its government vehicle fleet to all-electric by 2035. This commitment, recorded in 2021, makes the public sector a visible early adopter and creates demand that helps the broader EV market on the islands.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Antigua and Barbuda · Page: 1
"Transition the government fleet to allelectric by 2035."
Basic c-iea-pol-004
When does Argentina propose to ban the sale of new ICE vehicles?
Argentina has proposed a national ban on the sale of new internal combustion engine vehicles from 2041 onwards. This proposal, recorded in 2021, would gradually push the country's vehicle market towards zero-emission options as the deadline approaches over the next two decades.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Central and South America — Argentina · Page: 1
"Ban on sale of new ICE vehicles from 2041."
Indirect c-iea-pol-005
What ZEV bus targets has Buenos Aires set?
The city government of Buenos Aires has targeted 50 percent zero-emission buses by 2030 and 100 percent by 2050. A ZEV bus runs purely on electricity or hydrogen, with no tailpipe pollution, which is a major win for cleaner air in dense urban centres.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Central and South America — Argentina (Buenos Aires) · Page: 1
"50% ZEV buses by 2030, 100% by 2050."
Basic c-iea-pol-006
What ZEV target has Victoria, Australia announced for its light-duty fleet?
The Victorian state government in Australia has set an ambition for 50 percent of its light-duty vehicle fleet to be zero-emission by 2030. This 2021 commitment positions Victoria as one of the more ambitious Australian states on rapidly electrifying private cars.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Asia Pacific — Australia (Victoria) · Page: 1
"50% of LDV fleet to be ZEV by 2030."
Indirect c-iea-pol-007
What incentive does the Australian Capital Territory provide for new ZEVs?
The ACT government offers free vehicle registration for new zero-emission vehicles for two years, interest-free loans for buyers, and is installing 50 new EV charging stations as practical. These combined perks lower the upfront barriers to owning an EV in the territory.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Asia Pacific — Australia (ACT) · Page: 1
"Free vehicle registration for new ZEV for two years, interest free loans and 50 new electric vehicle"
Basic c-iea-pol-008
What ZEV sales ambition has Austria set for new heavy goods vehicles over 18 tonnes?
Austria has set a national ambition for 100 percent zero-emission vehicle share in new heavy goods vehicle sales above 18 tonnes by 2035. Heavy trucks are notoriously hard to electrify, so the 2035 target represents a serious commitment to clean freight technology.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Europe — Austria · Page: 2
"100%share of ZEVs in"
Indirect c-iea-pol-009
What tax exemptions does Austria grant to EVs?
In Austria, EVs are exempt from the standard consumption tax, the motor-related insurance tax, and the benefit-in-kind tax that normally applies to company cars. Company vehicle EVs are also fully tax deductible and exempt from value added tax for the operator.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Europe — Austria · Page: 2
"EVs are exempt from"
Basic c-iea-pol-010
What national EV target has Bangladesh set?
Bangladesh has set a national target that 30 percent of new vehicle registrations will be electric by 2030. It also offers a 10-year tax holiday for local EV manufacturing and assembly, which encourages domestic producers to invest in building EVs at home.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Asia Pacific — Bangladesh · Page: 2
"30% of new registrations to be electric by 2030."
Indirect c-iea-pol-011
What ZEV sales target has Flanders, Belgium set for 2025 and 2030?
The Flanders regional government in Belgium wants 20 percent of new car sales to be zero-emission by 2025. By 2030, it targets 50 percent battery electric or fuel cell sales alongside 20 percent plug-in hybrid sales, accelerating the region's switch to clean vehicles.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Europe — Belgium (Flanders) · Page: 2
"20% of sales to be ZEV by 2025, and 50% BEV or FCEV sales and 20% PHEV in 2030."
Basic c-iea-pol-012
What petrol and diesel car bans has the Brussels region of Belgium announced?
The Brussels regional government has legislated a ban on diesel cars in the region by 2030 and on petrol cars by 2035. These bans clear the way for cleaner technologies like battery electric and hydrogen fuel cell vehicles to dominate Brussels streets.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Europe — Belgium (Brussels) · Page: 3
"Ban on diesel cars in the region by 2030, petrol cars by 2035."
Basic c-iea-pol-013
What public transport EV target has Bolivia set?
Bolivia has set a national ambition for annual 10 percent growth in the share of electric vehicles in its public transportation fleet. That steady year-on-year increase helps the country build experience with electric buses gradually without overwhelming the national power grid.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer

"Annual 10% growth in the share of EVs in the Bolivian public transportation fleet."
Basic c-iea-pol-014
What proposal does Senate Bill No. 392/2023 in Brazil make for fuelling stations?
Brazil's proposed Senate Bill No. 392 of 2023 would require fuelling stations to install EV chargers on site. Forcing existing fuel stations to add chargers helps build a denser charging network quickly, using places drivers already visit to top up their cars.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer
Chapter: Policy Explorer 2024 · Section: Central and South America — Brazil · Page: 3
"Proposed Senate Bill No. 392/2023 obliges fuelling stations to have EV chargers."
Basic c-iea-pol-015
What is Cabo Verde's target for passenger EV sales in 2035?
Cabo Verde has set a national target for 100 percent of passenger light-duty vehicle sales to be electric by 2035. Interim targets are 35 percent by 2025 and 70 percent by 2030, mapping a steady path away from gasoline cars on the islands.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer

"35% share of passenger LDV sales to be EVs by 2025, 70% by 2030 and 100% by 2035."
Indirect c-iea-pol-016
What ZEV sales mandate has British Columbia set for light-duty vehicles?
British Columbia has accelerated zero-emission vehicle sales targets for light-duty vehicles, requiring 26 percent ZEV sales by 2026, 90 percent by 2030, and 100 percent by 2035. These provincial targets run ahead of Canada's national ambition for the same vehicle category.

What is Canada's national ZEV availability standard for auto importers?
Canada's national ZEV availability standard requires auto manufacturers and importers to meet annual zero-emission vehicle sales targets for light-duty vehicles: 20 percent by 2026, 60 percent by 2030, and 100 percent by 2035 across the country's vehicle market.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer

Basic c-iea-pol-018
What ZEV sales target has Quebec set for 2035?
Quebec's provincial government requires zero-emission vehicle sales to reach 22 percent in 2025, 85 percent in 2030, and 100 percent in 2035. The province also aims to put roughly 2 million electric vehicles on the road across Quebec by 2030.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer

Basic c-iea-pol-019
What is Chile's national target for light-duty vehicle sales by 2035?
Chile has set a national target for 100 percent of light-duty vehicle sales to be zero-emission by 2035, paired with a ban on internal combustion engine sales from that year onwards. This pairing closes the door cleanly on new gasoline cars.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer

Indirect c-iea-pol-020
What does Chile plan for highway EV charging infrastructure?
Chile has a proposed national public charging infrastructure plan targeting charging stations along interurban routes spaced at most every 100 kilometres apart. This even distribution lets EV drivers cross the long country without worrying about gaps in the charging network between cities.
Source: Global EV Outlook 2024 — Policy Explorer

Shenzhen has targeted that the proportion of new energy vehicles among newly registered vehicles, excluding replacement and renewal, will reach 60 percent by 2025. The city also plans roughly 43,000 fast charging piles and 790,000 slow charging piles by the same year.

Basic c-iea-pol-022
What petrol and diesel sales ban has Hainan, China legislated for 2030?
Hainan province in China plans to end the sale of petrol and diesel vehicles by 2030. From then on, all vehicle sales in Hainan will be either new energy vehicles or natural gas vehicles, making it a national leader on phasing out fossil fuels.

What is China's national NEV sales target for 2030?
China expects new energy vehicle sales to account for 45 percent of new vehicle sales by 2025 and 60 percent by 2030. NEV in China includes battery electric, plug-in hybrid, and fuel cell vehicles, so the target captures all major clean technologies.

What is China's national vehicle and vessel tax position on NEVs?
China's national legislation exempts new energy vehicles from the country's vehicle and vessel tax. Removing that recurring annual cost makes owning an electric car or plug-in hybrid noticeably cheaper compared with a conventional gasoline car over the long term.

What is the European Union's CO2 standard target for new cars by 2025?
The European Union's supranational CO2 emission standard requires a 15 percent reduction in CO2 emissions for both new cars and vans by 2025. This forces every automaker selling in the EU to push its fleet average down by that amount over the period.

Indirect c-iea-pol-045
How did Norway's EV tax treatment change in 2023?
Norway began introducing value added tax on higher-cost EV purchases from 2023 onwards. Before that, all EV sales were exempt from VAT entirely. The change reflects how mature the Norwegian EV market has become, with the most expensive cars no longer needing full support.
